401 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Eichorn


No. G022777.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


69 Cal. App. 4th 382; 81 Cal. Rptr. 2d 535; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 1100; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 588; 99 Daily Journal DAR 659



December 30, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published January 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding; petition for a writ of habeas corpus to challenge a judgment of the Municipal Court of Orange County. Muni. Ct. No. 93CM02515. James M. Brooks, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The writ is granted and the cause remanded to the former municipal court with directions to set aside the judgment of conviction and to proceed in conformity with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for sleeping in a public area by the Municipal Court of Orange County (California), in a petition for writ of habeas corpus. Appellant argued that he was induced to waive his right to a jury trial by the trial ruling that he could not present a necessity defense.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a homeless man, was arrested for violation of an anti-camping statute. Appellant had offered to prove that on the night of the violation, every available shelter was occupied and that he was involuntarily homeless. The lower court had found that appellant had violated the ordinance and he was not involuntarily homeless because he did not go to an armory shelter which its director had testified had probably not been available on that cold night. The court granted appellant's writ because it found that he had been improperly denied his right to present a viable necessity defense to show that he had violated the law because of the emergency nature of his situation for which he had inadequate alternatives.


OUTCOME: The writ was granted and the cause was remanded to set aside the judgment of conviction because appellant was entitled to raise a necessity defense to charges he violated the camping ordinance.

 

402 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Carlson v. Dep't of Fish & Game


No. B105789.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


68 Cal. App. 4th 1268; 80 Cal. Rptr. 2d 601; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 1049; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9227; 98 Daily Journal DAR 12868



December 18, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part III.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 6, 1999. Review Denied March 9, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 1368.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of the County of Los Angeles. Super. Ct. No. SC037173. Lorna Parnell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and remanded with directions to grant leave to amend the complaint. The parties are to bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of the County of Los Angeles (California), which denied plaintiff's motion for an order correcting the date of filing of a complaint, even though the complaint complied with Cal. R. Ct. 201, and sustained defendants' demurrer without leave to amend, dismissing the complaint on the basis of the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: After the lower court denied plaintiff's motion for an order correcting the date of filing a complaint and dismissed the complaint against defendant for failure to comply with the statute of limitations, plaintiff appealed. The court reversed and held that the local court clerk did not have the power under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 575.2(a) or under Superior Court of Los Angeles County Rules, rule 2.0(d) to reject the filing of a complaint for failure to comply with the local rule. Once the complaint complied with Cal. R. Ct. 202, it should have been filed. Therefore, the lower court erred in dismissing plaintiff's motion to correct the date of filing and thus the complaint was filed within the limitations period.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment and remanded with directions to grant leave to amend the complaint because the local court clerk should have filed plaintiff's complaint against defendant once it complied with the California Rules of Court.

 

403 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Comedy III Productions, Inc. v. Gary Saderup, Inc.


B120382


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


68 Cal. App. 4th 744; 80 Cal. Rptr. 2d 464; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 1036; 98 Daily Journal DAR 12735; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9134; 27 Media L. Rep. 1426; 49 U.S.P.Q.2D (BNA) 1282



December 15, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted March 17, 1999 (S076061), Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 1541.
Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions Cumulative Supplement (July 1999) to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Reprinted without change in the January 2000 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Reprinted without change in the January 2001 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Court.
Supreme Court of California Opinion of April 30, 2001, Reported at: 25 Cal. 4th 387.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. EC020205. Carl. J. West, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant artist and his company challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles (California), that rendered judgment for damages in favor of plaintiff registered owner under Cal. Civ. Code § 990 and entered an injunction; defendants sold lithographed copies of a sketch of the likenesses of deceased personalities.


OVERVIEW: Defendant artist and his corporation sketched and sold multiple lithographic prints and images of the Three Stooges without the consent of plaintiff registered owner. Based on the trial court's findings, profits were gained by defendants from the commercial sale of those products without the consent. The trial court held that the enterprise and sales were not protected by constitutional free speech guarantees. Defendants were liable under Cal. Civ. Code § 990 for profits and attorney fees and were enjoined. Defendants argued on appeal that their use did not fall under § 990 because they did not deal in a product or goods, that the statute covered advertisements, and they were exempted because the personalities remained newsworthy. Defendants contended their actions were constitutionally protected under U.S. Const. amend I and Cal. Const. art. I § 2. The court found that § 990 covered defendants' actions, they sold a product or goods, the statute protected newsworthy material and advertisements, and the sale of a likeness did not constitute free speech, absent a communicative message. The court affirmed damages, but modified injunctive relief because it was overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court modified and affirmed the judgment finding defendant artist and his company's use of the likeness and lithographs did in fact subject defendants to liability because their use resulted in the sale of goods that were not constitutionally protected as free speech. Defendants were liable to plaintiff for damages, but the injunctive relief was overly broad.

 

404 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Kacy S.


No. C023170.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


68 Cal. App. 4th 704; 80 Cal. Rptr. 2d 432; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 1031; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9117; 98 Daily Journal DAR 12715



December 14, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied March 17, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 1601.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Plumas County. Super. Ct. No. 4705 and 4706. Roger M. Settlemire, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment as to Kacy is affirmed. As to Daren, the probation condition that he not associate with any persons not approved by his probation officer is modified to provide only that he shall not associate with Jason B. As so modified, the judgment as to Daren is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant minors appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Plumas County (California), placing them on six months' probation on condition they submitted to urine testing to determine the presence of alcohol and illegal drugs in their systems pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 729.3, and that defendant one not associate with any persons not approved by his probation officer, and that defendant two not associate with a certain individual.


OVERVIEW: Defendant minors involved in an altercation were not removed from the physical custody of their parents but were placed on six months' probation on conditions they submitted to urine testing to determine the presence of alcohol and illegal drugs in their systems pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 729.3, and that defendant one not associate with any persons not approved by his probation officer. Defendants appealed, contending imposition of the urine testing condition was improper. The court disagreed, finding the testing condition related to criminal conduct and was reasonably related to future criminality, thus its imposition was within the juvenile court's discretion. Although urine testing constituted an intrusion on privacy, the effect of the intrusion was outweighed by the government's legitimate interest in closely monitoring the rehabilitation of minors who were granted probation and returned to the custody of their parents. Defendant one further contended the condition that he not associate with any persons not approved by his probation officer was overbroad and unreasonable. The court agreed, and imposed the condition that he not associate with a named individual.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that defendants be required to submit to urine testing on the grounds that the testing condition was within the juvenile court's discretion and the condition did not violate defendants' constitutional. The court modified the probation condition that defendant one not associate with any persons not approved by his probation officer to provide only that he not associate with a named individual.

 

405 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Duz-Mor Diagnostic Lab.


No. B113282.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


68 Cal. App. 4th 654; 80 Cal. Rptr. 2d 419; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 1028; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9082; 98 Daily Journal DAR 12683



December 11, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified December 24, 1998. Review Denied February 24, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 1220.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC123965. Ernest M. Hiroshige, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed insofar as it determines that Duz-Mor did not violate the Unfair Competition Act through either the offer of discounts to physicians' private-pay patients or through use of the "unbundled" billing system, and that Duz-Mor did not violate the False Claims Act through use of the "unbundled" billing system. The judgment is reversed insofar as it determines that Duz-Mor did not violate the Unfair Competition Act through the payment of commissions for marketing services. The case is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. Each party to bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney general sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which held that certain practices by respondent laboratory did not violate the Unfair Competition Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17200 et seq., or the False Claims Act, Cal. Gov't Code § 12651.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney general alleged that respondent laboratory violated the Unfair Competition Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17200 et seq., by charging discounted fees to certain patients, by paying commissions to an independent marketing contractor, and by "unbundling" Medi-Cal billing, so that certain tests which should have been billed together were billed separately. Appellant also alleged that the use of unbundled billing violated the False Claims Act, Cal. Gov't Code § 12651. The trial court found in favor of respondent. The court reversed the judgment insofar as it determined that respondent not violate the Unfair Competition Act through the payment of commissions for marketing services. Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 14107.2. The court affirmed the judgment insofar as it determined that respondent did not violate the Unfair Competition Act through either the offer of discounts to physicians' private-pay patients or through use of the "unbundled" billing system, and that respondent did not violate the False Claims Act through use of the "unbundled" billing system.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the trial court's decision, which held that respondent laboratory did not violate the Unfair Competition Act through the payment of commissions for marketing services. In all other respects, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court remanded the case to the trial court for proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

406 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Butler


No. H017510.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


68 Cal. App. 4th 421; 80 Cal. Rptr. 2d 357; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 1010; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8985; 98 Daily Journal DAR 12429



December 7, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied March 24, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 1784. Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5724.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Cruz County. Super. Ct. No. ME-26. Robert B. Yonts, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order issued by the Superior Court of Santa Cruz County (California), that committed him to the Department of Mental Health pursuant to its finding that defendant was a sexually violent predator under the Sexually Violent Predators Act, Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the trial court's order that found defendant was a sexually violent predator (SVP) pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq. and committed him to the state mental health department for treatment. The court found the trial court erred by simply conducting a facial review of the commitment petition at the probable cause hearing, but held reversal was not warranted because defendant failed to seek pretrial review of the trial court's ruling as to the nature of the probable cause hearing, was afforded the opportunity to cross-examine prosecution witnesses as well as call his own witnesses, and failed to show that he was denied a fair trial or otherwise suffered prejudice due to the error. The court held that the evidence which supported the trial court's finding that defendant fell within the parameters of the SVP law was sufficient and found that the breadth of the SVP statute's coverage was not impermissibly enlarged by the addition of express language to clarify that out-of-state crimes, which included elements of crimes the state defined as sexually violent offenses, were encompassed by the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial judgment and held that although it was error for the trial court to conduct a mere facial review of the commitment petition at the probable cause hearing, reversal was not justified because no evidence was presented to show that defendant was prejudiced by the trial court's error. The court also found the evidence at trial sufficiently supported the findings that defendant qualified as a sexually violent predator.

 

407 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Bennett


No. G020575.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


68 Cal. App. 4th 396; 80 Cal. Rptr. 2d 323; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 1011; 98 Daily Journal DAR 12419; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8939



December 4, 1998, Decided  
December 4, 1998


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County. Super. Ct. No. 95CF2944. Richard W. Luesebrink, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County (California) denying his motion to suppress base cocaine that was found in his shoe after he was arrested for violating parole, arguing that the court erred in denying his motion to suppress the cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for violating parole. He was booked and placed in a holding cell where the police searched him and found base cocaine in his shoe. Defendant's attorney filed a motion under Cal. Penal Code § 1538.5 to suppress the cocaine on three grounds. The motion was denied. The court held that a defendant who has sought the suppression of evidence at his or her preliminary hearing, who then seeks to renew the motion in the superior court, is not entitled to advance theories at the second hearing that were not raised and litigated during the first. Defendant was permitted to develop theories in the superior court that his attorney had abandoned during the first hearing on his motion to suppress, but the provisions of § 1538.5 (i) did not authorize him to do so. Therefore, the theories, and the evidence that went with them, were not properly before the superior court.


OUTCOME: The denial of defendant's motion to suppress cocaine was affirmed because a defendant who seeks to suppress evidence at his preliminary hearing, who attempts to renew the motion in the trial court, cannot advance theories at the second hearing that were not raised and litigated during the first.

409 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Ellison


No. F027634.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


68 Cal. App. 4th 203; 80 Cal. Rptr. 2d 120; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 1000; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8829; 98 Daily Journal DAR 12241



November 30, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II. and III.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied March 9, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 1499.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County. Super. Ct. No. SC068058A. Gary T. Friedman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the Superior Court of Kern County (California), for a misdemeanor of loitering in a public place with the intent to commit a narcotics offense, pursuant to Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11532. Appellant was also convicted of the felony offense of cocaine possession and another misdemeanor offense of falsely representing himself to a police officer.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for loitering in a public place with the intent to commit a narcotics offense based on Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11532, by challenging the constitutionality of the statute claiming that it was vague, overly broad, and violated the separation of powers doctrine. The court noted that a statute is not rendered impermissibly indefinite by its use of the word "loiter," that the specific intent referred to in the statute was narrowly defined such that it provided sufficient notice of the proscribed conduct, and that no reasonable person could have misunderstood its meaning. The court also found that the statute did not provide the police with unfettered discretion and that it gave the police adequate enforcement guidelines. The court rejected appellant's contention that the statute was overly broad because it found that the statute did not prohibit a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct. In addition, the statute did not violate the separation of power doctrine because any discretion possessed by the police to determine whether a crime had occurred was limited to probable cause to arrest. Appellant's conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, finding that the anti-loitering statute that appellant challenged met all constitutional requirements in that it provided sufficient notice of the proscribed conduct and sufficient police enforcement guidelines. Furthermore, it neither criminalized constitutionally protected conduct nor empowered the police to determine what types of behavior constituted a crime.

 

410 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Tily B., Inc. v. City of Newport Beach


No. G016950, No. G019250, No. G022132.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


69 Cal. App. 4th 1; 81 Cal. Rptr. 2d 6; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 1092; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 62; 99 Daily Journal DAR 69



November 30, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court From Unpublished to Published December 30, 1998.
As Modified December 30, 1998. Review Denied March 17, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 1621.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from judgments of the Superior Court of Orange County. Super. Ct. Nos. 726629. 748917 and 772146. H. Warren Siegel, John C. Woolley and Francisco J. Firmat, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgment in No. G016950 is affirmed. The judgment in No. G019250 is reversed. The judgment in No. G022132 is affirmed. The city, as the prevailing party, is entitled to its costs on appeal in each case.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff adult entertainment operators appealed judgments of the Superior Court of Orange County (California) that denied their petitions to compel defendant city to issue use and entertainment permits, set aside permit revocations/nonrenewals, and granted defendant summary judgment on plaintiffs' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims. Defendant appealed the trial court's order that defendant repeal Newport Beach, Cal., Municipal Code § 5.28.041(R)(S).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff adult entertainment operators appealed judgments that denied their petitions to compel defendant city to issue use and entertainment permits, and granted summary judgment to defendant on plaintiffs' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims. Defendant sought reversal of a judgment that ordered repeal of an ordinance that required performers at adult clubs at minimum be clad in pasties and G-strings. The court found defendant's amended licensing scheme, which replaced an unconstitutional "primary use test" with an objective standard for determining whether a business qualified as a restaurant, was a constitutional basis for denial of plaintiffs' permit application because their club was outside the definition of a restaurant. The court ruled that the trial court erroneously ordered defendant to repeal the pasties and G-strings ordinance because it was a content neutral ordinance that constitutionally addressed defendant's interest in limiting the undesirable secondary effects associated with adult entertainment. The court found plaintiff's civil rights claim was barred by the statute of limitations and unsupported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to defendant city on plaintiff adult entertainment operators' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims, and also affirmed denial of plaintiffs' petitions for writs of mandate to compel defendant to issue use and entertainment permits for their club. The court reversed the trial order that directed defendant to repeal an ordinance requiring performers at adult clubs to wear no less than pasties and G-strings.

 

411 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Zeghtchanian


B104777


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


67 Cal. App. 4th 1441; 79 Cal. Rptr. 2d 866; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 978; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8682; 98 Daily Journal DAR 12077



November 24, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] CERTIFIED FOR PARTIAL PUBLICATION - Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication. The portions of this opinion to be deleted from publication.

NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied March 9, 1999 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 1367.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. GA025604. Thomas W. Stoever, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction for two counts of attempted child stealing in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 664 and § 278 and of disobeying a court order in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 166(a)(4) by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), arguing that the dependency court order giving custody to her ex-husband was invalid.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of attempted child stealing in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 664 and § 278 and of disobeying a court order in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 166(a)(4) after she tried to take her child away from her ex-husband, who had a dependency court order awarding him custody. The court found that Cal. Penal Code § 278 did not mandate the existence of a valid custody order as an element of proof of the crime of child stealing; however, because defendant was divorced, the circumstances of this case required proof of such an order to meet the prosecution's burden to establish that defendant took the child from someone with "lawful charge" of the child. The court held that defendant was entitled to collaterally attack the validity of the dependency court order because she had an interest in being free of incarceration by reason of a void order. The court affirmed her convictions, however.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for child stealing and disobeying a court order. However, the court held that defendant was entitled to collaterally attack the validity of the dependency court order that awarded custody to her ex-husband because the prosecution had to show that the child was taken from a person with "lawful charge" of the child.

 

412 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Braun v. Bureau of State Audits


No. A075423.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


67 Cal. App. 4th 1382; 79 Cal. Rptr. 2d 791; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 968; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8628; 98 Daily Journal DAR 11905



November 23, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part II.B.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied March 9, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 1341. Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5011.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Francisco County. Super. Ct. No. 970990. David A. Garcia, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of dismissal is affirmed with costs to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant university official brought suit against respondents, state auditors and agencies, for defamation, emotional distress, and negligence, arising out of an investigation of appellant's department. Respondents demurred, arguing that the state auditor's report was privileged under Cal. Civ. Code §47(a), and the Superior Court of San Francisco County (California) dismissed the case. Appellant sought review of the dismissal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant university administrator was the subject of a state audit under the Reporting of Improper Governmental Activities Act, Cal. Gov't Code § 8547, et seq. The auditors made public a report finding that appellant had grossly mismanaged her department, and listing many improprieties. Appellant brought suit against respondent state auditors for defamation and other torts, and respondents demurred that the complaint failed to state a cause of action, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code §430.10(e). The trial court held that the report was absolutely privileged under the Reporting Act and Cal. Civ. Code § 47(a) and (b), and dismissed the complaint. The court affirmed, holding that the audit constituted an official proceeding authorized by law under Cal. Civil Code § 47(b), so that statements made in furtherance of the audit were absolutely privileged. The court held that, although the university was constitutionally autonomous, it was subject to legislative control to ensure the security of its funds under Cal. Const. art. IX, § 9. The court held that Cal. Gov't Code § 8547.7(c) provided for the release of reports and findings to the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant's complaint, holding that an investigative audit by the state auditor under the Reporting Act was an "official proceeding," such that all statements made in furtherance of the audit, including the report of the audit, were absolutely privileged. The court held that the Reporting Act authorized the Bureau of State Audits to make the report public.

 

413 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Anti-Defamation League of B'Nai B'Rith v. Superior Court


No. A080694.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


67 Cal. App. 4th 1072; 79 Cal. Rptr. 2d 597; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 944; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8451; 98 Daily Journal DAR 11713; 27 Media L. Rep. 1321



November 16, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Super. Court No. 951031. Alex Saldamando, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order to show cause is discharged. The petition for writ of prohibition and/or mandate is granted, and respondent court is directed to set aside and vacate its September 19, 1997, order (as amended at the November 6, 1997, status conference). The parties shall bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a non-profit organization and its investigative employee, sought to set aside a discovery order issued by respondent Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), that granted reconsideration and ordered compliance with certain discovery requests by real parties in interest. Respondent court stayed the effect to its order pending the court's final determination of the writ petition.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, a non-profit organization and its investigative employee, were defendants in an action brought by 17 real parties in interest for invasion of privacy on the grounds that petitioners violated Cal. Civ. Code § 1798.53 by secretly gathering personal information about real parties in interest and disclosing the information to others. Petitioners sought to set aside a discovery order issued by the trial court on the grounds that real parties in interest had overcome the journalist's qualified privilege. The court held that petitioners, as journalists, were immune from liability for violating § 1798.53 under U.S. Const. amend. I, as to all but one and possibly two of the real parties in interest by virtue of their status as limited purpose public figures. As to the remaining nonpublic figures, the court held petitioners were not protected from liability and a discovery order. The court also held petitioners were entitled to the protection only insofar as the information sought to be discovered was obtained and used for legitimate journalistic purposes. The trial court's order was vacated and the matter was remanded for reconsideration.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's discovery order because it found that petitioners were protected by U.S. Const. amend. I, as to claims of at least 14 real parties in interest. The court found that petitioners' privilege did not encompass non-journalistic disclosures and held that discovery tailored to reveal whether private disclosures were made should be permitted.

 

414 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



San Bernardino Public Employees Ass'n v. City of Fontana


No. E021207.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


67 Cal. App. 4th 1215; 79 Cal. Rptr. 2d 634; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 956; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8545; 160 L.R.R.M. 2179; 98 Daily Journal DAR 11843



November 16, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. Super.Ct.No. SCV36883. Bob N. Krug, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. Defendants shall recover costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from the writ of mandate granted by the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California) in favor of plaintiff labor organization, which challenged defendant's ability to alter through collective bargaining longevity pay, personal leave accrual, and retiree medical insurance under a memoranda of understanding negotiated with defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff labor organization entered into memoranda of understanding with defendant city that provided for longevity pay, leave accrual increases based on longevity, and paid retiree medical and dental insurance benefits. These longevity-based benefits had been agreed upon through the collective bargaining process under the Meyers-Milias-Brown Act, Cal. Gov't. Code § 3500 et seq. Defendant proposed to reduce the benefits during subsequent negotiations, and plaintiff took the position that the longevity-based benefits were vested and could not be bargained away. The trial court agreed that employees represented by plaintiff possessed vested, contractual rights to the benefits. The court reversed the trial court's judgment, concluding that the collective bargaining agreements, as implemented through previous memoranda of understandings, were of fixed duration such that once they expired under their own terms, there was no legitimate expectation that the longevity-based benefits would continue unless they were renegotiated as part of a new bargaining agreement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, concluding that the benefits at issue could not have become permanently and irrevocably vested as a matter of contract law, that within the context of the Meyers-Milias-Brown Act, the collective bargaining process properly included annual leave and longevity pay benefits, and that the trial court merely issued an advisory opinion in granting plaintiff labor organization's petition.

 

415 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Denison


A077542, A082619


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


67 Cal. App. 4th 943; 79 Cal. Rptr. 2d 524; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 926; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8342



November 10, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified December 10, 1998. Review Denied March 9, 1999 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 1343.


PRIOR HISTORY: Marin County Superior Court. Court No. SC084837A. Honorable Terence Boren.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought habeas corpus relief from his conviction in the Superior Court of Marin County (California) for possession of cocaine and related drug paraphernalia. Defendant asserted that the police stop to conduct a probation search of the passenger in the car defendant was driving violated his rights under U.S. Const. Amend. IV.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought habeas corpus relief from his conviction for possession of cocaine and related drug paraphernalia that resulted from a police stop of the car he was driving. The court granted the writ of habeas corpus because defendant had received ineffective assistance of counsel. The court initially held that the officers' stop of defendant's car to initiate a probation search of his passenger did not violate his rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV because the search was neither arbitrary nor prolonged, and the governmental interest outweighed defendant's inconvenience. The officer had reasonable cause to seize the paper bag containing the Valium because he reasonably suspected the bag was controlled by the parolee. However, the court held that mere possession of Valium was not a crime under state law and no other rationale existed to support defendant's arrest. Defense counsel's failure to challenge probable cause for the arrest fell below the standard of reasonable competence and subjected defendant to prejudice because the search of his home incident to the arrest uncovered the drugs and paraphernalia which were the basis of his conviction.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus because he was denied his right to effective counsel. The court vacated the judgment of conviction and remanded the matter to the lower court.

People v. Albritton


No. D026988.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


67 Cal. App. 4th 647; 79 Cal. Rptr. 2d 169; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 897; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8109; 98 Daily Journal DAR 11255



October 29, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. 1 


1 Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II.C. through VII.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied February 17, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 898.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. SCD114372. Charles L. Patrick, Judge. (Judge of the Municipal Court for the San Diego Judicial District, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, section 6 of the California Constitution.)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) for child abuse resulting in death under Cal. Penal Code § 273ab.


OVERVIEW: Defendant often took care of the daughter he had with his live-in girlfriend. Defendant claimed that she almost drowned one night. The victim was taken to the hospital where she died. The medical examiner concluded that she died from shaken baby syndrome. Defendant was convicted of involuntary manslaughter, a lesser-included offense of murder, under Cal. Penal Code § 192(b). Defendant was also convicted of child abuse resulting in death under Cal. Penal Code § 273ab and was sentenced to 15 years to life in prison on the child abuse count and 4 years for the involuntary manslaughter conviction, which was stayed under Cal. Penal Code § 654. The court affirmed defendant's convictions and found no inconsistency between the guilty verdict of child abuse resulting in death and the guilty verdict of involuntary manslaughter. Substantial evidence supported the involuntary manslaughter conviction. The court determined that Cal. Penal Code § 273ab was not a murder statute because it did not require malice aforethought. All of the elements of child abuse resulting in death were proven.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and held that the guilty verdict of child abuse resulting in death was not inconsistent with the guilty verdict of manslaughter. The child abuse resulting in death statute was not a murder statute because it did not contain an essential element of murder, malice aforethought. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad, nor was it an unconstitutional strict liability offense.

 

417 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Englebrecht


No. D030992.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


67 Cal. App. 4th 486; 79 Cal. Rptr. 2d 89; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 887; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8012; 98 Daily Journal DAR 11109



October 26, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITION for writ of habeas corpus following contempt finding by Superior Court of San Diego County for willfully violating two provisions of a preliminary injunction. Super. Ct. No. N76652. John S. Einhorn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is directed to vacate its finding that Englebrecht was in contempt of court for possessing a pager within the Target Area. In all other respects, the petition is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner requested a writ of habeas corpus and sought relief from the trial court's decision that petitioner was in contempt for willfully violating two provisions of a preliminary injunction.


OVERVIEW: The district attorney filed a complaint that alleged that street gang members had created a public nuisance by engaging in illegal activity and terrorizing residents within a one-mile target area of the city. The trial court issued a preliminary injunction against petitioner and others. Petitioner was arrested when he was found with other gang members. At the time of his arrest, petitioner had a pager in his possession. The trial court found petitioner in contempt of court for violating the preliminary injunction provisions forbidding association with known gang members and possessing a pager. Petitioner was sentenced to two concurrent five-day jail terms and fined. The court ordered the trial court to vacate the contempt finding. The court held that the preliminary injunction provision forbidding possession of a pager was unconstitutionally overbroad, because it proscribed all possession and use of pagers, even those that might have a legitimate communication function. The court concluded that gang activities were not the kind of associations entitled to protection under U. S. Const. amend. I. Therefore, the nonassociation provision of the preliminary injunction was proper.


OUTCOME: The court directed the trial court to vacate its finding that petitioner was in contempt of court for possessing a pager within a one-square mile target area of the city, a provision of the preliminary injunction. The court held that this provision was unconstitutionally overbroad. In all other respects, the petition was denied. The court upheld the constitutionality of the nonassociation provision of the preliminary injunction.

 

418 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



County of Orange v. Ivansco


No. G018839.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


67 Cal. App. 4th 328; 78 Cal. Rptr. 2d 886; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 868; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7862; 98 Daily Journal DAR 10897



October 16, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a post-judgment order of the Superior Court of Orange County. Super. Ct. No. AD-57734. Richard G. Vogl, Temporary. Judge. *


*  Pursuant to Cal. Const., art. VI, § 21.



DISPOSITION: The matter is remanded to the trial court with directions to reconsider the child support order in light of the discretion available under section 4059, subdivision (g) and section 4071, subdivision (a)(2). Ivansco shall recover his costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant noncustodial father challenged a postjudgment order from the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which modified his child support obligation. Respondent county filed a show cause order seeking to increase appellant's monthly child support because the twins' mother was still receiving Aid to Families With Dependent Children. The trial court increased appellant's monthly child support order after a contested hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant noncustodial father was ordered to pay child support for his twins and to reimburse respondent county for Aid to Families With Dependent Children (AFDS) payments made to their mother. Respondent sought to increase appellant's monthly child support; the mother still received AFDC. Appellant was the sole support of his teenage son, who lived with him. The court increased appellant's monthly child support order under Cal. Fam. Code § 4071.5 without considering the teenager's expenses, because the twins were AFDC recipients. The court reversed and held that § 4071.5 was unconstitutional because it deprived the trial court of discretion to consider appellant's expenses for children in his custody in setting child support. The trial court had discretion to make a maximum hardship deduction for children residing with appellant, even when appellant's noncustodial children received AFDC. The trial court must consider custodial and noncustodial children, as well as respondent's AFDC reimbursement rights, in awarding child support. On remand, the trial court must reconsider the child support order using the discretion provided in Cal. Fam. Code §§ 4059(g), 4071(a)(2).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and held the statutory section unconstitutional because it deprived the trial court of discretion to consider a parent's expenses for custodial children in determining noncustodial child support for a child receiving Aid to Families With Dependent Children (AFDC). The case was remanded for the trial court to reconsider appellant noncustodial father's child support as well as respondent county's AFDC reimbursement rights.

 

419 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Cal. Rifle & Pistol Ass'n v. City of W. Hollywood


No. B108910.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


66 Cal. App. 4th 1302; 78 Cal. Rptr. 2d 591; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 812; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7503; 98 Daily Journal DAR 10389



September 29, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied December 22, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 8550.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the County of Los Angeles. Super. Ct. No. BC144600. David Horowitz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Respondents to recover costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a pistol association and other groups and individuals, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of the County of Los Angeles (California), upholding an ordinance passed by respondent city that banned the retail and wholesale sale of any handgun classified as a "Saturday Night Special."


OVERVIEW: Respondent city passed an ordinance that banned the retail or wholesale sale of any handgun classified as a "Saturday Night Special." Appellants, a pistol association and other groups and individuals, challenged the ordinance on grounds that state law preempted it. The trial court entered summary judgment for respondent, holding that the ordinance was not preempted and was valid. Appellants sought review. The court affirmed, holding that the ordinance clearly fell within an area of police power left undisturbed by the state legislature. None of the state statutes pertaining to the regulation of guns expressed a legislative intent to divest respondent generally of its police power to regulate the sale of handguns. The ordinance did not violate equal protection or due process guaranties because such protections were for people and not inanimate objects such as handguns. Whether or not the ordinance treated the sellers and buyers of the banned guns dissimilarly to sellers and buyers of unbanned guns was irrelevant because the two groups were not similarly situated for constitutional purposes. The ordinance was a rational legitimate means for addressing the stated harm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court upholding an ordinance that banned the sale of certain handguns within respondent city because state statutes addressing the regulation of guns did not preempt the ordinance. The ordinance was reasonably related to promoting the public health, safety, comfort and welfare, and was a rational and legitimate means to achieving that purpose.

 

420 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Cheyanna M. v. A.C. Nielsen Co.


No. B115423.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


66 Cal. App. 4th 855; 78 Cal. Rptr. 2d 335; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 781; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7224; 98 Daily Journal DAR 9963



September 15, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. Nos. VC020944 and VC023271. Thomas I. McKnew, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. Appellant is entitled to costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor child sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondents, her grandparents and the defendants in a consolidated wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant minor child was born to unmarried parents. Her father never formally acknowledged her as his child, and shortly before her birth he was killed crossing the street. After she was born, his parents asked her and her mother to live with them. Appellant, through her guardian ad litem, filed a wrongful death action against defendants, which was consolidated with respondent grandparents' action. Respondent grandparents then filed a motion for summary judgment, contending that appellant lacked standing to maintain the wrongful death action because her father had never openly held her out as her child, and thus she was not an heir. The trial court granted the motion and appellant sought review. The court reversed and held that under intestacy law, because appellant was born after her father died, it was impossible for the father to hold appellant out as his child. Consequently appellant was permitted to prove paternity through evidence that was clear and convincing. Because these material facts were still in dispute, summary judgment was improper. The case was remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded, holding that summary judgment was improperly granted against appellant minor child in a wrongful death action. The court held that because appellant's father died before she was born, appellant was entitled under the intestacy laws to establish paternity by clear and convincing evidence.

 

421 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Blount


A078082, A082548


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


66 Cal. App. 4th 561; 78 Cal. Rptr. 2d 125; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 755; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6910; 98 Daily Journal DAR 9510



September 1, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] CERTIFIED FOR PARTIAL PUBLICATION - Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts III A and III B.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified September 22, 1998. Review Granted December 16, 1998 (S073792), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 8185.
Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Court.
Review Dismissed November 10, 1999 and cause remanded to Ct. App., 1st Dist., Div. 2 (rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct., Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 7815.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Solano County. Solano County Super. Ct. No. VC37437. Hon. Dwight C. Ely.



DISPOSITION: Remanded to the trial court for the limited purpose of re-computing Blount's jail and prison time credits. In all other respects, judgment affirmed and the petition for a writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Solano County (California), which convicted appellant on a jury verdict of two counts of second-degree robbery and sentenced appellant to an enhanced prison term.


OVERVIEW: Following appellant's robbery conviction, he admitted two prior prison term enhancement allegations and was sentenced to prison. Appellant appealed and filed a habeas corpus petition asserting that his trial counsel provided ineffective assistance. The court held that an ineffective assistance claim involved a showing that counsel's performance was deficient, and proof of actual prejudice. Here, appellant asserted his counsel was ineffective because counsel did not collaterally attack the constitutionality of his prior conviction where that conviction was based upon an involuntary guilty plea. Appellant asserted the plea was involuntary because he was not advised that by pleading guilty, he had to comply with statutory reporting requirements. However, the failure to advise a criminal defendant did about registration did not constitute any kind of constitutional error, and in order to challenge a prior conviction on any ground, a defendant had to allege a denial of his constitutional rights. Accordingly, appellant's petition was denied as appellant failed to carry his burden of establishing the prejudice prong of his ineffective assistance claim. Judgment affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction affirmed, and appellant's petition for habeas corpus denied because appellant's prior to conviction did not violate any of appellant's constitutional rights, appellant's trial counsel's failure to attack that prior conviction could not serve as the basis for appellant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim.

 

422 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Cal. ex rel. Dep't of Motor Vehicles v. Superior Court


No. B113661.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


66 Cal. App. 4th 421; 78 Cal. Rptr. 2d 88; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 749; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6864



August 31, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing September 29, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 818. Review Denied November 18, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 7485.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in Mandamus. Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. Nos. CA000499 and CA001085 and BC165106. Bruce E. Mitchell, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: The alternative writ is discharged. All stays are vacated. A writ of mandamus is hereby issued ordering the trial court to vacate its previous orders certifying the class and to issue new and different orders consistent with this opinion. Each party to bear its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the California Department of Motor Vehicles, sought a writ of mandate directing the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) to vacate its order certifying a class of persons entitled to refunds of vehicle license fees on vehicles originally sold outside the state that were higher than the fees charged similar vehicles sold within the state.


OVERVIEW: The trial court certified a class in consolidated actions seeking refunds of illegally assessed vehicle license and use taxes. Petitioner, the California Department of Motor Vehicles, sought a writ of mandate directing the trial court to vacate its order on the grounds that the class improperly included persons who had not filed tax refund claims or consented to representation, and that it improperly ordered petitioner to provide notice to all purported members of the class. The court issued the writ of mandate, directed the trial court to enter an order certifying a class limited to persons whose timely claims were rejected within three years of the filing of each case, and held that there was no requirement that each claimant consent to representation, but that each person could opt out of the class. The court also ordered that because notification of eligible class members was rendered impracticable by petitioner's practice of returning rejected claims, the parties must equally share the expense. The court also held that because it failed to provide sufficient notice to petitioner, the trial court must reconsider its appointment of contractors to assist in the notification.


OUTCOME: The court issued a writ of mandate ordering the trial court to vacate its order certifying the class and to issue a new order, finding that the class must be limited to persons whose timely claims were rejected within three years preceding the filing of each of the consolidated cases, that there was no requirement that each claimant consent to representation prior to certification, and that the parties must share the expense of notification.

State Comp. Ins. Fund v. Workers' Comp. Appeals Bd.


No. B120000.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


66 Cal. App. 4th 1154; 78 Cal. Rptr. 2d 448; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 804; 98 Daily Journal DAR 10287



August 28, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published September 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING to review a decision of the Workers' Compensation Appeals Board. W.C.A.B. No. PAS00135.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the WCAB is annulled and the matter is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant workers' compensation carrier sought review of a decision of the California Workers' Compensation Appeals Board that determined that unreasonable delay had occurred in appellant's payment of an annuity and imposed penalties and interest on appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant workers' compensation carrier issued checks to a disabled worker as annuity payments. When the worker had difficulty cashing the checks, he complained to appellee, the California Workers' Compensation Appeals Board, that appellant had violated Cal. Lab. Code § 4651. Appellee agreed and imposed penalties and interest for unreasonable delay pursuant to § 4651. Appellant sought judicial review and asserted that § 4651 did not apply to annuity payments and that, in the alternative, if § 4651 did apply, no violation had occurred. The court held that appellant had not violated § 4651 because the funds were received within three business days of the date stipulated by the parties. The court held that appellant therefore did not owe penalties and interest. The court annulled appellee's decision imposing penalties and interest on appellant and remanded the matter for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court annulled appellee's decision imposing penalties and interest on appellant workers' compensation carrier because it held that appellant had not violated the statute prohibiting unreasonable delays in payments to disabled workers. The court remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

424 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Stirling v. Jones


C029207


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


66 Cal. App. 4th 277; 77 Cal. Rptr. 2d 791; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 739; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6697; 98 Daily Journal DAR 9192



August 26, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Withdrawn October 14, 1998 and the Reporter of Decisions is directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 6656.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDINGS: Super.Ct.No. 98CS00687. James T. Ford, Judge of the Superior Court of the County of Sacramento.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of mandate Granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of the County of Sacramento (California), which held that he could not use "Chief Deputy Attorney General" as his proposed ballot designation for the election of Attorney General under Cal. Elec. Code § 13107(a)(3), as it contained more than three words.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought to use "Chief Deputy Attorney General" as his proposed ballot designation in the Attorney General election. Respondent, Secretary of State, rejected the designation, stating that under Cal. Elec. Code § 13107(a)(3), the designation could not be more than three words. Petitioner filed suit seeking a mandate that he be allowed to use his designation. The trial court refused and petitioner challenged the ruling. The court held that § 13107(a)(3)'s three-word limit did not violate petitioner's constitutional rights to equal protection and freedom of speech, and dismissed his claim that his requested ballot designation must be accepted because it was the only accurate designation. However, the court determined that under Cal. Elec. Code §9(5), hyphenated words that appear generally in a dictionary shall be considered as one word. The court stated that "Attorney-General," as hyphenated appeared in a dictionary, and thus constituted one word. The court concluded that petitioner substantially complied with the election code's time limit for determining his designation. The court granted the mandate, and ordered that "Chief Deputy Attorney-General" be placed on the ballot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, and held that petitioner could have "Chief Deputy Attorney-General" placed on the ballot for the Attorney General election as his proposed ballot designation, as "Attorney-General" constituted one word, and that he substantially complied with the election code's time limit.

People v. Lopez


No. F028223.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


66 Cal. App. 4th 615; 78 Cal. Rptr. 2d 66; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 760; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6970; 98 Daily Journal DAR 9572



August 26, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published September 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County. Super. Ct. No. 38727. Glade F. Roper, Judge. *


* Judge of the Tulare Municipal Court, Porterville Division, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, section 6 of the California Constitution.



DISPOSITION: Except to the extent of this modification to the conditions of probation imposed upon appellant, the judgment is affirmed. The case is remanded to the trial court to reconsider, upon motion by either of the parties, whether the phrase "identified by law enforcement or the probation officer" should remain in condition No. 15.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County (California), contending the condition of probation proscribing gang association and indicia should have been stricken or narrowed because it: 1) was not reasonably related to the instant crime or to future criminality; 2) violated his constitutional rights of freedom of association, speech and due process; and 3) violated the terms of the plea agreement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled nolo contendere pursuant to a plea agreement, and appealed the probationary sentence imposed by the trial court. The court held that condition No. 15 suffered from constitutionally fatal overbreadth because it prohibited appellant from associating with persons not known to him to be gang members, and from displaying indicia not known to him to be gang related. The court therefore modified the condition so as to add the element of knowledge of persons known to be gang members, and to make it applicable only to displays of symbols known by appellant to have a gang connotation. The condition was further modified so as to incorporate the statutory definition of "gangs" and to stipulate that the removal of tattoos on his body that existed prior to sentencing was not required. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded to the trial court for reconsideration of whether the phrase "identified by law enforcement or the probation officer" should remain in condition No. 15.


OUTCOME: The conditions of probation imposed on appellant were affirmed with the exception of the court's modification of condition No. 15. The court held that condition No. 15 suffered from constitutional overbreadth and vagueness. The court therefore modified the condition so as to remedy the constitutional infirmities and remanded to the trial court for reconsideration of the removal of certain other language.

 

426 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Isaac v. City of L.A.


No. B109234.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


66 Cal. App. 4th 586; 77 Cal. Rptr. 2d 752; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 733; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6568; 98 Daily Journal DAR 9076



August 21, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified September 10, 1998. Second Modification on Denial od Rehearing September 21, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 793. Review Denied November 18, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 7467.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC 090601. Paul G. Flynn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the superior court is affirmed. The parties are to bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city officials sought review of judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) in favor of respondents, owners of master-metered real property, in their action for a refund of special assessments levied against them for unpaid utility bills under Los Angeles City, CA Admin. Code, § 6.500 et seq., (1987). Appellants asserted that ordinance did not violate equal protection, due process, or Cal. Const. art. XIII A.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a judgment in favor of respondents in their action against appellant city officials for a refund of special assessments levied by appellants against respondents' master-metered real properties on account of delinquent utility bills. The court held that Los Angeles City, CA Admin. Code, § 6.500 et seq., (1987), an ordinance which empowered appellants to make the assessments and record a super-priority lien on respondents' real properties, was preempted by the statewide statutory scheme governing the priority of liens upon real property. The court found that the lien imposed by the ordinance was not a special tax or a special assessment and thus did not implicate the concerns of Proposition 13, Cal. Const. art. XIII A. The court found that at most the lien was a user fee. The court held that the area of lien priority was preempted when it was a matter of statewide concern due to the need for uniformity. The court held that the ordinance disrupted the state's statutory scheme and was therefore not a valid exercise of municipal authority under Cal. Const. art. XI, § 5(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment on different grounds. The court did not reach equal protection and due process arguments and held that ordinance did not implicate concerns of Proposition 13. The court held that the ordinance was invalid when the area of lien priority was preempted by the state. The court found that due to the need for uniformity, lien priority was a matter of statewide concern and was not a proper matter for municipal action.

 

427 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Rodriguez


No. B112980.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


66 Cal. App. 4th 157; 77 Cal. Rptr. 2d 676; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 727; 98 Daily Journal DAR 9025



August 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review denied November 24, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 7910.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the County of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. LA025190. Sandy R. Kreigler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The abstract of judgment is ordered corrected to reflect that defendant (appellant) was sentenced to a term of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. The superior court is ordered to forward a certified copy of the corrected abstract to the Department of Corrections. In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review for his conviction for first-degree murder, under the special circumstance of Cal. Penal Code § 190.2(a)(21), from the Superior Court of the County of Los Angeles County (California). Appellant asserted that the statute, which required a life sentence for an intentional murder by shooting out of a vehicle, was unconstitutional on its face and as applied, under U.S Const. amend. XIV and VIII.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for first degree murder. Following an altercation in a parking lot, appellant followed victim in his vehicle, and eventually fired shots from his car that killed victim. Appellant asserted that the special circumstance under which he was convicted, Cal. Penal Code § 190.2(a)(21) was unconstitutional both on its face and as applied under the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and U.S. Const. amend. VIII. First, the court rejected appellant's argument that the statute was overbroad when there was no constitutionally protected activity that was being chilled. Next, the court held that the statute was facially valid when appellant himself acknowledged that it could be constitutionally applied to some circumstances. Third, the court held that the statute as applied was not unconstitutional when the legislature had rational reasons to discourage the carrying of loaded firearms in vehicles. Fourth, the court held that the statute did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VIII when life in prison was a permissible punishment for any intentional murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional on its face when appellant acknowledged that there were constitutional applications. The court held the statute was not overbroad when the legislature had an interest in discouraging carrying loaded weapons in cars. The court held that the statute was not cruel and unusual punishment when life in prison was permissible for any intentional murder.

 

428 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Ensoniq Corp. v. Superior Court


No. H016861.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


65 Cal. App. 4th 1537; 77 Cal. Rptr. 2d 507; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 712; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6387; 98 Daily Journal DAR 8833



August 14, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied November 18, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 7593.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County. Super. Ct. No. 193688. James Emerson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Let a peremptory writ of mandate issue, directing respondeat superior court to (1) vacate its order of April 17, 1997, that the hearing on Dattoro's motion to return property will be held in conformance with the procedures outlined in McGraw, supra, 100 Cal. App. 3d 154; and (2) enter a new and different order granting the motion to return property and returning actual possession of the items seized pursuant to search warrant No. 96-038 to Dattoro. Each party to this writ proceeding is to bear his or its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of mandate to compel respondent, the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), to vacate its order ruling that petitioner had no standing to participate in a hearing on a motion of petitioner's former employee for return of property seized under a search warrant and permitting the district attorney to present evidence that petitioner was the rightful owner of the disputed property.


OVERVIEW: After a design engineer employed by petitioner resigned and took engineering notebooks and other items, petitioner reported an alleged theft of trade secrets. The district attorney obtained a search warrant for the former employee's residence and vehicle, and the notebooks and other items were seized. The district attorney decided not to prosecute on the grounds that he lacked evidence to prove intent. The former employee filed a motion to return the seized property under Cal. Penal Code §§ 1536, 1539, 1540. The trial court ruled that petitioner had no standing to participate in the hearing, and that the district attorney should oppose the motion. Petitioner sought review by filing a petition for a writ of mandate. The court granted the petition, and ordered the trial court to vacate its order regarding conduct of the hearing and to enter an order returning the disputed property to the former employee. It held that petitioner lacked standing to apply for delivery of the property or to prove its ownership in criminal court, and that the district attorney could not be compelled, in the absence of evidence that the property was stolen, to oppose a motion for return of the property.


OUTCOME: The court held that petitioner had no standing to apply for delivery of the property or to prove its ownership, and further that the district attorney could not be compelled to oppose a motion for the return of the property. The court granted the petition for writ of mandate, and ordered the trial court to vacate its order setting a hearing and to enter an order returning the actual possession of the property to the former employee.
