People v. Gray


No. A078807.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


66 Cal. App. 4th 973; 78 Cal. Rptr. 2d 191; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 776; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7168; 98 Daily Journal DAR 9875



August 12, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976(b), this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts III and IV.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Partially Published September 10, 1998. Review Denied November 18, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 7448.
Review denied by People v. Gray, 1998 Cal. LEXIS 7448 (Cal., Nov. 17, 1998)
Review denied by People v. Gray, 2012 Cal. LEXIS 3075 (Cal., Mar. 28, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: San Francisco Superior Court. Contra Costa County Super. Ct. No. 970032-9. Hon. Richard Richard S. Flier.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction, by the Contra Costa County Superior Court (California), of attempted carjacking and attempted kidnapping, contending that Cal. Penal Code § 215(a) was unconstitutionally vague, that the evidence was insufficient to support the attempted carjacking conviction, and that the trial court erred in its denial of appellant's motion for a mistrial and in its rulings on various evidentiary motions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of attempted carjacking and of attempted kidnapping, and on review, the court affirmed his convictions. It held that the terms "felonious taking" and "temporarily deprive" in Cal. Penal Code § 215(a) permitted a conviction based on an intent either to permanently or temporarily deprive an owner of possession of his car, and were not unconstitutionally vague. The court further held that the victim was deprived of possession even though not physically forced out of her car, and that the evidence was sufficient to show that appellant exercised dominion and control over the car by force or fear. The court further held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's motion for a mistrial although his sudden decision to testify may have adversely affected his counsel's trial strategy; that appellant did not sustain his burden of showing that his counsel was ineffective; and that his sentence was neither grossly disproportionate to his crimes nor so disproportionate as to shock the conscience and offend fundamental notions of human dignity, and thus did not violate constitutional prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that the carjacking statute was not unconstitutionally vague, that sufficient evidence showed appellant's intent to exercise dominion and control over his victim's car even though she remained in the car, that appellant failed to demonstrate that his counsel was ineffective, and that his sentence was not disproportionate so as to violate the prohibition on cruel and unusual punishment.

 

430 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Costa v. Workers' Comp. Appeals Bd.


No. G022181.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


65 Cal. App. 4th 1177; 77 Cal. Rptr. 2d 289; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 684; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5994; 63 Cal. Comp. Cases 814; 98 Daily Journal DAR 8309; 136 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P58,440



July 30, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for writ of review from a decision of the Workers' Compensation Appeals Board. WCAB Case No. AHM0053703.



DISPOSITION: The order of the WCAB denying reconsideration of petitioner's claim is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order of respondent Workers' Compensation Appeals Board (California), which dismissed, for lack of jurisdiction, petitioner's application to adjudicate his claim for workers' compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: The court agreed that respondent Workers' Compensation Appeals Board (WCAB) lacked jurisdiction to hear petitioner's claim for workers' compensation benefits, because petitioner's union and employer had agreed to handle employment-related injury claims through an alternative dispute resolution (ADR) procedure authorized by Cal. Lab. Code § 3201.5. Explaining, the court observed that petitioner, having failed to seek resolution of his claim through the ADR procedure, then failed to demonstrate that § 3201.5 and the ADR plan were facially unconstitutional. Noting that Cal. Const. art. XIV, § 4 authorized the legislature to create a complete system of workers' compensation, including the use of arbitration, the court ruled that nothing in the constitution required an expedited hearing or only a pass through one procedural level before reaching the WCAB. Moreover, the statute required government approval and monitoring of the plan to prevent abuse. Further, the ADR procedure established by the union plan was binding on individual employees and, thus, enforceable, as the union had no discretion in limiting the prosecution of claims that were constitutionally authorized.


OUTCOME: Order dismissing, for lack of jurisdiction, petitioner's application for workers' compensation benefits affirmed, because respondent workers' compensation appeals board lacked jurisdiction to hear claim absent any evidence that statute authorizing alternative dispute resolution (ADR), and employer's and union's ADR procedure, were facially unconstitutional, and because ADR procedure established by union plan was binding on individual employees.

 

431 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Craig


No. E020253, No. E021863.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


65 Cal. App. 4th 1082; 83 Cal. Rptr. 2d 1; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 679; 98 Daily Journal DAR 8195; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5925



July 29, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts 1., 3. and 4.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied November 4, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 7379.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING; Petition for Writ of Habeas Corpus. APPEAL from the Superior Court of Riverside County. Super.Ct.No. RIF71131. Patrick F. Magers, Judge.

Previously Reported at 77 Cal. Rptr. 2d 272.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. The petition for writ of habeas corpus is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), and filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, all in connection with his conviction for threatening the life of, or threatening to do serious bodily harm to, a deputy public defender, Cal. Penal Code § 76. He claimed that § 76 required a present ability to make good the threat, and that his trial counsel was incompetent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sent a letter to the deputy district attorney in which he threatened his former public defender. The court held that the letter was an appropriate basis for a conviction under Cal. Penal Code § 76, and affirmed. The court held that § 76 did not require that a defendant have a present ability to carry out the threat, notwithstanding that Cal. Jury Instructions, Criminal No. 7.40, engrafted the present ability requirement onto the crime. The court noted that such requirement was not necessary for § 76 to pass constitutional muster, either. The court rejected a contention that only threats that were capable of immediate execution were constitutionally punishable. The court held that a reasonable doubt instruction was not flawed for lacking a "moral certainty" component. The court found defendant's habeas corpus petition meritless. Alleged error generally related to trial tactics aimed at keeping defendant's extensive murderous, assaultive, and threatening criminal record out of evidence, and defendant showed no prejudice from an arguably objectionable witness response regarding the letter's contents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for threatening the life of a public defender, and denied his petition for writ of habeas corpus. The court held that it was not error to reform a standard jury instruction to delete a reference to present ability to carry out a threat, as present ability was not required by statute or the constitution. Defendant also failed to demonstrate ineffective assistance of counsel.

 

432 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Terhune v. Superior Court


No. A081264.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


65 Cal. App. 4th 864; 76 Cal. Rptr. 2d 841; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 654; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5791; 98 Daily Journal DAR 8025



July 24, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Contra Costa County Super. Ct. No. 972059-0. John C. Minney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The alternative writ is discharged and the stay previously imposed shall remain in effect until the remittitur issues. The petition for a peremptory writ is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, parole board director, challenged the ruling of respondent Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California) which dismissed a petition of commitment of a parolee under the Sexually Violent Predators Act, Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq. and under Cal. Code Regs. tit. 15 § 2616(a)(7).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, parole board director, challenged an order of respondent superior court, which dismissed a petition to commit a parolee under the Sexually Violent Predators Act (SVP Act), Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq. and to hold him for psychiatric treatment under Cal. Code Regs. tit. 15 § 2616(a)(7). Petitioner argued that the revocation of parole for psychiatric treatment under § 2616(a)(7) did not violate substantive procedural due process requirements. The court held that although the legislature vested petitioner with broad power both to impose conditions of parole and revoke parole, petitioner was not authorized to hold a prisoner who had served a determinate term beyond his release date and then revoke his parole before he was released into the community, based solely on a determination that he had a mental disorder and was in need of psychiatric treatment within the meaning of § 2616(a)(7). Therefore, the court concluded that petitioner's utilization of parole revocation under § 2616(a)(7) instead of civil commitment for a mentally disordered inmate who was about to be released into the community on parole was an act in excess of its statutory authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent superior court that dismissed the petition for commitment of a parolee under the Sexually Violent Predators Act and parole revocation based on mental disorder regulation. The court stated that petitioner exceeded its statutory powers because there was no probable cause to commit the parolee within the meaning of applicable statutes.

Santangelo v. Allstate Ins. Co.


No. C027317.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


65 Cal. App. 4th 804; 76 Cal. Rptr. 2d 735; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 643; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5732; 98 Daily Journal DAR 7969



July 23, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified August 18, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. 97CS00898. Joe S. Gray, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment (order) is affirmed. Allstate shall recover its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant auto passenger challenged the order of the Superior Court of Sacramento County, Super. Ct. No. 97CS00898 (California) which denied her petition to compel arbitration against respondent insurer.


OVERVIEW: Appellant passenger sought to recover under the uninsured motorist (UM) provision of an insurance policy issued by respondent insurer and initiated arbitration pursuant to Cal. Ins. Code § 11580.2 et seq. An amendment to § 11590.2 was adopted requiring that her arbitration be completed within five years. Appellant's claim for arbitration had reached its five-year mark and the trial court denied her motion to compel arbitration. The trial court found that arbitration was initiated when appellant sent a letter formally demanding arbitration, it was not concluded within five years, and appellant produced no evidence that it was impossible to conclude arbitration. The trial court's order further stated § 11580.2(i) was procedural and could be retroactively applied. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed the trial court order holding that even before the amendment § 11580.2, appellant was subject to dismissal for delay in prosecution. The court held that after the amended § 11580.2 took effect, appellant took no action to get her case going, and failed to explain how an extension would help her or to demonstrate any abuse of discretion in the trial court's determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order denying appellant passenger's petition to compel arbitration, holding that appellant had initiated arbitration by her letter and failed to conclude arbitration within five years of that date as required by the amended arbitration law. The court held that appellant took no action to conclude arbitration or to show that it was impractical or impossible to do so.

Gonzalez v. County of Tulare


No. F025954.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


65 Cal. App. 4th 777; 76 Cal. Rptr. 2d 707; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 650; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5735; 98 Daily Journal DAR 7944



July 20, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County. Super. Ct. No. 95-171507. Howard R. Broadman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Respondents are awarded costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of the order from the Superior Court of Tulare County (California) which sustained a demurrer on their petition for administrative mandamus.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowners sought review of an order sustaining a demurrer to their petition for administrative mandamus. Appellants objected to respondent county's issuance of conditional use permits and the enactment of a zoning ordinance. Respondents demurred the original petition on the ground that it failed to state a cause of action and it was time barred by former Cal. Gov't Code § 65009 and former Cal. Gov't Code § 65907. Appellants countered the demurrers with the argument that former § 65009(c)(2), and § 65907(a), did not apply. Appellants maintained that Cal. Gov't Code § 65860 was the controlling statute. The court held that under the correct interpretation of statutory law, the service limits of former § 65009(c) governed the action to the extent it related to the new zoning law enacted and that former § 65907 applied to appellants' petition challenging the issuance of the conditional use permit. Therefore appellants' mandamus petition was not served upon respondents within the then existing 120-day limit of former Cal. Gov't Code § 65009, even though the action was timely filed, and the trial court did not err in sustaining respondents' demurrer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order, which dismissed appellants' writ of mandamus action where it was shown that the petition was timely filed, but not timely served upon respondents according to a 120-day statutory limit required by the applicable law.

In re Jeremy G.


No. C028422.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


65 Cal. App. 4th 553; 76 Cal. Rptr. 2d 585; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 623; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5510; 98 Daily Journal DAR 7665



July 13, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 6, 1998. Review Denied October 28, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 7251.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Joaquin County. Super. Ct. No. 53613. Jack Fraser, Juvenile Court Referee.



DISPOSITION: The juvenile court's order granting the minor's suppression motion is reversed. The petition of October 22, 1997, is ordered reinstated and the matter is remanded to the juvenile court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of San Joaquin County (California), that granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence of contraband seized during a weapon's search of defendant's home.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a minor, was arraigned on several criminal offenses and placed on electronic home monitoring. He was directed not to have any weapons. Thereafter, officers received information from a confidential informant that a juvenile wearing a home detention bracelet was selling marijuana from a specified apartment. An officer arrived at defendant's home and asked defendant if he was "searchable." Defendant told officers that he was searchable for weapons. However, defendant was not under a search condition. Officer then conducted a search of the residence for weapons and found contraband. The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress this evidence and the appellate court reversed. The court held that the officer's reliance on defendant's statement that he was searchable for weapons was reasonable. The court found that defendant was 16 years old and did not exhibit signs of immaturity or lack intelligence. As such, the officer could have reasonably believed that defendant was aware of his legal circumstances and would not make a statement against his interest unless it was true. The court therefore reversed the trial court decision and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded a trial court decision granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence of contraband seized during a weapon search of his home. The court found that the search was based on defendant's statement to officer that defendant, a minor on house arrest, was searchable for weapons. The court held that officer's reliance on this statement was reasonable, and thus the officer was entitled to conduct the search.

 

436 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Leckie v. County of Orange


No. G021484.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


65 Cal. App. 4th 334; 76 Cal. Rptr. 2d 426; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 598; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5228; 98 Daily Journal DAR 7299



June 30, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified July 23, 1998. Review Denied October 14, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 6835.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County. Super. Ct. No. 758164. Robert E. Thomas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed; the trial court is directed to enter judgment for the Board, which is entitled to recover its costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant County Assessment Appeals Board sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which granted summary judgment to plaintiff trustee on his claim that the creation of a life estate in real property, upon fee owner's death, was not a change in ownership triggering reassessment for property tax purposes.


OVERVIEW: Trust settlor transferred his home into a revocable trust, providing for a friend to enjoy a life estate upon settlor's death. The remainder interest was then to pass to settlor's children. When settlor died, the county assessor treated the transfer of the life estate to the friend as a change in ownership for tax purposes. Plaintiff trustee challenged the ruling, but it was sustained by defendant County Assessment Appeals Board. Plaintiff filed a tax refund complaint, and the trial court granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment on the transfer of ownership issue. Defendant appealed. The court applied the three-pronged test in Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 60, which defined a change of ownership as a transfer of a present interest in real property, including the beneficial use thereof, the value of which is substantially equal to the value of the fee interest. Finding that the lower court's ruling finding no transfer for assessment purposes was contrary to the language of the tax code and related administrative rules, as well as to the common meaning of the word "ownership," the court reversed and ordered judgment entered for defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of plaintiff trustee, because the creation of a life estate in real estate, upon the death of the fee owner, constituted a transfer of "ownership" of the real property within the meaning of the state tax code and related regulations, and triggered value reassessment for real estate tax purposes.

O'Connor v. Superior Court


F029232


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


65 Cal. App. 4th 113; 76 Cal. Rptr. 2d 138; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 579; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5128; 98 Daily Journal DAR 7165



June 26, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied October 14, 1998 and the Reporter of Decisions is directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 6851.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDINGS: application for writ of mandate. Super. Ct. No. 13974. Paul R. Martin, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal petitioner filed for a writ of mandate/prohibition seeking review of an order of respondent, the Madera County Superior Court (California), which denied petitioner's motion to suppress evidence in a criminal action charging petitioner with possession and cultivation of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with possession and cultivation of marijuana. He filed a motion to suppress, asserting that the search warrant was issued without probable cause, that the search warrant was not issued by a neutral and detached magistrate, and that the executing officer's reliance on the warrant was not objectively reasonable. The trial court denied the motion. Petitioner filed for a writ of mandate/prohibition. The court found that the officer requesting the warrant presented it to his father, a judge. There was no evidence that the officer's father had a direct, personal stake in seeing the warrant issue. Although there was an appearance of partiality, it was not enough to render the judge constitutionally disqualified to act or to implicate the exclusionary rule of U.S. Const. amend. IV. There was ample evidence to show that the judge fulfilled the neutrality requirement. Even if the neutrality requirement had been violated, suppression of evidence was not the appropriate remedy based on the application of a good faith exception to the exclusionary rule. Petitioner's writ was denied.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied. Criminal petitioner was not entitled to a writ of mandate's writ of mandate/prohibition to challenge respondent court's denial of petitioner's motion to suppress evidence, because respondent did not violate the neutrality requirement of the federal constitution.

 

438 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Jovine v. FHP, Inc.


No. B105314.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


64 Cal. App. 4th 1506; 76 Cal. Rptr. 2d 322; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 565; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4960; 14 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 150; 98 Daily Journal DAR 7084; 141 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P58,967



June 24, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC106488. Reginald A. Dunn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The summary judgment is reversed in its entirety and the matter is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings not inconsistent with the views expressed herein. Each party shall bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which adopted the findings of the court-appointed referee and granted summary judgment in favor of defendant employer and supervisor on plaintiff's eight claims for damages arising from her discharge.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee brought suit against defendants, her employer and supervisor, for wrongful discharge. The trial court referred the case to a referee for disposition of the discovery issues. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment which was ruled upon by the referee in defendants' favor. The trial court adopted the referee's holding, and plaintiff appealed. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that the original reference of law and motion matters was not authorized by either statute or the consent of the parties and amounted to an improper delegation of judicial power. There was nothing in the record, other than one phrase in the written order, which made any reference to matters other than discovery issues. The trial court had no authority to make a general reference without plaintiff's consent, and plaintiff did not consent to a general reference. The reference exceeded the authority allowed in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 639(e), which provided for reference to a referee for determination of discovery issues. Plaintiff did not waive any of her objections to the reference and was not estopped to assert her right to object.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded. Defendant employer and supervisor were not entitled to summary judgment in plaintiff employee's wrongful discharge action, because the trial court exceeded its jurisdiction by referring the matter to a referee without the express written consent of the parties.

Proposition 103 Enforcement Project v. Quackenbush


No. B112528.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


64 Cal. App. 4th 1473; 76 Cal. Rptr. 2d 342; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 567; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4969; 98 Daily Journal DAR 7076



June 24, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified July 10, 1998. Review Denied September 16, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 6090.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BS 037146. Kurt Lewin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the matter is remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion. The Proposition 103 Enforcement Project shall recover its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant referendum enforcement project sought review of a decision from the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California), that granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, an insurance commissioner and various insurers. Appellant filed a petition for preliminary and permanent injunction and a complaint for declaratory relief seeking a determination that Cal. Ins. Code § 769.2 was invalid.


OVERVIEW: California voters approved an insurance initiative (Proposition 103), which reduced and instituted control of insurance rates and was incorporated into Cal. Ins. Code § 1861.01. Subsequently, the legislature added Cal. Ins. Code § 769.2, which governed the liability of insurers to refund policyholders' overpayments of premiums for a specified period of time. Appellee referendum enforcement project sought to have § 769.2 declared invalid and to enjoin appellee commissioner from enforcing its provisions in current and future settlements with appellee insurers as to a determination of appellees' liability to refund policyholders' overpayments. The lower court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the decision was reversed and remanded. The appellate court held that, pursuant to Cal. Const. art. II, § 10(c), the enactment of § 769.2 was an unauthorized attempt to amend Proposition 103 because § 769.2 both took away from the provisions of Proposition 103 and changed its scope and effect. The appellate court determined § 769.2 was invalid because it did not further the provisions of Proposition 103.


OUTCOME: The lower court's grant of summary judgment to appellee insurance commissioners and various insurers on appellant referendum enforcement project's claims that a provision of the California Insurance Code was invalid was reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The appellate court held that the relevant provision was invalid because it was an act in excess of the amendatory powers granted to the legislature by the voters.

 

440 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Bunnell v. Dep't of Corr.


No. C025611.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


64 Cal. App. 4th 1360; 76 Cal. Rptr. 2d 58; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 557; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4806; 98 Daily Journal DAR 6805



June 22, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part I of the Discussion.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. 95AS02216. Joe S. Gray, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. CDC shall recover its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former warden appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant California Department of Corrections on plaintiff's claims of violation of 18 U.S.C.S. § 2510 and Cal. Pen. Code § 630 et seq., for placement of a wiretap and listening to plaintiff's conversations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff former warden brought suit against defendant California Department of Corrections, alleging violations of federal and state wiretap laws, 18 U.S.C.S. § 2510 et seq. and Cal. Pen. Code § 630 et seq. Plaintiff was fired and also criminally charged for misconduct that was discovered by a wiretap placed on a telephone. Defendant's motion for summary judgment was granted. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that plaintiff failed to file his suit within the two-year statutory period provided for in 18 U.S.C.S. 2520(e) because it was brought more than three years after he discovered the wiretap. The court held that the state tolling provisions of Cal. Gov't. Code § 945.3 did not apply to the federal claim because 18 U.S.C.S. 2510 et seq. carried its own express statute of limitations with no express tolling provisions. The court held that no federal equitable tolling doctrine applied and that the statute of limitations was not tolled during the pendency of the criminal proceedings against plaintiff.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of defendant California Department of Corrections was affirmed on the grounds that plaintiff former warden filed his suit for violations of state and federal wiretap laws outside the one-year limitations period for the state claims and outside the two-year limitations period for the federal claims.

 

441 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Burbank-Glendale-Pasadena Airport Auth. v. City of Burbank


No. B116038.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


64 Cal. App. 4th 1217; 76 Cal. Rptr. 2d 297; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 545; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4640; 98 Daily Journal DAR 6564



June 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied September 16, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 6115.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County. Super. Ct. No. 168216. Barbara A. Lane, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Costs to respondent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant airport authority challenged an order from the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent city. Appellant alleged the parking tax imposed by respondent was preempted by the Anti-Head Tax Act, violated U.S. Const., art. I, § 8, cl. 3, U.S. Const., art. VI, cl. 2, Burbank, Cal., City Charter § 41, Cal. Gov't. Code § 53723, and the joint powers agreement that created appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant airport authority challenged a judgment granting respondent city's motion for summary judgment in an action that challenged respondent's transient parking tax (TPT). The court reviewed the matter de novo, and affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held as a matter of law that the TPT did not violate the Supremacy Clause, U.S. Const., art. VI, cl. 2, because it was not a tax on air commerce, was paid by the customer, and was not imposed exclusively upon airport businesses. Thus, the TPT was not preempted by the Anti-Head Tax Act, 49 U.S.C.S. § 40116. The court held that the TPT did not violate the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const., art. I, § 8, cl. 3, because it was not a tax on air commerce. The TPT was analogous to the taxes permitted by 49 U.S.C.S. § 40116(e)(1). All transient parking facilities within respondent paid the tax, and it was reasonably related to services provided by respondent because customers used respondent's streets to reach the parking lots. The TPT did not violate Burbank, Cal., City Charter § 41 or Cal. Gov't. Code § 53723 because it was grandfathered, and it did not breach the joint powers agreement which created appellant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of respondent city was affirmed. Respondent's transient parking tax was not preempted by the Anti-Head Tax Act, did not violate the federal Supremacy or Commerce Clauses, did not violate respondent's charter or code, and did not breach the joint powers agreement that created appellant airport authority.

 

442 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Kessel v. Leavitt


B108792 c/w B110750


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


64 Cal. App. 4th 1087; 75 Cal. Rptr. 2d 639; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 532; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4598; 98 Daily Journal DAR 6496



June 15, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied October 14, 1998 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct., Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 6715.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from an order and judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. Nos. SS 006478 and SC 043857. Alan B. Haber and Robert M. Letteau, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), that dismissed plaintiff's foreign judgment against defendant adoption attorney for lack of personal jurisdiction. The judgment was registered under the Sister State Money-Judgments Act, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code §1710.10 et seq. (1974). Plaintiff argued the judgment was entitled to full faith and credit under U.S. Const. art. IV, § 1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant adoption attorney contested West Virginia's personal jurisdiction, lost, and suffered a large judgment in plaintiff father's action for fraudulent concealment of his child in an adoption transaction. Plaintiff registered the judgment in California under the Sister State Money-Judgments Act (act), Cal. Civ. Proc. Code, § 1710.10 et seq. (1974). The court reversed the order that vacated the judgment, the ruling on demurrer, and the judgment of dismissal without leave to amend. The court held that although Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1710.40(a) permitted a sister state judgment to be vacated on any ground which would have been a defense to an action in this state on the sister state judgment, the motion to vacate should not have been heard while the West Virginia appeal was pending. Defendant received a full and fair hearing on the jurisdictional issue in West Virginia, the ruling was entitled to full faith and credit under U.S. Const. art. IV, § 1, and it was protected from collateral attack pending appeal. Defendant's sole remedy was to have sought a stay of enforcement pending appeal, which was mandatory under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1710.50(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that vacated plaintiff father's judgment against defendant adoption attorney, the ruling on demurrer, and the judgment of dismissal. The West Virginia ruling on jurisdiction was entitled to full faith and credit under the federal constitution, and defendant's sole remedy was a stay of enforcement pending appeal.

San Diego Gas & Elec. Co. v. City of Carlsbad


No. D027407.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


64 Cal. App. 4th 785; 75 Cal. Rptr. 2d 534; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 515; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4423; 98 Daily Journal DAR 6042



June 9, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied September 23, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 6314.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. N69413. Lisa Guy-Schall, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The summary judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and its officials, appealed the order of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) that entered summary judgment in favor of plaintiff utility company in a declaratory relief action that alleged that Cal. Const. art. XII, § 8 and Cal. Pub. Util. Code § 701 et seq., preempted a city regulation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that Cal. Const. art. XII, § 8 and Cal. Pub. Util. Code § 701 et seq. preempted defendant city's floodplain ordinance that required plaintiff utility to obtain a permit to deposit sand from its dredging operations. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that defendant city's requirement that plaintiff obtain a special use permit to dispose of sand from its dredging operations placed a significant physical and economic burden on the operation and maintenance of plaintiff's facilities. The court held that the ordinance went beyond defendant city's police power into a field that was significantly and fully occupied by the state in such a manner as to indicate clearly that a paramount state concern would not tolerate further or additional local action. The court held that Cal. Pub. Util. Code § 2902, which gave local entities power to promote safety in certain respects, did not preserve local power to regulate the dredging activity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of plaintiff utility because the state constitution and state statutes preempted defendant city's floodplain ordinance.

Warren v. Superior Court


A081080


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


64 Cal. App. 4th 618; 75 Cal. Rptr. 2d 351; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 506; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4339; 98 Daily Journal DAR 5909



June 5, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified on Denial of Rehearing June 26, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 581. Review Denied September 23, 1998 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, section 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Court.), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 6239.


PRIOR HISTORY: San Francisco County Super. Ct. No. 167098-01. Honorable Mary C. Morgan, Retired Judge of the San Francisco County Municipal Court, assigned by the Chief Justice Court, San Francisco County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Let a peremptory writ of mandate issue commanding respondeat superior court to vacate its order disqualifying Judge Warren. Judge Warren shall recover his costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner judge filed a petition for writ of mandate and sought review from an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), in a suit against petitioner trial judge in a felony case. Petitioner was challenged for cause, pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 170.1(a)(6), by defendant's counsel, and the Chief Justice to Retired Municipal Court granted the challenge and disqualified petitioner.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner judge was assigned as trial judge in a felony case. Petitioner informed defendant and his counsel that he suspected that the peremptory challenges had been done on the basis of race. Petitioner was challenged for cause, pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 170.1(a)(6), by defendant, and the Chief Justice to Retired Municipal Court granted the challenge and disqualified petitioner. Petitioner filed a petition for writ of mandate and sought review from respondent, Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. The court held that petitioner had standing to contest his disqualification under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code §§ 170.1 and 170.3. Pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 170.1, petitioner could be disqualified if a person aware of the facts might reasonably entertain a doubt that petitioner would be able to be impartial. The court determined that petitioner only expressed concern over counsel's conduct, which was not grounds for disqualification. The court held that the order disqualifying petitioner was error. The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate issue commanding the lower court to vacate its order of disqualification.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate commanding the lower court to vacate its order disqualifying petitioner judge as trial judge in a felony case from respondent, Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. The court held that petitioner's actions expressing concern over counsel's conduct were not grounds for disqualification because a reasonable person aware of the facts would not doubt that petitioner could be impartial.

 

445 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Scott


No. B112469.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


64 Cal. App. 4th 550; 75 Cal. Rptr. 2d 315; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 501; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4343; 98 Daily Journal DAR 5893



June 5, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied January 18, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 565. Rehearing Denied June 30, 1998. Review Denied September 30, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 6549.


PRIOR HISTORY: MOTION for self-representation on Appeal. Super. Ct. No. BA134892.



DISPOSITION: Scott's motion to proceed in propria persona is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of assault with a firearm under Cal. Penal Code, §245(a)(2) and possession of a firearm by a felon under Cal. Penal Code § 12021(a)(1), and brought a motion to proceed in propria persona on appeal and petition for writ of habeas corpus in which he alleged a deprivation of his right to represent himself on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted and brought a motion to proceed in propria persona on appeal and petition for writ of habeas corpus for deprivation of his right to represent himself on appeal. The court denied the motion to proceed in propria persona and held that there was neither a federal constitutional right to an appeal nor the right to be present at, or to argue, one's own appeal and that the denial of self-representation on an initial appeal as of right did not contravene due process or equal protection guarantees. The court held that the right of a criminal defendant to access to the initial appeal as a matter of right, and the right to counsel at that stage, flowed from the due process and equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, not from U.S. Const. amend. VI. The court held that due process did not allow self-representation as prisoners were precluded from presenting oral argument, there was an elaborate mechanism to ensure competent legal representation of criminal appellants, laypersons generally were ill-equipped to prosecute an appeal, and the administrative burden of self-representation would hinder the efficient functioning of the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to proceed in propria persona on appeal of convictions and held that there was no constitutional right to self-representation on the initial appeal as of right and the denial of self-representation at this level did not violate due process or equal protection guarantees.

People v. Bradley


No. B110426.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


64 Cal. App. 4th 386; 75 Cal. Rptr. 2d 244; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 488; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4172; 98 Daily Journal DAR 5741



June 1, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II.A.4.-7. and II.B-H.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified June 11, 1998. Review Denied September 16, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 6071.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. YA030127. Jean E. Matusinka, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction for possession of a completed check with the intent to defraud ( Pen. Code, § 475a) is reversed and the charge is dismissed. The trial court is to either impose or strike the prior prison term enhancement in Nos. A588238 and A701585 in compliance with California law. The clerk of the superior court is to then prepare an amended abstract of judgment which: deletes all references to count two; awards presentence credits of 259 days, which includes 86 days of conduct credits; and reflects the disposition of the trial court in connection with the imposition or striking of the prior prison term enhancements in Nos. A588238 and A701585, if they are imposed. In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) for forgery under Cal. Penal Code § 470 and possession of a completed check with the intent to defraud under Cal. Penal Code § 475a.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed and dismissed, without comment, defendant's conviction for possession of a completed check with the intent to defraud under Cal. Penal Code § 475a, remanded with directions to impose or strike defendant's sentence enhancements for prior prison terms, and affirmed the remainder of his conviction. Although defendant was found to have served four prior prison terms under Cal. Penal Code § 667.5 (b) and to have previously been convicted of four serious felonies under Cal. Penal Code §§ 667(b)-(i) and 1170.12 (a)-(d), the trial court never struck or imposed the prior prison term enhancements either pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1385 (a) or former Cal. Penal Code § 1170.1 (h). The court found that the trial court's refusal to sentence was legally unauthorized and held that the trial court judge retained the power under §1385 (a) to strike a § 667.5 (b) prior prison term enhancement. The court held that the repeal of former § 1170.1 (h) did not violate ex post facto principles, as it did not result in an increase in the punishment for a prior prison term pursuant to § 667.5 (b).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and dismissed defendant's conviction for possession of a completed check with the intent to defraud and remanded his forgery case with directions that the trial court either impose or strike defendant's prior prison term enhancements of his sentence. The trial court retained the power to strike prior prison term enhancements and the enhancement law did not violate ex post facto protections.

People v. Falsetta


A077116


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


64 Cal. App. 4th 291; 75 Cal. Rptr. 2d 232; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 483; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4063; 98 Daily Journal DAR 5605



May 28, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted August 12, 1998 (S071521), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 5180.
Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Supreme Court of California Opinion of November 1, 1999, Reported at: 21 Cal. 4th 903.


PRIOR HISTORY: Alameda County. Alameda County. Super. Ct. No. CH20852. Jeffrey W. Horner, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Alameda County Superior Court (California) that convicted defendant of forcible oral copulation, assault with the intent to rape, assault with force likely to cause great bodily injury, and kidnapping with sentence enhancements for inflicting great bodily injury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of assault with the intent to rape and other related crimes. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions. The court held that Cal. Evid. Code § 1108, which allowed the trial court to admit evidence of two previous sex crimes, did not offend a fundamental principle of justice and therefore comported with due process. The court recognized that in order for evidence to be admissible under § 1108, a trial court must weigh the probative value of the prior sex crime evidence against the possibility that the evidence's admission will be prejudicial, misleading, or time-consuming. The court held that the trial court had no duty to give defendant's proposed limiting instruction on the issue of the prior sex crimes because the proposed instruction was partially incorrect, lengthy, and potentially confusing. The court recognized that even if the trial court erred by failing to give a limiting instruction, any error was harmless because the prior crimes were similar to the charged offense; the testimony on those crimes was neither lengthy nor cumulative; and the other evidence against defendant was overwhelming.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of forcible oral copulation, assault with the intent to rape, assault with force likely to cause great bodily injury, and kidnapping because the statute that allowed the introduction into evidence of other sex crimes did not offend due process and the trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury on the use of the prior sexual misconduct evidence.

Rainbow Disposal Co. v. Escondido Mobilehome Park Rental Review Bd.


No. D027338.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


64 Cal. App. 4th 1159; 75 Cal. Rptr. 2d 746; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 539; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4613; 98 Daily Journal DAR 6533



May 26, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published June 15, 1998. Review Denied August 19, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 5521.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. N67137. Lisa Guy-Schall, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant disposal company sought review of an order from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which denied its petition for an administrative writ of mandamus challenging the adequacy of a mobile home park rental increase authorized by respondent mobile home rent review board.


OVERVIEW: Appellant disposal company filed a motion for administrative mandamus challenging respondent mobile home rent review board's decision to grant a rent increase in a mobile home park. Appellant sought review of a lower court's order denying its petition for administrative mandamus. The court affirmed the lower court's order. The court found that in making a reference to rent control in a published decision, the Public Utilities Commission (PUC) was merely acknowledging that its task was to control utility rates, not rent. Accordingly, the PUC's prohibition against recovering gas and electricity costs from tenants through rent surcharges was not a rent control, but a utility-rate control. The court determined that respondent correctly viewed the PUC's decision as precluding appellant's recovery of its expenditures on gas and electric improvements through a rent increase. The court concluded that the evidence sufficiently supported respondent's finding that a consultant's recommended increase provided appellant a fair return on its equity investment. Respondent was not obliged to reject the consultant's analysis just because another formula would have yielded a higher rent increase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a lower court's order denying appellant disposal company's petition for writ of mandamus challenging respondent mobile home rent review board's rental increase, because appellant could not recover expenditures for gas and electric improvements through a rent increase. The court concluded that the evidence sufficiently supported respondent's finding that the rent increase provided appellant a fair return on its investment.

People v. Frazier


No. C022971.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


63 Cal. App. 4th 1307; 74 Cal. Rptr. 2d 627; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 433; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3780; 98 Daily Journal DAR 5120



May 15, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts I and III through VI.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied August 19, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 5502.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. 95F00596. Jack Sapunor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of methamphetamine pursuant to Cal. Health & Safety Code, §11377(a), and sentence under Cal. Penal Code §§ 667(d), 1170.12, the three strikes law, by the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for possession of methamphetamine after police discovered the drug and drug paraphernalia at his home. Defendant contended that he thought the drugs belonged to his brother, who had visited his home, and told his wife to dispose of the drugs. On appeal, defendant contended, inter alia, that the trial court had a duty to instruct the jury sua sponte on Cal. Jury Instructions - Criminal No. 12.06, regarding the defense of transitory possession. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that defendant's possession of the controlled substance was neither fleeting nor personally for the purpose of abandonment, disposal, or destruction. Thus, defendant's lengthy possession of the contraband denied him the right to a momentary possession instruction under Cal. Jury Instructions - Criminal No. 12.06, despite his stated intent to dispose of the drugs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of possession of methamphetamine because he was not entitled to a jury instruction regarding the defense of transitory possession, as his possession of the substance was neither fleeting or for the purpose of disposal.

People v. Ritson


C026168


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


63 Cal. App. 4th 1276; 74 Cal. Rptr. 2d 698; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 427; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3683; 98 Daily Journal DAR 5079



May 14, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted August 12, 1998 (S071200), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 5177.
Review Dismissed December 15, 1999 and cause remanded to the Ct. of App., 3d Dist. (rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 8656.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of El Dorado County. Super. Ct. No. PR000332. Eddie T. Keller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions in the Superior Court of El Dorado County (California) for committing a lewd and lascivious act with a minor, Cal. Penal Code § 288(c)(1), annoying or molesting a minor after having suffered a prior conviction for a specified sexual offense involving a minor, Cal. Penal Code § 647.6(a), (c)(2), attempted kidnapping, Cal. Penal Code §§ 664, 207(a), 208(b), and sexual battery, Cal. Penal Code § 243.4(d)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for committing a lewd and lascivious act with a minor under the age of 14, counts of annoying or molesting a minor under the age of 18 after having suffered a prior conviction for a specified sexual offense involving a minor, attempted kidnapping of a minor under the age of 14, and misdemeanor sexual. On appeal, the court reduced the charges of annoying or molesting a minor under the age of 18 to misdemeanors under Cal. Penal Code § 647.6(a), holding that defendant's prior conviction under Cal. Penal Code § 288a(c) was not an enumerated offense under Cal. Penal Code § 647.6(c)(2), which would have permitted a § 647.6(a) offense to be deemed a felony. Evidence of defendant's prior crimes was admissible under Cal. Evid. Code § 1108, where the crimes were similar to the present offenses, showed intent and modus operandi, and were not remote in time. The child-witness jury instruction was proper. The omission of lesser-included- and -related-offense and unanimity jury instructions was at most harmless error. The 105-year sentence was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court reduced defendant's convictions on three counts of annoying or molesting a minor after having suffered a prior conviction for a specified sexual offense involving a minor to misdemeanors, because defendant had no prior conviction that would justify their being made into felonies. The court affirmed defendant's remaining convictions, denying his challenges to the admission of evidence and the court's jury instructions.

People v. O'Roark


No. B093085.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


63 Cal. App. 4th 872; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 924; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 399; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3419; 98 Daily Journal DAR 4683



May 5, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts 2 through 7.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. SA019408. Leslie W. Light, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction is affirmed. The judgment sentencing appellant to a determinate prison term of 27 years followed by three consecutive terms of 25 years to life is reversed, and the matter is remanded for resentencing to enable the trial court to exercise its discretion whether to vacate one or more of the qualifying prior felony conviction findings under the three strikes law on its own motion in the furtherance of justice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: California Supreme Court remanded cause to the court for reconsideration of appeal filed by appellant from judgment of Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of second-degree robbery and sentenced him to determinate term of 27 years followed by three consecutive terms of 25 years to life.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of three counts of second-degree robbery. The jury found he had three prior serious felony convictions within the meaning of the three strikes law, Cal. Penal Code § 667. Appellant was sentenced to a determinate term of 27 years followed by three consecutive terms of 25 years to life. The court affirmed. The California Supreme Court remanded with directions to reconsider the cause. The court affirmed appellant's conviction, but reversed the sentence. Prior serious felony convictions sustained before the effective date of Cal. Penal Code § 1192.7, which defined what constituted a serious felony for purposes of the three strikes law, could qualify as strikes if the felony resulting in that prior conviction was in the list of serious felonies in section 1192.7 on June 30, 1993. Thus, the trial court properly determined that appellant's 1978 robbery conviction and 1987 bank robbery conviction could be used as strikes. However, the court remanded to enable the trial court to exercise its discretion whether to vacate one or more of the qualifying prior felony conviction findings under the three strikes law on its own motion in the furtherance of justice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, but reversed the sentence and remanded to enable the trial court to exercise its discretion whether to vacate one or more of the qualifying prior felony conviction findings under the three strikes law on its own motion in the furtherance of justice.

 

452 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Baby Boy H.


No. F029022.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


63 Cal. App. 4th 470; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 793; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 359; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3068; 98 Daily Journal DAR 4179



April 21, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 8, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 4502.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County. Super. Ct. No. 83730. Jerold L. Turner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, whose baby had been adjudged dependent after respondent county human services department filed a juvenile dependency petition under Cal. Welf. & Inst. § 300, filed an appeal from the judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County (California), which determined that reunification services need not be provided to appellant.


OVERVIEW: Respondent county human services department filed a juvenile dependency petition against appellant after she gave birth to a baby who tested positive for opiates. At the time, two of her children were dependent children and her parental rights had been terminated with respect to two other children who had been adopted. The trial court adjudged the baby a dependent child. Thereafter, it terminated reunification services for appellant's two other dependent children. After the dispositional hearing for appellant's baby, the trial court determined that reunification services need not be provided to appellant. The court affirmed. Cal. Welf. & Inst. § 361.5(b)(10)(A) stated that reunification services need not be provided to a parent where, as here, the court found by clear and convincing evidence that adoption was ordered for the minor's sibling after the sibling had been removed from the parent pursuant to section 361. Section 361.5(b)(10) did not violate a parent's constitutional right to procedural due process because, at the dispositional hearing, the burden was on the state to prove, by clear and convincing evidence, that the child's removal from the parent's custody was necessary.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed judgment that reunification services need not be provided. California Welfare and Institutions Code provided that reunification services need not be provided to parent where, as here, court found by clear and convincing evidence that adoption plan was ordered for minor's sibling after sibling had been removed from parent.

 

453 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Waste Management of Alameda County v. Biagini Waste Reduction Sys.


No. A077664.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


63 Cal. App. 4th 1488; 74 Cal. Rptr. 2d 676; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 446; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3846; 98 Daily Journal DAR 5307



April 21, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976(b), this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts I., II., III., and V.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Partially Published May 20, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County. Super. Ct. No. 773909-5A. Sandra Lynn Margulies, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Costs are awarded to respondent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California) granting plaintiff's request for a preliminary injunction and commanding defendant to refrain from collecting or disposing of any solid waste within the city in violation of the terms of a city ordinance as well as an agreement between plaintiff and the city.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance to create an exclusive franchise for collection and disposal of solid waste. The city entered into an exclusive arrangement with plaintiff. Plaintiff filed a complaint for damages and declaratory and injunctive relief alleging defendant had contracted with others to collect and dispose of construction debris generated within the city. The trial court granted a preliminary injunction commanding defendant to refrain from its collection activities. Defendant appealed. The court concluded that the trial court did not err by issuing a preliminary injunction because the terms of the city ordinance constituted a constitutionally valid exclusive franchise waste collection ordinance. The court found that the ordinance and the associated agreement by which plaintiff became the exclusive franchise collector of solid waste generated and transported within the city had no impermissible discriminatory effect upon interstate commerce. The ordinance did not directly regulate interstate commerce, and the court found that the incidental burden it imposed was not clearly excessive in relation to the benefits obtained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in plaintiff's favor and awarded costs to plaintiff. The court concluded that the city ordinance did not violate the dormant commerce clause doctrine and that plaintiff and the city were entitled to contract for an exclusive franchise agreement for waste collection.

People v. Robinson


No. B107563.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX

April 20, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County. Super. Ct. No. F248907. Teresa Estrada-Mullaney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The trial court here properly denied appellant's ex post facto violation motion. The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court, San Luis Obispo County (California), finding him to be a mentally disordered offender pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 2962, when he violated his parole after conviction for two counts of involuntary manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of two counts of involuntary manslaughter under Cal. Penal Code § 192(b) and was sentenced and later paroled. After violating his parole, the Board of Prison Terms found that appellant met the mentally disordered offender criteria under Cal. Penal Code § 2962. The trial court upheld the commitment, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed, finding that the mentally disordered offender statutory scheme was civil in nature, and that the retroactive application of a nonpenal statute did not violate the U.S. Const. or Cal. Const. ex post facto clauses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's finding that appellant met the mentally disordered offender criteria for commitment because the nonpenal statutory scheme did not violate constitutional ex post facto clauses.

Mapstead v. Anchundo


No. H016459.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


63 Cal. App. 4th 246; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 602; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 336; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2911; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3967



April 17, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 12, 1998. Review Denied July 22, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 4809.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Monterey County. Super. Ct. No. M34796. Harkjoon Paik, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The appeal from the judgment on the merits is dismissed as moot. The trial court's "Amended Revised Order Amending Judgment To Specify Costs and Attorneys Fees," filed December 18, 1996, is reversed. Each party shall bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant registrar and appellant intervenor sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Monterey County (California), which found that appellant registrar improperly excluded certain signatures on a referendum petition pursuant to Cal. Elec. Code § 9144 and, therefore ordered the referendum to be placed on the ballot. Appellants also sought review of an award of attorney fees to appellee intervenor.


OVERVIEW: A referendum petition was circulated protesting the adoption of a certain ordinance. Appellee sought a writ of mandate after appellant registrar certified that the referendum petition lacked sufficient valid signatures under Cal. Elec. Code § 9144. The trial court determined that appellant should have counted certain excluded signatures, ordered the referendum to be placed on the election ballot, and awarded attorneys fees to appellee intervenor. On review, the court found that appellant correctly certified that a referendum petition contained insufficient signatures for placement on the ballot. However, under the particular circumstances of the case, the court held that the controversy had become moot by virtue of the intervening election. Therefore, the court denied appellant intervenor's request to treat the election as a nullity. Accordingly, the appeal was dismissed, and the trial court's order awarding attorney fees was reversed.


OUTCOME: The appeal from the judgment on the merits was dismissed because the controversy became moot by virtue of the intervening election. However, the court held that appellant registrar correctly certified that the petition contained insufficient signatures for placement on the ballot, therefore, the award of attorney fees and costs to appellee intervenor was reversed as inappropriate.

Weaver v. State of California


No. B112827.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


63 Cal. App. 4th 188; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 571; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 333; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2870; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3893



April 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 8, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 4394.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. GC014750. Terry Smerling, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The summary judgment is affirmed. The parties are to bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minor sought review of a grant of summary judgment in favor of defendants, officer, supervisor, commissioner, and the State of California, by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) in plaintiff's action under state law and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 to recover for injuries he sustained in an automobile accident following a police pursuit.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff minor was a passenger in a vehicle that was involved in a police chase. Plaintiff was injured when defendant officer ran his car into the rear of the vehicle, causing it to crash. Plaintiff filed suit against defendants, officer, supervisor, commissioner, and the State of California, alleging state law claims and a claim under 42 U.S.C.S § 1983 for the violation of his U.S. Const. amend. IV rights. The trial court granted defendants' motions for summary judgment. The court affirmed, concluding that defendant state was immune from liability for the state law claims pursuant to Cal. Veh. Code § 17004.7 because it adopted a policy on vehicular pursuits that complied with § 17004.7(c). Further, the court found that defendants police officer and supervisor were immune from liability for the state law claims pursuant to Cal. Veh. Code § 17004.7, as plaintiff's injuries arose out of the operation of a police vehicle. The court also found that defendant commissioner was immune from liability for the acts of his subordinates under Cal. Gov't Code § 820.8. Finally, the court held that the § 1983 claim was properly dismissed because the seizure of the vehicle was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of defendants, officer, supervisor, commissioner, and the State of California, because defendants were immune from liability for plaintiff minor's state law claims, and the seizure of the vehicle in which plaintiff was a passenger was reasonable and thus did not violate plaintiff's Fourth Amendment rights.

 

457 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Consol. Fire Prot. Dist. v. Howard Jarvis Taxpayers' Ass'n


No. B112714.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


63 Cal. App. 4th 211; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 586; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 334; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2866; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3887



April 16, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC 162641. Richard P. Kalustian, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Defendants are awarded their costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff fire protection district appealed the decision by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted judgment on the pleadings to defendant taxpayers' association on plaintiff's claim seeking to validate a resolution permitting a fire suppression assessment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff fire protection district filed a complaint against defendant taxpayers' association to validate a resolution, which permitted a fire suppression assessment without voter approval. Defendant asserted that the resolution violated Cal. Const. art. XIII D, that the resolution was not adopted according to law, and that the complaint failed to state a cause of action. The trial court granted judgment on the pleadings to defendant. Plaintiff appealed. The appellate court held that plaintiff's complaint failed to state a cause of action. Plaintiff argued that once the assessment was levied a contract arose between plaintiff and the property owners subject to assessment. The assessment contract allegedly could not be impaired by a law subsequently passed under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1. However, the court concluded that the type of contract rights at issue were not subject to constitutional protection. In addition, the court determined that plaintiff had no contract as there was no enforceable duty to provide fire protection at all. Rather, plaintiff's resolution was an ordinance subject to repeal through the initiative process.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision to grant defendant taxpayers' association judgment on the pleadings because the resolution permitting a fire suppression assessment did not create a contract between defendants and plaintiff fire suppression district that was subject to constitutional protection from laws enacted after the resolution.

Bostean v. Los Angeles Unified School Dist.


No. B109857.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


63 Cal. App. 4th 95; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 523; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 329; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3827; 13 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1594; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2810



April 15, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC127487. Robert H. O'Brien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the cause is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the views expressed herein. Appellant is entitled to costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Superior Ct. No. BC127487 (California), which denied appellant's request for a writ of mandamus and entered judgment in favor of appellees, school district, personnel commission, individual members of commission, and personnel director, in appellant's action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 alleging that he was wrongfully put on indefinite illness leave.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee was placed on indefinite, involuntary illness leave by appellee school district for a period of seven months. He was reinstated when he successfully appealed the suspension to appellee personnel commission. Appellant thereafter filed suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 alleging that the failure of appellees, school district, personnel commission, individual members of commission, and personnel director, to provide him with written notice of the intended action and an opportunity to respond before imposing the illness leave, and the failure to afford him a hearing afterwards deprived him of his due process rights under U.S. Const. amend XIV. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of appellees. The court reversed, concluding that appellant, as a classified employee, had a property interest in his continued employment and that he was entitled to hearing prior to being placed on leave in light of the seriousness of the deprivation, which resulted in appellant losing pay and benefits, the lack of other procedural protections for appellant, and the lack of any substantial governmental interest in placing appellant on leave without a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of appellant employee's request for a writ of mandamus and the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees, school district, personnel commission, individual members of commission, and personnel director, because appellees deprived appellant of his due process rights by failing to hold a hearing prior to placing appellant on involuntary illness leave. The court remanded the matter for further proceedings.
