In re Genesha S.


E021495


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


63 Cal. App. 4th 1206; 74 Cal. Rptr. 2d 481; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 421; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3690; 98 Daily Journal DAR 5033



April 14, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published May 13, 1998. July 8, 1998 the Reporter of Decision directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 4514.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County.. (Super.Ct.No. J-148315). John N. Martin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant biological father sought review of the judgment by the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), which terminated his parental rights, on grounds that he did not receive notice of the jurisdictional/dispositional hearing or the detention hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was the biological father of a child born addicted to cocaine. The mother refused to identify appellant as the father. At a jurisdictional/dispositional hearing the child was declared a child of the court. After the hearing, respondent Department of Public Social Services learned the identity of appellant and notice of a Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26 permanency planning hearing was served on appellant, who filed a Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 388 petition alleging that he could have been located and seeking to set aside the previous orders. The trial court concluded that appellant was not a presumed father and was not entitled to notice prior to the § 366.26 hearing and terminated appellant's parental rights. The court affirmed the trial court's decision, but on different rationale. Appellant was not entitled to notice of the jurisdiction/disposition hearing as his identity was unknown, and appellant was not a quasi-presumed father. In addition, appellant's due process right to notice was not violated. Appellant could have qualified for notice had he filed a voluntary declaration of paternity or a paternity action prior to the dependency proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because at the time of the jurisdictional/dispositional hearing appellant biological father's identity was unknown so no notice was required, and appellant's due process rights were not violated as he was not a person entitled to notice.

 

460 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Townsend


No. H015880.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


62 Cal. App. 4th 1390; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 438; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 313; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2712; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3715



April 10, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 15, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 4666.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County. Super.Ct.No. 181399. Melinda Stewart, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which convicted defendant of selling and offering to sell cocaine base and possession of cocaine base for sale and enhanced sentence under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11353.6(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of selling and offering to sell cocaine base and possession of cocaine base for sale. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erroneously substituted "when" the offense occurred for "where" the offense occurred in the last clause of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11353.6(b), a statute which created sentence enhancement for conviction of narcotics offenses within 1,000 feet of a school. Defendant argued that the instruction triggered the application of § 11353.6(b) if minors were using the school facility. The court affirmed and held that § 11353.6(b) enhancement applied whenever students were on campus, whether the school was open or closed and the offense took place either on campus or in a public area within 1,000 feet of school boundary. The court held that the trial court's use of when for where was of no significance and that the instruction did not allow the jury to convict on a legally sufficient theory. The court held that the statute was not vague and that ambiguity alone did not mean that a statute was vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of selling and offering to sell cocaine and possession of cocaine base for sale and enhanced sentence because the enhancement section in which the trial court substituted the word when for where was of no significance. The court held that the enhancement statute was not vague because it was capable of more than one meaning.

People v. Pulliam


No. D029293.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


62 Cal. App. 4th 1430; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 371; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 314; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2696; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3690



April 10, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 22, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 4775.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. CA126115. Ernest Borunda, Judge. *


* Judge of the Municipal Court for the South Bay Judicial District, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, section 6 of the California Constitution.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a ruling of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which found defendant guilty of loitering in a public place with intent to commit an act of prostitution in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 653.22.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of loitering in a public place with intent to commit an act of prostitution in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 653.22 after a police officer found defendant in a known prostitution area and defendant admitted that she was in the area to engage in prostitution. She was dressed in a manner which resembled a prostitute and was waiving down a vehicle when the officer arrived. Defendant challenged the trial court ruling and claimed that § 653.22 was unconstitutional because it was vague and overbroad. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the statute at issue was neither vague nor overbroad. The statute was not vague because it provided adequate notice to citizens of the proscribed conduct and provided guidelines to permit nonarbitrary enforcement. The statute was not overly broad where it criminalized only the conduct of loitering with intent to commit prostitution and did not on its face prohibit a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court ruling, which found defendant guilty of loitering in a public place with intent to commit an act of prostitution. The court overruled defendant's claims on appeal and held that the penal statute at issue was neither vague nor overly broad.

In re T.A.J.


No. A076464.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


62 Cal. App. 4th 1350; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 331; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 308; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2659; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3638



April 9, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Alameda County. Super. Ct. No. J167658. Martin J. Jenkins, Judge, and Claudette Brooks, Referee.



DISPOSITION: For the reasons stated in this opinion, the finding on the petition is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor sought review of his conviction by the Superior Court of Alameda County (California) for having sexual intercourse with a minor not more than three years older or younger than himself in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 261.5.


OVERVIEW: Appellant minor was convicted of the misdemeanor offense of having consensual intercourse with a minor not more than three years older or younger than himself in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 261.5. The appellate court affirmed the conviction. Appellant contended that § 261.5 unconstitutionally violated his right to privacy in violation of Cal. Const. art. I, § 1, and could not be applied to him as he was a member of a protected class as defined by the statute. The court reasoned that adults enjoyed a constitutional sexual privacy right whereas minors did not due to their age and maturity. The court also stated that even if minors had the same privacy rights as adults they had no legitimate expectation of privacy, as minors were incompetent to exercise the responsibilities of sexual emancipation. The court also rejected appellant's argument that he was a minor and defined as a victim under the statute, and, therefore, could not be prosecuted as a perpetrator. The fact that appellant could have also been a victim did not prevent him from being a perpetrator.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed appellant minor's conviction for having consensual intercourse with a minor not more than three years older or younger than himself because as a minor appellant did not have a constitutionally protected sexual privacy right, and could be prosecuted as a perpetrator even though he was also defined as a victim under the statute.

People v. Steffens


No. H015980.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


62 Cal. App. 4th 1273; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 314; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 300; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2576; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3535



April 7, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts C, D, E, F, G and H.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied July 15, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 466.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 178893. Robert P. Ahern, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is hereby modified so as to strike the altering count due to the insufficiency of the evidence to support it. The trial court is ordered to amend the abstract of judgment accordingly and forward a certified copy of the abstract to the Department of Corrections. The modified judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions by the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California) for acquiring an access card with intent to defraud, and alteration of and fraudulent use of an access card.


OVERVIEW: Credit cards and ATM cards were found at defendant's residence. Defendant arrived under the influence of methamphetamine and made statements. Defendant was later convicted of acquiring an access card with intent to defraud, alteration and fraudulent use of an access card, and being under the influence of methamphetamine. The court found that the trial judge's instructions on the use count, Cal. Penal Code § 484e and § 484f, were sufficient. However, the court agreed with defendant that the altering count, § 484f(c), required proof that defendant actually caused transactions to be charged to a person other than the one to whom the card was issued. The court examined the legislative history and concluded that the intent of the alteration offense subdivision was to address a situation where the card was altered to that of another account. Because the trial judge's instruction eliminated the requirement of actual billing to another account, the altering count was reversed and retrial was barred as no evidence was presented of the precise nature of the alterations. The judgment was affirmed as to the other counts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the alteration count entered against defendant but otherwise affirmed the judgment. The trial judge incorrectly excluded an element of the offense in his instruction to jury; therefore reversal was required. The court also barred retrial on the count as no evidence to prove the offense was presented.

 

464 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Meller & Snyder v. R & T Properties


No. B102700.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


62 Cal. App. 4th 1303; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 740; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 303; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2600; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3553



April 7, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. SC010289. David M. Rothman, Judge. *


* Retired Judge of the Los Angeles Superior Court, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, § 6 of the California Constitution.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. The matter is remanded for further proceedings consistent with the views expressed in this opinion. Defendant, R & T Properties, Inc., is to recover its costs on appeal from plaintiff, Meller & Snyder.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered judgment for plaintiff law firm in a joint debtor proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff law firm filed a complaint for breach of contract and other claims. The complaint named an individual doing business under a fictitious name and also other fictitious defendants, but not defendant corporation. After trial, judgment was entered against defendant, but the judgment was later expunged for lack of jurisdiction. Next, plaintiff filed an amendment to its complaint and substituted defendant for one of the fictitious defendants. A joint debtor summons was issued against defendant, and at the proceeding, the trial court only required plaintiff to establish the judgement and entered judgment for plaintiff. On appeal, the court reversed. The trial court was required to determine whether plaintiff had complied with Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 474, which required plaintiff to be ignorant of the true name of defendant at the time of naming it as a fictitious defendant. Remand was required for this determination. After examining precedent, the court also concluded that because defendant denied liability due process required plaintiff to prove its case on the merits. As a result, the court reversed and remanded for the trial court to hold the required proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment by the trial court for plaintiff law firm in the joint debtor proceeding because the trial court did not first determine whether plaintiff was aware of the true name of defendant corporation at the time of naming defendant in the pleading under a fictitious name, and the trial court did not require plaintiff to prove its case against defendant as required by due process.

 

465 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Smith


No. D027274.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


62 Cal. App. 4th 1233; 72 Cal. Rptr. 2d 918; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 296; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2574; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3481



April 6, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. SCD117670. William D. Mudd, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the matter is remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which convicted appellant of second degree felony murder based on the underlying crime of extortion under Cal. Penal Code § 518.


OVERVIEW: Appellant fatally shot the victim, whom appellant had known for 20 years. The victim came to appellant's apartment to discuss a $ 75 debt that the victim owed appellant. Appellant refused to accept the victim's offer to repay $ 5 of the debt. The victim was shot in the head and killed, but appellant maintained that the victim was shot accidentally. The trial court convicted appellant of second degree felony murder. Appellant sought review. The court reversed the conviction and remanded for a new trial. The court held that the underlying crime of extortion under Cal. Penal Code § 518 was not an inherently dangerous felony and could not be used to support the application of the second degree felony murder rule. Although the use of force or a threat that created fear under Cal. Penal Code § 520 raised extortion to the level of a felony, the conduct required was not life-threatening. The prosecution argued three theories to support the second degree murder conviction, and the court could not discern which theory was the basis of the jury's verdict. The court could not determine beyond a reasonable doubt that the error did not contribute to the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial the decision of the trial court that convicted appellant of second degree felony murder based on the underlying crime of extortion because extortion was not inherently dangerous and could not support application of the second degree felony murder rule.

 

466 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Cal. Serv. Station Etc. Ass'n v. Am. Home Assur. Co.


No. A074154.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


62 Cal. App. 4th 1166; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 182; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 290; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2464; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3384; 63 Cal. Comp. Cases 373



April 2, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 15, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 4544.


PRIOR HISTORY: Trial Court: San Francisco Superior Court. Super. Ct. No. 932990. Carlos Bea, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant association and appellant trust sought review after the San Francisco Superior Court (California) entered a judgment notwithstanding the verdict or a new trial. Appellants alleged that respondent insurer negligently failed to disclose past dividend calculations for its workers' compensation policies when appellants agreed to market the policies to its members. Cal. Code Regs. tit. 10, § 2505, Cal. Evid. Code § 669.


OVERVIEW: Appellant association and appellant trust filed a lawsuit against respondent insurer alleging negligence based on respondent's failure to disclose past dividend calculations for its workers' compensation policies. The trial court entered a judgment notwithstanding the verdict, or a new trial, after a jury verdict. The court affirmed and held that respondent had no duty to disclose pricing information. The court held that an insured person's initial decision to obtain insurance and the corresponding decision of an insurer to offer coverage remained, at the inception of the contract at least, an arm's-length transaction to be governed by traditional standards of freedom to contract. The court rejected appellants' contention that Cal. Code Regs. tit. 10, § 2505, created a duty of care because an agency, the California Insurance Commission, could not independently impose a duty of care if that authority had not been delegated to the agency by the legislature. The court also held that violation of a statute did not lead automatically to negligence liability; Cal. Evid. Code § 669(a) created only a presumption of negligence, which could be rebutted by Cal. Evid. Code § 669(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The court held that respondent insurer had no duty to disclose past dividend calculations for its workers' compensation policies because respondent did not have a fiduciary relationship with appellant association and appellant trust. The court held that the relationship was governed by traditional standards of freedom to contract.

 

467 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Ketchum v. Cal.


No. C026528.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


62 Cal. App. 4th 957; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 152; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 275; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2398; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3258



March 31, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing April 30, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 384.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. 95AS05709. John R. Lewis, Judge. *


* Judge of the Sacramento Municipal Court, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, section 6 and California Constitution.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff heirs sought review after the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) granted defendant state's motion for summary judgment in a wrongful death action on grounds that defendant had immunity under Cal. Veh. Code § 17004.7. Plaintiffs' mother was killed after being struck by a car that was being pursued by the California Highway Patrol.


OVERVIEW: After their mother died from injuries she received after being struck by a car that was being pursued by the California Highway Patrol (CHP), plaintiff heirs brought a wrongful death action against defendant state. The trial court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment on grounds that defendant had immunity under Cal. Veh. Code § 17004.7. Plaintiffs contended that § 17004.7 violated due process; that the CHP had not validly adopted a pursuit policy pursuant to § 17004.7 because the policy was signed by the deputy commissioner rather than the commissioner of the CHP; and that the policy failed to comply with Cal. Veh. Code § 17004.7(c). The court affirmed. The court rejected plaintiff's due process claim because there was a rational relationship between the legislative policy and the statute. Because the commissioner had approved the policy and the deputy commissioner could sign the approval form in his absence, the trial court properly found that the pursuit policy was adopted by the CHP. And the court rejected the contention that the only way a pursuit policy could provide guidelines was by listing manifest perils.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order that granted summary judgment to defendant state in a wrongful death action filed by plaintiff heirs. The court held that defendant had immunity pursuant to statute because defendant had validly adopted a pursuit policy as statutorily required.

 

468 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Cochran


No. E019590.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


62 Cal. App. 4th 826; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 257; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 262; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2303; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3132



March 27, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 14, 1998. Review Denied June 10, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 3811.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. Super.Ct.No. FVI-03335. Jules E. Fleuret, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Superior Court of San Bernardino (California), which convicted him of assault resulting in the death of a child under the age of eight, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 273ab.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought relief from his conviction of assault resulting in the death of a child under the age of eight, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 273ab. In affirming the decision, the court found that defendant was not deprived of a fair trial when two jurors belatedly disclosed that they knew members of the victim's family because the jurors' acquaintance was too minimal to have produced a substantial likelihood that it influenced the jurors, the evidence of guilt was strong, and the presumption of prejudice had been overcome by the circumstances and content of the nondisclosure. The court ruled that defendant had the care and custody of the victim, because the child lived in his home, he had assumed a parent-like role, and the child's mother had characterized him as a surrogate father. The court ruled that the trial court did not err in instructing the jury with revised jury instructions, and the absence of the terms "moral certainty" and "depending on moral evidence" did not unconstitutionally reduce the people's burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of assault resulting in the death of a child under the age of eight because the late disclosure of two jurors to acquaintance with members of the victims family was too minimal to result in prejudice, defendant had the care and custody of the victim, and the trial court was required to use the 1994 version of a jury charge.

Guevara v. Superior Court


No. H016326.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


62 Cal. App. 4th 864; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 421; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 264; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2305; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3129



March 27, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order extend time was terminated June 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Cruz County, No. S6-09574. Robert Yonts and William Kelsay, Judges.

Original Opinion of December 19, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 1068.



DISPOSITION: Let a peremptory writ of mandate issue directing the Santa Cruz County Superior Court to vacate its order denying petitioner's Penal Code section 995 motion and enter a new and different order granting his motion as to the Penal Code section 245, subdivision (a)(1) counts. Petitioner's request for relief from the superior court's denial of his demurrer is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner defendant sought review of an order by peremptory writ of mandate to the Superior Court of Santa Cruz County (California), which denied petitioner's motion to set aside an information alleging enhanced sexual assault offenses and motion to dismiss and demurrer based on violations of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with sexual offenses and assault under Cal. Penal Code § 245(a)(1), for engaging in unprotected consensual sexual intercourse with a minor without disclosing his human immunodeficiency virus (HIV)-positive status. Petitioner filed motions to set aside the assault charge, dismiss the charges, and a demurrer, which were denied. Petitioner filed a petition for writ of mandate or prohibition, seeking to vacate the charges because there was insufficient evidence to prove that bodily fluids were likely to produce bodily harm to a victim of sexual assault. Further, petitioner asserted that a sentence enhancement under § 12022.85 for being HIV-positive was a violation of equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court granted a peremptory writ of mandate as to the assault charge under § 245(a)(1) because the state failed to offer proof that bodily fluids of petitioner were likely to produce bodily injury. However, the court held that petitioner was not denied equal protection by a sentence enhancement under § 12022.85, because the state had a legitimate interest in identifying persons infected with HIV, who knowingly had unprotected sexual intercourse.


OUTCOME: The court issued a mandate directing respondent judge to vacate its order denying petitioner defendant's motion to dismiss and grant petitioner's motion to dismiss aggravated assault charges, and affirmed trial court's denial of petitioner's demurrer, because the state failed to prove supporting aggravating circumstances of the assault and the enhanced sentence did not violate petitioner's equal protection rights.

 

470 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Friedland v. City of Long Beach


No. B106721.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


62 Cal. App. 4th 835; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 427; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 261; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2299; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3123



March 27, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order and judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC147635. Judith C. Chirlin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Costs are awarded to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed an appeal after the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) sustained defendant agencies' demurrer without leave to appeal. After the time within which to appeal the final judgment entered in defendants' validation action had expired, plaintiffs filed a taxpayer suit. Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 860 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The issue in this case was whether plaintiff taxpayers could maintain a taxpayer suit filed after the period within which to appeal a judgment in a validation action had expired. Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 860 et seq. allowed a public agency to obtain a judgment that its financing commitments with respect to an aquarium were valid, legal, and binding. Defendant agencies filed a validation action and obtained a final judgment. Plaintiffs did not take part in, or timely challenge, the validation action. Plaintiffs then sought a declaratory judgment that defendants had invalidly authorized a gift of public funds and a use of public trust funds inconsistent with the purposes of the trust. The trial court sustained defendants' demurrer. The court affirmed and held that matters that had been or could have been adjudicated in a validation action (including constitutional challenges) had to be raised within the limitations period or they were waived. The court held that validation statutes subjected public agencies' enactments to judicial review and that granting plaintiff's request would encourage agencies to validate their enactments by the safer, less public means of inaction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff taxpayers' lawsuit. The court held that a key objective of a validation action was to limit the extent to which delay due to litigation might impair a public agency's ability to operate financially and that even constitutional challenges were subject to the statutory limitations period.

County Mobilehome Positive Action Com. v. County of San Diego


No. D025554.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged summary judgment by the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which dismissed appellant's challenge of San Diego County, Cal., Code of Regulatory Ordinances Relating to the Standard Mobilhome Park Accord div. 10, § 510.101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation challenged the order of the lower court, which granted summary judgment in favor of respondents county and association. Respondent county enacted San Diego County, Cal., Code of Regulatory Ordinances to the Standard Mobilhome Park Accord div. 10, § 510.101 et seq., pursuant to an agreement that respondent association would offer renters a 15-year lease that contained rent stabilization, conditioned upon respondent county's agreement that it would not pass rent control legislation that would affect respondent association members for a 15-year period. The court reversed the lower court and directed the lower court to enter judgment in favor of appellant. The court found that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it restricted respondent county's exercise of police power and posed a conflict with applicable constitutional prohibitions.

People v. Gentry


No. B103738


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


62 Cal. App. 4th 643; 72 Cal. Rptr. 2d 797; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 232; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2120; 98 Daily Journal DAR 2900



March 23, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted June 24, 1998 (S069817), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 4041.
Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Review Dismissed September 15, 1999 and cause remanded to Ct. App., 2d Dist., 2d Dist., Div. 6 (rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 6250.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County of Ventura. Super. Ct. No. CR 37983. Ventura County. Thomas J. Hutchins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which convicted defendant of assault with a firearm and sentenced him to four years in state prison after it barred use of defendant's prior juvenile adjudications as strikes under the Three Strikes Law, Cal. Penal Code §§ 667.5(c) and 1192.7(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of assault with a firearm and sentenced to four years in state prison after the trial court barred the use of his prior juvenile adjudications from use by the state as strikes under the Three Strikes Law, Cal. Penal Code §§ 667.5(c) and 1192.7(c). On appeal by the state, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment barring the use of his prior juvenile adjudications from use by the state as strikes, and found that the state had the right to appeal under Cal. Penal Code § 1238 because the trial court in effect struck the prior convictions. The court found that, while the trial court erred in finding that the prior adjudications did not count as strikes because there was no express finding of fitness by the juvenile court, the prior adjudications did not constitute strikes for purposes of the Three Strikes Law because its clauses could only be read to require that defendant was subject to strikes only if he had been adjudged a ward of the juvenile court for an offense under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 707(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence of defendant for assault with a firearm finding that the trial court properly barred use of defendant's prior juvenile adjudications as strikes to enhance his sentence.

People v. Reed


No. F025847.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


62 Cal. App. 4th 593; 72 Cal. Rptr. 2d 615; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 238; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2141; 98 Daily Journal DAR 2908



March 23, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part I. A. and part II.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 15, 1998. Review Denied July 8, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 4489.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County. Super. Ct. No. 15746. Edward M. Lacy, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County, (California), which convicted appellant of indecent exposure with a prior conviction for the same offense, Cal. Penal Code § 314(1), and commission of a lewd and lascivious act upon a child under the age of 14 years, Cal. Penal Code § 288(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with indecent exposure with a prior conviction for the same offense, Cal. Penal Code § 314(1), and commision of a lewd and lascivious act upon a child under the age of 14 years, Cal. Penal Code § 288(a). Appellant pleaded nolo contendre to the latter charge without having been informed of a consequential limitation on parole eligibilty. Appellant hired new counsel and filed a motion to withdraw his plea which was denied by the trial court. Appellant was convicted of both crimes, and sought review. The court affirmed and held that appellant's lack of information about parole eligibility did not undermine the voluntariness of his plea, nor did counsel render constitutionally inadequate representation when he failed to inform the client about the prison sentence credit limitations in Cal. Penal Code § 2933.1. Parole eligibility was a collateral rather than a direct consequence of appellant's plea. Thus, failure to inform him of that counsequence did not constitute incompetent representation, nor did it undermine the voluntariness of his plea because under federal law such eligibility is a collateral consequence of the plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions because his attorney's failure to inform him of the collateral consequences of the his plea does not constitute incompetent representation, and defendant's lack of information about parole eligibility did not undermine the voluntariness of his plea because under federal law such eligibility is a collateral consequence of the plea.

 

474 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Kidd v. Cal.


No. C009484.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


62 Cal. App. 4th 386; 72 Cal. Rptr. 2d 758; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 226; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2057; 98 Daily Journal DAR 2789



March 20, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super.Ct.No. 334961. Ronald B. Robie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. On remand, the trial court is directed to vacate its order granting defendants' motion for judgment on the pleadings, enter an order denying defendants' motion, declare plaintiffs' rights were violated by the use of supplemental certification and that supplemental certification is void as violative of the state Constitution and statutes, enjoin defendants from using supplemental certification and fashion an equitable remedy to redress the violation of plaintiffs' constitutional and statutory rights. Plaintiffs shall recover costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicants sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which granted a judgment on the pleadings in favor of defendant agencies in plaintiffs action to challenge an affirmative action program.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff applicants were denied jobs after defendant agencies offered positions to certain minorities and women pursuant to a supplemental certification program even though plaintiffs scored higher on civil service exams. The court found that the trial court erred in granting judgment on the pleadings in favor of defendants because although defendant's use of supplemental certification had been rescinded there was no assurance that supplemental certification would not be resumed in the future, therefore plaintiffs' action was not moot. The court found that supplemental certification violated the merit principle embodied in Cal. Const. art. VII, § 1(b) and could not be justified as a byproduct of the power to set up laws relating to personnel administration. The court also found that the supplemental certification violated Cal. Const. art. I, § 31 which banned the grant of preferential treatment on the basis of race, sex, color, ethnicity, or national origin. Finally, the court rejected plaintiff's request that defendants discharge all employees hired through supplemental certification because the court had no authority to adjudicate the rights of those not party to the action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision in favor of defendant agencies because the supplement certification program violated several constitutional and statutory provisions, and even though defendants rescinded the use of the program there was no guarantee it would not be used again in the future.

People v. Bautista


H015917


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


62 Cal. App. 4th 337; 72 Cal. Rptr. 2d 752; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 219; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1973; 98 Daily Journal DAR 2758



March 19, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied June 17, 1998 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 4001. Certiorari Denied January 11, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 306.


PRIOR HISTORY: Santa Clara County Superior Court. Santa Clara County. Super.Ct.No. 187167. Hon. Paul R. Teilh, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Santa Clara County Superior Court, Santa Clara County (California), which convicted him of possession of methamphetamine, Cal. Health & Safety Code §11377(a), and using or being under the influence of methamphetamine, Cal. Health & Safety Code §11550(a).


OVERVIEW: During defendant's trial for possession of methamphetamine, Cal. Health & Safety Code §11377(a), and using or being under the influence of methamphetamine, Cal. Health & Safety Code §11550 (a), the trial court instructed the jury that a conviction for the latter crime could be based on proof showing that defendant's use of methamphetamine occurred "on or about" the date alleged in the information. Defendant was convicted of both crimes, and sought review. The court affirmed the convictions and held that § 11550(a) did not require a showing that defendant's use occurred immediately prior to his arrest. Just as § 11550(a) did not tie the act of using the controlled substance to the danger of addiction, it likewise did not impose any limitations according to the amount of time that has elapsed between the act and the arrest. The only temporal restriction on a prosecution for an act of using proscribed drugs in violation of § 11550(a) is the one-year statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for possession of methamphetamine and using or being under the influence of methamphetamine because the trial court accurately stated, in a supplementary jury instruction, that a conviction could be based on proof showing that defendant's use of methamphetamine occurred "on or about" the date alleged in the information.

Yee v. Mobilehome Park Rental Review Bd.


No. D026324.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


62 Cal. App. 4th 1409; 73 Cal. Rptr. 2d 227; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 312; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2699; 98 Daily Journal DAR 3694



March 18, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published April 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County, Super. Ct. No. N62671. Lisa Guy-Schall, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Each party is to bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant park owners challenged the decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which refused to award them damages for the lost profits during the period of time when the trial court only permitted them to raise the rent on their property by $ 40.


OVERVIEW: Two years after appellant park owners purchased two mobile home parks, a rent control initiative ordinance was passed. Appellant filed a lawsuit contending that the ordinance constituted an illegal taking, however, the trial court held that the ordinance did not constitute a taking. The Texas Supreme Court affirmed the trial court's decision. Appellants also filed a rent increase application with respondent mobile home park rental review board and respondent agreed to a $ 27.50 increase. On appeal, the court held that the evidence did not adequately support respondent's decision. On remand, respondent increased the rent to $ 40. Appellant again challenged respondent's decision and the court once again remanded the case, this time setting the rental increase at $ 96.96. Appellant then challenged the trial court court's refusal to award them damages for the "lost profits" during the period when they were only permitted a $ 40 increase. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision, holding that they were not entitled to damages under Cal. Gov't Code § 820.2, because respondent was not liable for injuries resulting from the trial court's exercises of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision denying appellant park owners' request for lost profits for the period of time that they were only allowed a $ 40 increase, an amount set by the trial court. The court held that appellants' were not entitled to damages, because respondent mobile home park rental review board was not liable for injuries resulting from the trial court's exercises of discretion.

People v. Evans


No. F027371.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


62 Cal. App. 4th 186; 72 Cal. Rptr. 2d 543; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 213; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1933; 98 Daily Journal DAR 2668



March 17, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts 2, 3, and 4 of the Discussion.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied June 17, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 3988.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kings County. Super. Ct. No. 875. Louis F. Bissig, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the Superior Court of Kings County (California) for driving under the influence in violation of Cal. Veh. Code §§ 23152(a) and (b), and other related offenses, arguing that the trial court committed error in not charging the jury not to draw inferences by his not testifying.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving under the influence in violation of Cal. Veh. Code §§ 23152(a) and (b), driving with a blood-alcohol concentration of 0.08 percent or more in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 23175, having suffered three prior convictions for driving under the influence within the past seven years in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 31, giving false information to a peace officer, driving on a license suspended for driving under the influence in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 14601.2(a), and having three prior convictions for that offense within the past five years. Appellant challenged his conviction, contending the trial court committed error in failing to give a jury instruction that explained his right not to testify and cautioned jurors not to draw inferences. The court affirmed appellant's convictions. The trial court committed error in failing to give the requested instruction. However, after reviewing extensive case law the court concluded that the error was subject to harmless error analysis. The error was harmless, so appellant was properly convicted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving under the influence and other offenses. Although the trial court committed error in failing to give appellant's requested jury charge that explained his right not to testify and cautioned jurors not to draw inferences, the error was harmless so appellant was properly convicted.

Milagra Ridge Partners v. City of Pacifica


No. A076279.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


62 Cal. App. 4th 108; 72 Cal. Rptr. 2d 394; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 205; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1873; 98 Daily Journal DAR 2676



March 13, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 27, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 3507.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo Superior County. Super. Ct. No. 393831. Judith W. Kozloski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Costs to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged the decision of the Superior Court of San Mateo Superior County (California), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellee city in appellant's action for inverse condemnation, declaratory relief, and writ of mandate.


OVERVIEW: Summary judgment was granted to appellee city in appellant landowner's action against appellee for inverse condemnation, declaratory relief, and writ of mandate. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in concluding appellee was entitled to judgment as a matter of law because the action was not ripe for adjudication. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that appellant's taking claim was not ripe for adjudication. The court held that because appellant did not submit an application to develop the property under the existing zoning, the court had no way of determining how appellee would react to any development proposal. The court held that whether existing regulations would prevent an economically viable use of appellee's property was dependent on appellee's final action on a proposal to develop. The court rejected appellant's contention that further applications to develop the property would be futile, holding that appellee's plan did not preclude all development and appellant was free to propose a development that conformed to the existing general plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellee city in appellant landowner's action for inverse condemnation, declaratory relief, and writ of mandate because the action was not ripe for adjudication and appellant's contention that further applications to develop the property would be futile was without merit.

 

479 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. James


No. E019765.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


62 Cal. App. 4th 244; 74 Cal. Rptr. 2d 7; 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 201; 98 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1845; 98 Daily Journal DAR 2567



March 12, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts I.C. and IV.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified March 30, 1998. Review Denied June 10, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 3812.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Superior Court of Riverside County. Super.Ct.No. CR-66667. W. Charles Morgan, Judge.

Original Opinion Previously Reported at: 72 Cal. Rptr. 2d 342.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of her conviction by the Superior Court of Riverside County (California) for second degree murder, manufacture of methamphetamine, and conspiracy to manufacture methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was manufacturing methamphetamine, and a fire occurred which killed her children. Appellant was convicted by a jury of second degree murder, manufacturing methamphetamine, and conspiracy to manufacture methamphetamine. The appellate court affirmed the convictions. The appellate court concluded that the manufacture of methamphetamine was an inherently dangerous felony for purposes of the second degree felony-murder rule. In reaching its conclusion the court examined the processes used in the manufacturing of methamphetamine and noted the hazardous materials used and potential fires that could occur. Cases were noted where warrantless searches of places suspected to contain methamphetamine labs were permitted due to the exigent circumstance of immediate danger. Furthermore, the determination that manufacturing methamphetamine was inherently dangerous was a matter of law and it was proper for the trial court to so instruct the jury. Finally, the determination that manufacture of methamphetamine was an inherently dangerous felony did not violate due process as the holding was not unexpected or unforeseeable.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed appellants' convictions for second degree murder, manufacturing methamphetamine, and conspiracy to manufacture methamphetamine. The manufacture of methamphetamine was an inherently dangerous felony for purposes of the second degree felony-murder rule, and the application of the rule did not violate due process. The evidence was also sufficient for the jury to find that appellant acted with implied malice.
