Lowe v. City of Commerce


No. B104511.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


59 Cal. App. 4th 1075; 69 Cal. Rptr. 2d 356; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 1010; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9202; 97 Daily Journal DAR 14804



November 6, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of This Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published, December 8, 1997. Rehearing Denied November 26, 1997. Review Denied February 3, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 521.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BS038045. Robert O' Brien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment appealed from is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant casino patron challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) denying appellant's writ for mandate. Appellant was excluded from respondent casino under a local ordinance prohibiting certain conduct.


OVERVIEW: Appellant casino patron was banned from respondent casino by respondent city under a municipal ordinance permitting removal of persons who are boisterous, offensive to others, or if removed on more than one occasion, persons whose presence is inimical to the casino's interests. Appellant was removed after respondent casino's employees noted that he promoted his business to casino customers, used private casino facilities without permission, and sexually harassed a casino employee. The city's hearing board denied appellant's challenge to the exclusion and the trial court denied his writ for mandate. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that the ordinance was constitutionally certain, not preempted by state law, and that the city's exclusion order was supported by substantial evidence. The court noted that the ordinance furthered the substantial government interest of protecting the attending public's safety and welfare, and that the California legislature expressly intended to exercise concurrent jurisdiction with local governments regarding gaming regulations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment against appellant casino patron; finding that a local ordinance relied upon by respondents, casino and city, to exclude appellant was constitutional, and that substantial evidence supported the exclusion.

 

533 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Spry


No. F024542, No. F027268.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


58 Cal. App. 4th 1345; 68 Cal. Rptr. 2d 691; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 898; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8496



November 4, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts I., III., and IV. of the Discussion.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County. Super. Ct. No. 518875-0. Gary S. Austin, Judge. ORIGINAL PROCEEDING; petition for writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the matter remanded to the trial court for further appropriate proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for possession of heroin from the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), arguing that the trial court improperly shifted the burden of proof from the prosecution to the defense and failed to state the applicable burden of proving the elements of the defense of lawful possession of heroin for the purpose of disposal.


OVERVIEW: At his trial on the charge of possession of heroin, appellant relied on the defense of lawful possession for the limited purpose of disposal, and that such temporary possession was not unlawful. The trial court convicted appellant as charged and appellant sought review. On review, appellant argued the instruction improperly shifted the burden of proof from the prosecution to the defense and failed to state the applicable burden of proving the elements of the defense of lawful possession of heroin for the purpose of disposal. The court reversed the conviction and remanded, concluding that the jury was not correctly instructed as to the magnitude of appellant's burden of proving his affirmative defense. Although the jury was correctly instructed as to the elements of the defense, the instructions were incomplete in their failure to identify which party had the burden of meeting the four conditions and the level of the burden required to establish the conditions. Given the state of the evidence and the deficiencies in the instruction, the court concluded that the error was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, and thus, reversal of the conviction was required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for possession of heroin and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings. The trial court's failure to identify which party had the burden of proving the affirmative defense of lawful possession of heroin for the purpose of disposal was not harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt.

 

534 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Aguilar


No. A075729.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


58 Cal. App. 4th 1196; 68 Cal. Rptr. 2d 619; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 886; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8354; 97 Daily Journal DAR 13491



October 30, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review Denied February 18, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 944.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Marin County. Super. Ct. No. SC078917A. John A. Sutro, Judge. *


* Judge of the Marin Municipal Court, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, section 6 of the California Constitution.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Marin County (California), convicting him of the crime of torture under Cal. Penal Code § 206 on the grounds of an unconstitutionally vague statute and improper jury instructions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of the crime of torture under Cal. Penal Code § 206. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed finding that the terms "cruel or extreme pain and suffering," "any sadistic purpose," and "torture" were not unconstitutionally vague. The court found that "cruel pain" was equivalent to "extreme" or "severe" pain which comported with the common dictionary definition of "cruel," and that the common meaning of "sadistic purpose" was sufficiently definite. Section 206 expressly defined the crime of torture as requiring the intent to inflict extreme pain which was consistent with case law. The trial court did not err in failing to give jury instructions that the crime of torture included elements of premeditation and prolonged pain, because they were not elements of the crime of torture under § 206. The court found that the jury instruction which defined "reasonable doubt" in terms of an "abiding conviction" without reference to the terms "moral evidence" and "moral certainty" did not violate appellant's due process rights, because the omitted terms would add nothing to a jury's understanding of reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction holding that the terms challenged by appellant were sufficiently clear and the jury charges included the elements of the crime charged and properly omitted reference to "moral certainty" in the definition of "reasonable doubt."

 

535 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Bamba


No. A073612.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


58 Cal. App. 4th 1113; 68 Cal. Rptr. 2d 450; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 884; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8357; 97 Daily Journal DAR 13453



October 29, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part II C. and part II D.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County. Super. Ct. No. SC36703. Clarence B. Knight, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is vacated and this matter is remanded to the trial court for the limited purpose of allowing the trial court to exercise its discretion pursuant to Romero. "If, on remand, the trial court . . . decides to exercise its discretion to strike [one or both of] the prior felony conviction allegations in furtherance of justice . . ., the court must set forth the reasons for that decision in strict compliance with section 1385(a). Any such decision will be reviewable for abuse of discretion according to the procedures generally applicable to such decisions." (Romero, supra, 13 Cal. 4th at p. 532.) In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for assault with a deadly weapon, Cal. Penal Code § 245(a)(1), felony false imprisonment, Cal. Penal Code §§ 236 and 237, and possessing methamphetamine, Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11377(a) after a jury trial in the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California). In the published portion of the opinion, the court addressed claims § 236 was vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for assault with a deadly weapon, Cal. Penal Code § 245(a)(1), felony false imprisonment, Cal. Penal Code §§ 236 and 237, and possessing methamphetamine, Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11377(a) after a jury trial. In the published portion of the opinion, the court addressed appellant's claims that the felony false imprisonment statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The court explained that citizens were required to apprise themselves not only of statutory language, but also of legislative history and subsequent judicial construction. Furthermore, the personal liberty addressed in the statute related to the freedom from physical restraint, and the context gave the facially standardless phrase a constitutionally sufficient concreteness. Rejecting appellant's argument that the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad in that it could have prohibited speech protected by U.S. Const. amend. I, the court noted appellant offered no incident. Finally, the court decided the evidence, that appellant refused to stop his van so victim could get off, was sufficient to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for felony false imprisonment, assault with a deadly weapon, and possessing methamphetamine. In the published portion of the opinion, it addressed the challenges to the false imprisonment conviction. It vacated the judgment and remanded the matter to the trial court for the limited purpose of resentencing because the trial court committed instructional error.

People v. Vong


No. B098599.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


58 Cal. App. 4th 1063; 68 Cal. Rptr. 2d 436; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 873; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8320; 97 Daily Journal DAR 13377



October 28, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts enclosed by brackets [FACTUAL and PROCEDURAL BACKGROUND, and DISCUSSION parts 1. through 5.].


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied February 3, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 509.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. KA028257. Wade Olsen, Temporary Judge. **


** Pursuant to Cal. Const., art. VI, § 21.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction is affirmed. The case is remanded to the trial court for hearing on a motion to dismiss one or more of the prior convictions alleged for the purpose of sentence enhancement under the Three Strikes law. If the motion to dismiss a strike is granted, then the court shall resentence and impose such new and modified sentence as is appropriate with the prior conviction dismissed. If the motion to dismiss a strike is denied, then the sentence previously imposed shall remain in force.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his sentence, imposed by the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California), for his conviction of possession of cocaine, enhanced under the three strikes sentencing law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of possession of cocaine. The trial court did not entertain appellant's motion to dismiss one or more of the "strikes" under the three strikes sentencing law, which arose from appellant's two prior robbery convictions. The trial court stated that it lacked power to dismiss allegations of prior serious felony convictions and enhanced appellant's sentence accordingly. The court held that Cal. Penal Code § 1385 conferred upon trial courts the discretionary power to dismiss allegations of prior felony convictions which otherwise would require substantial sentence enhancements under the three strikes law. Therefore, the court remanded the case for the trial court to entertain appellant's motion to dismiss one or more strikes. The court held that, on remand, the trial court must conduct a hearing on appellant's motion, with appellant present and represented by counsel.


OUTCOME: The court remanded appellant's sentence for his conviction of possession of cocaine for the trial court to entertain appellant's motion to dismiss one or more of the strikes against him because the trial court had the power to entertain such a motion.

 

537 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Yoshioka v. Superior Court


No. B110759.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


58 Cal. App. 4th 972; 68 Cal. Rptr. 2d 553; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 861; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8267; 97 Daily Journal DAR 13331



October 27, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 18, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (application for a writ of mandate/prohibition) Super. Ct. No. KC020037. Theodore D. Piatt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The petition for a writ of mandate is denied. Real parties in interest are awarded costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner uninsured motorist applied for a writ of mandate from the judgment of the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California), which granted respondent tortfeasors' motion in limine to exclude all evidence of general damages and to bar all jury instructions on that issue pursuant to Proposition 213, which created Cal. Civ. Code § 3333.4. Petitioner maintained that Proposition 213 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner uninsured motorist sought to recover non-economic damages from respondent tortfeasors, the real parties in interest. After the accident, an initiative, creating Cal. Civ. Code § 3333.4, was passed prohibiting uninsured motorists and drunk drivers from collecting non-economic damages in actions arising out of the use or operation of a motor vehicle. The trial court granted respondents' motion in limine to exclude all evidence of general damages and to bar all jury instructions on that issue. Petitioner sought a writ of mandate and challenged the initiative's constitutionality. On review, the court denied the petition for a writ of mandate. Applying the initiative retroactively did not violate petitioner's constitutional right to due process and, under the rational relationship test, did not violate his rights to equal protection. The uninsured motorist classification was rationally related to the electorate's interests in restoring balance to the justice system and in reducing costs of auto insurance. The initiative did not violate the single-subject rule because its primary objective was to limit recovery of non-economic damages for drivers who broke the law.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner uninsured motorist's request for a writ of mandate from the order, which granted the motion in limine filed by respondent tortfeasors, the real parties in interest, and which excluded all evidence of general damages and barred all jury instructions on that issue. The court upheld the constitutionality of the retroactive application of the initiative prohibiting uninsured motorists from collecting non-economic damages.

 

538 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Lyon Metal Prods. v. State Bd. of Equalization


No. A076008.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


58 Cal. App. 4th 906; 68 Cal. Rptr. 2d 285; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 860; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8221; 97 Daily Journal DAR 13284



October 24, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review Denied January 14, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 62. Cert. Denied June 8, 1998, 66 U.S.L. Week 3782.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of San Francisco County. No. 971950. Donna J. Hitchens, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is reversed, and the matter is remanded with instructions to enter judgment in favor of the Board.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant California State Board of Equalization challenged the order of the Superior Court of San Francisco County (California), which held that California's state sales tax under Cal. Rev. & Tax Code § 6007 was invalid to the extent it applied to drop shipments of goods from California wholesalers directly to retail customers inside the state.


OVERVIEW: Respondent wholesaler brought an action against appellant California State Department of Equalization that alleged the drop shipment rule, codified by Cal. Rev. & Tax Code § 6007, was invalid on both statutory and constitutional grounds. Respondent had shipped goods subject to the retail sales tax from respondent's in-state warehouse directly to in-state retail customers and made the delivery at the request of an out-of-state retailer, who bought the goods at wholesale from respondent and then resold them to the in-state customer. The trial court held that § 6007 was invalid as a burden on interstate commerce to the extent that it applied to drop shipments of goods from in-state wholesalers directly to in-state retail customers. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the case with instructions to enter judgment in favor of appellant. The court determined the tax was valid because it met a four part test that showed that (1) the tax applied to activity that had a substantial nexus to the state; (2) it was fairly apportioned; (3) it was not imposed in a discriminatory way on interstate commerce only; and (4) it was fairly related to services provided in the state.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the matter was remanded with instructions to enter judgment in favor of appellant California State Board of Equalization. The court concluded that drop shipments by respondent wholesaler, directly to in-state consumers on behalf of an out-of-state retailer, were validly subject to the state's retail sales tax which was not unconstitutional discriminatory to out-of-state retailers.

National Paint & Coatings Assn. v. State of California


No. B108082.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


58 Cal. App. 4th 753; 68 Cal. Rptr. 2d 360; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 845; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8179; 97 Daily Journal DAR 13181



October 22, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review Denied January 14, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 140.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of dismissal of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC 149790. Emilie H. Elias, Temporary Judge. *


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed. Respondent shall recover its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant paint manufacturer associations challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which dismissed appellants' complaint that private enforcement provisions of the Safe Drinking Water and Toxic Enforcement Act of 1986, Cal. Health & Safety Code §§ 25249.5- 25249.13, violated the California and United States Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant paint manufacturer associations filed an action alleging that private enforcement provisions of the Safe Drinking Water and Toxic Enforcement Act of 1986 (Act), Cal. Health & Safety Code §§ 25249.5- 25249.13, violated the separation of powers doctrine under the California Constitution, and the due process clauses of the California and United States Constitutions. The trial court dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the Act's grant of standing to sue to any person in the public interest was not unconstitutional because the federal constitutional requirement that a party must make out a case and controversy to have standing was not present under the California Constitution. The court held that appellants had not alleged facts sufficient to show the private enforcement provisions of the Act violated the constitutional separation of powers doctrine. The court also held that the private enforcement provisions did not violate due process by entrusting prosecutorial power to private citizens with a financial interest in successful prosecution of the claim because private enforcement complements public enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant paint manufacturer associations' complaint, holding that the right to sue granted to any person in the public interest under the Safe Drinking Water and Toxic Enforcement Act of 1986 (Act) did not violate the California Constitution because the Constitution did not contain a case or controversy requirement and that the Act did not violate the federal and state constitutional due process clauses.

People v. Mendez


E017322


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


58 Cal. App. 4th 773; 68 Cal. Rptr. 2d 525; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 847; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8188; 97 Daily Journal DAR 13203



October 22, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review Granted February 3, 1998 (S066175), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 486.
Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Court.
Supreme Court of California disposition reported at: 19 Cal. 4th 1084.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. Super.Ct.No. FBA-2599. Walter L. Blackwell III and Rufus L. Yent, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, who pled guilty to second degree murder under a plea bargain, contested the judgment from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), contending that the trial court erred in calculating presentence custody credits, and by failing to hold a hearing into whether he was competent, or alternatively that Cal. Penal Code § 1372 (c) was unconstitutionally vague as to the hearing.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a plea bargain, appellant plead guilty, and then appealed as to whether or not a hearing as to his competency was required. The appellate court held that since his appeal went to the validity of his guilty plea, and he failed to request a certificate of probable cause within 60 days after the judgment was rendered, his appeal was barred. Further, his appeal was barred because he failed to raise his objection in the trial court. The appellate court commented that it saw no relevant distinction between requesting a certificate of probable cause belatedly and failing to request one at all. Finally, the fact that the record had been prepared and certified could not be construed as an implied certificate of probable cause. The appellate court held that the appeal in its entirety must be dismissed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's action on appeal was barred where he sought to attack his guilty plea, but failed to object at trial or to timely request a certificate of probable cause.

Forty-Niner Truck Plaza v. Union Oil Co.


No. C021946.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


58 Cal. App. 4th 1261; 68 Cal. Rptr. 2d 532; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 874; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8322; 97 Daily Journal DAR 13405



October 22, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] Opinion certified for partial publication. 1 


1 Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts 1.d., 1.e., 2., 3., 4., 5., 6., 7., 8., 9., and 10.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied February 18, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 1038.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgment of the Superior Court of the County of Sacramento. Super. Ct. No. CV531830. Horace Cecchettini, Judge.



DISPOSITION: That part of the judgment granting a nonsuit to National and Clipper on the plaintiffs' civil conspiracy count is reversed. In all other respects, the judgment and postjudgment orders are affirmed. Each party shall pay its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation and appellant oil company sought review of an order by the Superior Court of the County of Sacramento (California), that granted a new trial after a jury awarded a multimillion dollar verdict to appellant corporation for violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code 20999.25(a), but the trial court granted a new trial to appellant oil company when it found that the great weight of the evidence was against the jury's verdict.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation and appellant oil company challenged the trial court's order that granted a new trial after a multimillion-dollar award to appellant corporation because of appellant oil company's violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code 20999.25(a). Appellant corporation asserted the trial court erred in the grant of a new trial, and appellant oil company asserted the trial court erred when it denied its motion for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part and rejected appellant corporation's contention that the statute was unconstitutional, and held that it was rationally related to the legitimate state interest of ensuring greater access to service stations by the motoring public, and that the statute did not constitute a taking pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. V, and Cal. Const. art. I, § 19. The court rejected appellant oil company's assertion that the statute was preempted by the Petroleum Marketing Practices Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 2801 et seq., because the federal statute covered franchise terminations while the state statute covered sales of a franchise. The court held that a bona fide offer was based on an objective market value.


OUTCOME: A order by the trial court was affirmed in part and reversed in part because the statute that regulated the sale of service station franchises was rationally related to a legitimate state interest, because a federal statute did not preempt the state statute as they addressed two separate issues, because the statute did not constitute a taking, and because a bona fide offer was to be based on an objective standard of market value.

 

542 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Wiley v. County of San Diego


D022069


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


58 Cal. App. 4th 434; 68 Cal. Rptr. 2d 193; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 825; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8047; 97 Daily Journal DAR 12953



October 15, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Review Granted December 23, 1997 (S066034), 1997 Cal. LEXIS 8643. Respondent's Review Denied December 23, 1997, 1997 Cal. LEXIS 8643. Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Court. Supreme Court of California disposition reported at: 19 Cal. 4th 532.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. 659219. James R. Milliken and G. Dennis Adams, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a county and public defender, appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) in favor of plaintiff, a former client in a criminal case, on his legal malpractice claim. Defendants alleged that the claim was untimely under Cal. Gov't. Code §§ 91.2 and 945.4, and that the admission of plaintiff's habeas corpus transcript, and the exclusion of defendants' investigations were erroneous.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was convicted of battery in a trial in which he was defended by defendant public defender (defendant). At a habeas corpus hearing, the trial court granted the petition and found that defendant's pre-trial investigation was inadequate. Plaintiff sued defendants, the public defender and the county, for malpractice, and the trial court entered judgment for plaintiff. On appeal, the court held that although plaintiff's claim was untimely under Cal. Gov't. Code §§ 91 and 945.4, because defendants did not include the mandatory language of Cal. Gov't. Code § 911.3(a) in their letter to plaintiff rejecting his claim, under Cal. Gov't. Code § 911.3(b), defendants' waived the defense of untimeliness. Because defendant's alleged malpractice occurred before plaintiff was convicted, the trial court abused its discretion by admitting the transcript of the habeas corpus hearing that occurred after the conviction and by excluding evidence of plaintiff's polygraph results and other investigations undertaken by defendant. The court held that plaintiff was not required to prove actual innocence. Therefore, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for plaintiff, a former client, on his malpractice claim against defendants, county and public defender, and remanded the case for a new trial. Although defendants waived the defense of untimeliness by not using statutory language to reject plaintiff's claim, the trial court erroneously admitted irrelevant transcript of plaintiff's habeas corpus hearing and excluded relevant evidence of defendants' investigations.

 

543 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Banks


B098423


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


58 Cal. App. 4th 513; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 916; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 822; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8003; 97 Daily Journal DAR 12895



October 14, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied February 3, 1998 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 508.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. SA020600. Leslie W. Light, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The one-year, stayed county jail sentence imposed by the trial court is vacated and a six-month, stayed county jail sentence is hereby imposed in its place. The judgment as modified is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California) that convicted him of sale or possession of an instrument to defraud a telephone company, possession of property from which a serial number had been removed, and possession of a firearm by a felon under Cal. Penal Code §§ 502.7(b)(1), 537e(a), and 12021. Appellant challenged the constitutionality of § 502.7(b)(1) and the jury instructions.


OVERVIEW: A police officer searched appellant's car and found a handgun, a phone without a serial number on it, five phones whose electronic serial numbers (ESN) had been changed, a device for detecting ESN readers, and a device for programming ESN numbers into other phones. As a result, appellant was convicted of possession of a firearm by a felon, a device to defraud a telephone company, and property with their serial numbers removed in violation of Cal. Penal Code §§ 12921, 502.7(b)(1), and 537e(a), and sentenced to one year. On appeal, the court held that the language of § 502.7(b)(1) was easily understood. Thus, it was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The court held that the electronic removal of the ESNs was sufficient evidence to support a conviction under § 537e(a). Because appellant was not in immediate danger when the gun was found, appellant was not entitled to jury instructions as to his right to have a gun for self-defense purposes. However, because the phones were worth less than $ 400, appellant's sentence under § 537e(a)(1) was limited to six months. Therefore, the court affirmed the convictions, vacated the sentence, and imposed a six-month sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions, vacated the one-year sentence, and imposed a six-month sentence. The court held that the statute prohibiting defrauding devices was constitutional, and that appellant's possession of a gun when he was not threatened precluded instructions on self defense, but the property's low value mandated a lower sentence.

 

544 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Kaplan v. LaBarbera


No. B105716.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


58 Cal. App. 4th 175; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 903; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 811; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7917; 97 Daily Journal DAR 12715



October 7, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for partial publication. The portions of this opinion to be deleted from publication are identified as those portions between double brackets, e.g., [[/]].


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County. Super. Ct. No. CV 076779. Diane L. Levison, Temporary Judge. **


** Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Costs on appeal are awarded to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father filed an appeal from the decision of the Superior Court, San Luis Obispo County (California), which granted defendants district attorney and agencies' motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff father sued defendants district attorney and agencies. Plaintiff's complaint alleged many causes of action under state law and a federal cause of action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Defendants moved for summary judgment, which the trial court granted. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that all of plaintiff's causes of action arose from defendants' role in collecting child support from plaintiff. There was no dispute that if defendant public employees committed any of the acts alleged in the complaint, the acts were committed while prosecuting a judicial proceeding within the scope of their employment. Thus the employees were immune from liability under Cal. Gov't Code § 821.6. Plaintiff appeared to contend that the employees were not immune because their acts were ministerial in nature. The court held that the plain language of Cal. Gov't Code § 821.6 showed that prosecutorial immunity was not limited to discretionary acts. Because the public employees were immune from liability, defendants were also immune. Plaintiff failed to provide any applicable statutory exception.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that granted defendants district attorney and agencies' motion for summary judgment because defendants were immune from liability by statute.

People v. Smith


No. C012464.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


57 Cal. App. 4th 1470; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 604; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 764; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7642; 97 Daily Journal DAR 12263



September 24, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing October 23, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 867. Review Denied January 14, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 171.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of El Dorado County. Super. Ct. No. SR910043. Terrence M. Finney, Judge, J. Hilary Cook, Judge. *


* Assigned by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Superior Court of El Dorado County (California), of the offense of assault with a deadly weapon upon the person of a peace officer, Cal. Penal Code § 245(c), contending the trial court prejudicially misinstructed the jury on the mental state required for the offense.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of the offense of assault with a deadly weapon upon the person of a peace officer, Cal. Penal Code § 245 (c). The incident arose when a line of police officers blocked traffic on a highway. According to defendant he had been directed by an officer to drive his car forward; he did so and his car inadvertently struck an officer. The jury was instructed under former Cal. Jury Instructions - Criminal No. 9.00 (5th ed. 1988) that assault required a general criminal intent. The jury sent a note to the trial court regarding "intent" and the trial court read an abbreviated instruction, that defendant must intend to commit an act, the natural and probable consequence of which if successfully completed would be the application of physical force upon the person of another. The jury returned a guilty verdict. On appeal, defendant contended the trial court prejudicially misinstructed the jury on the mental state required for the offense. The court found that the abbreviated instruction directed the jury to apply an improper negligence standard to the assault element of the offense. The error was prejudicial; the court reversed thus conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction on the grounds that the trial court's abbreviated instruction directed the jury to apply a negligence standard to the assault element of the offense, but negligence did not satisfy the mental state required for conviction of assault with a deadly weapon. In the absence of this error, it was likely that defendant would have obtained a more favorable result from the jury.

 

546 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Estrada


No. B102559.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


57 Cal. App. 4th 1270; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 596; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 763; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7638; 97 Daily Journal DAR 12248



September 24, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 14, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 95.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. GA023311. Terry Lee Smerling and Thomas William Stoever, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of first degree burglary and forcible rape and sentenced him under Cal. Penal Code § 667.61, California's one strike law.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of first degree burglary under Cal. Penal Code § 460(a) and forcible rape under Cal. Penal Code § 261(a)(2) and sentenced appellant to 25 years to life under the one strike law, Cal. Penal Code § 667.61(a),(d). The court affirmed, finding that the trial court erred in not instructing the jury what facts it must find for purposes of the special sentencing allegations under Cal. Penal Code § 667.61, but the error was harmless because the record did not demonstrate a reasonable probability that the jury would have found that appellant committed burglary to commit nonforcible rather than forcible rape. The trial court did not err in failing to strike the burglary allegation for purposes of sentencing under § 667.61 because § 667.61 clearly prohibited striking the allegation. The court applied a four-prong test examining the nature of the offender and the case and comparing punishment for his offense with punishments for other offenses that were as serious or more serious than appellant's offense in California and other jurisdictions and found that appellant's sentence did not constitute cruel or unusual punishment under the facts of the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, finding that any error committed by the trial court was harmless, the trial court had no discretion to strike the burglary allegation as appellant desired, and appellant's punishment was not cruel or unusual punishment under the facts.

Leone v. Medical Board


B103344, B101297


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


57 Cal. App. 4th 1240; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 689; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 761; 97 Daily Journal DAR 12258; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7635



September 24, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted December 23, 1997 (S065485), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 8640.
Reprinted without change in the January 2000 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Court.
Supreme Court of California Opinion of April 3, 2000, Reported at: 22 Cal. 4th 660.


PRIOR HISTORY: MOTIONS to dismiss appeals from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BS035371. Super. Ct. No. BS036241. Robert H. O'Brien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The motions to dismiss the appeals are hereby denied. Our orders of October 25, 1996, and March 5, 1997, relieving the parties of their obligations to file briefs on the merits of the respective appeals, are to remain in effect pending finality of this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent medical board filed a motion to dismiss appellant doctors' petitions seeking review of the judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 2337, which provided that appellate review of physician disciplinary actions would be done through the process of a writ petition.


OVERVIEW: Respondent medical board revoked the licenses of appellant doctors and the trial court denied each appellant's request for administrative mandamus to overturn the respondent's decisions. Appellants sought review, and respondents filed a motion to dismiss under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 2337 which mandated that appellate review would be done solely through the process of a writ petition. Under § 2337, the appellate court was not required to place the case on calendar for oral argument or to file a written decision explaining its analysis and resolution of the claims of error absent issuance of an alternate writ or an order to show cause. The court denied the respondent's motion to dismiss holding that § 2337 violated the constitutional jurisdiction vested in the court in all matters over which the trial court had original jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court denied respondent medical board's motions to dismiss appellant doctors' petitions finding that the legislation which changed the appellate review process for physician disciplinary actions unconstitutionally infringed on the appellate jurisdiction vested in the court.

Lambert v. City and County of San Francisco


A076116


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


57 Cal. App. 4th 1172; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 562; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 758; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7589; 97 Daily Journal DAR 12189



September 23, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted January 14, 1998 (S065446), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 34.
Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Court.
Review Dismissed July 28, 1999 and cause remanded to Ct. App., 1st Dist., Div. 1 (rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct., Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 5006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court City and County of San Francisco. San Francisco County Super. Ct. No. 963368. Honorable William Cahill.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The San Francisco Planning Commission, applying the amended San Francisco Planning Code, denied plaintiff hotel owner's application for a conditional use permit to convert 24 residential units to tourist use. Plaintiff sought judicial review and the Superior Court City and County of San Francisco (California) granted summary judgment to defendant City and County of San Francisco. Plaintiff then appealed.


OVERVIEW: The San Francisco Planning Commission denied plaintiff hotel owner's application for a conditional use permit to convert 24 residential units to tourist use based on the San Francisco Planning Code. The superior court granted defendant city and county of San Francisco summary judgment. The court of appeal affirmed. The amendment of the planning code limiting the ability of landowners to convert residential hotel units to tourist units substantially furthered legitimate interests in ensuring the existence of affordable residential housing, did so by a means reasonably and directly related to its goals, and did not deprive hotel owners of the economically viable use of their property. It followed that neither the restriction on development resulting from the commission's refusal to grant the conditional use permit sought by plaintiff nor the amendment of the Planning Code was a taking in violation of U.S. Const. amend. V or Cal. Const. art. I, § 19. As a general rule, no taking resulted from the down-zoning of property in such a manner as to limit its potential for development. Substantial evidence supported the commission's findings and its decision to deny the permit.


OUTCOME: The court found that the amendments to San Francisco's Planning Code met constitutional requirements and did not effectuate a taking on affected hotel owners such as plaintiff. The decision to deny plaintiff a conditional use permit to alter his hotel also did not effect a taking. Substantial evidence supported the planning commission's findings that the denial would further legitimate governmental interests.

Bd. of Admin. v. Wilson


No. C021663.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


57 Cal. App. 4th 967; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 477; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 740; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7468; 97 Daily Journal DAR 12031



September 18, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. ** 


** Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part II of the Discussion.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. CV377815. John R. Lewis, Judge. **


** Judge of the Sacramento Municioal Court, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, section of the California Constitution.



DISPOSITION: The order denying the motion for attorney's fees is affirmed. The cross-appeal is dismissed as moot. Defendant shall recover his costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school board sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which denied attorney's fees in a suit for impairment of contract against appellee governor under California's private attorney general statute, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1021.5 and the federal Civil Rights Attorney's Fees Awards Act of 1976, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988.


OVERVIEW: Appellant school board filed an impairment of contract action against respondent governor and did not plead or argue violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Postjudgment, appellant sought to recover attorney's fees stating they enforced constitutional rights of members and beneficiaries under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 and Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1021. The trial court entered judgment in favor of school board stating on the impairment of contracts claim but denied attorney's fees and respondent cross-appealed the finding that the amount of fees and costs sought was reasonable. The court held that under state statute the denial of attorney's fees was proper where large sums would have inured to the direct benefit of appellant's members, making an award under a private attorney general theory inappropriate. The court held that a trial court retains discretion under § 1988 to deny attorney's fees where a postjudgment motion would have unfairly surprised the affected party where party did not plead or argue civil rights violations during trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the motion for attorney's fees because denial was proper where postjudgment assertion of a civil rights claim surprised and prejudiced the defendants when no civil rights claim was argued during trial. Fees under state statute were denied because large sums would have inured to the direct benefit of the appellant's members making an award of fees under a private attorney general theory inappropriate.

 

550 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Suter v. City of Lafayette


No. A073743.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


57 Cal. App. 4th 1109; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 420; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 729; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7426; 97 Daily Journal DAR 11940



September 16, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied December 10, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 8365.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court Contra Costa County. Super. Ct. No. C-94-05444. James R. Trembath, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed insofar as it holds that Lafayette Municipal Code section 8-609 is not preempted by state law. In all other respects the judgment is affirmed. The matter is remanded to the trial court to determine whether appellants are entitled to attorney fees, and, if so, to award them reasonable fees for successfully challenging section 8-609. Each party will bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant gun seller's challenged the decision of the Superior Court Contra Costa County (California), which sustained a demurrer to appellants' complaint that alleged that an ordinance enacted by respondent city was preempted by state law without leave to amend, and dismissed the action.


OVERVIEW: Respondent city enacted an ordinance requiring persons seeking to sell, transfer or lease weapons to obtain land use permits and police permits in addition to the licenses already required by state and federal law. Appellant gun sellers contended that the ordinance was preempted by state law. The trial court sustained a demurrer to appellants' complaint without leave to amend, and entered judgment dismissing the action in its entirety. The court held that local governments were not generally excluded by state law from imposing additional licensing requirements on firearm dealers. Therefore, the court found that with one exception, the specific provisions at issue here did not conflict with, duplicate, or enter into a field fully occupied by state law and were not, therefore, preempted. However, the court held that the section which required dealers to employ two of three alternatives for the storage of weapons was preempted by state law since it attempted to enter into a field of regulation from which the state had implicitly excluded all other regulatory authority.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court in so far as it applied to the section which required dealers to employ two of three alternatives for the storage of weapons because this section was preempted by state law because it attempted to enter into a field of regulation from which the state had implicitly excluded all other regulatory authority. However, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court on all remaining issues.

Ashurst v. Monterey Peninsula Unified Sch. Dist.


H016156


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


57 Cal. App. 4th 665; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 316; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 712; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7253; 97 Daily Journal DAR 11709



September 9, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied December 10, 1997 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 8510.


PRIOR HISTORY: Monterey County Superior Court. Monterey County. Super. Ct. No. M34919. The Honorable Richard M. Silver.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of an order from the Monterey County Superior Court (California), which denied his petition for a writ of administrative mandate directing respondent school district to reinstate him.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee was a janitor for respondent school district. He engaged in sexual intercourse with a 15-year-old student. A few years later, when respondent learned of the incident, respondent recommended appellant's dismissal. After an evidentiary hearing, the hearing officer upheld the recommendation. Appellant filed a petition for writ of administrative mandate directing respondent to reinstate him, which the trial court denied. Upon review, the court affirmed, finding that appellant's declaration against interest that he engaged in sexual intercourse with a minor student was not inadmissible hearsay and that respondent was not barred by the statute of limitations in Cal. Educ. Code § 45113. The court found that appellant's statement to a police officer after being given his Miranda warnings was not hearsay, but that it qualified as an admission and a confession, and thus, was admissible against appellant. The court concluded that the limitations period in § 45113 was subject to the delayed discovery rule; thus, it was tolled until respondent discovered that a criminal act had taken place against one of its students.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant employee's writ of administrative mandate, finding that his statement to a police officer after being given his Miranda warnings was an admission and a confession rather than hearsay. The court also concluded that the statute of limitations was subject to the delayed discovery rule, and thus, it was tolled until respondent school district had discovered a criminal act had taken place against its student.

 

552 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Econ. Empowerment Found. v. Quackenbush


No. A072693.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


57 Cal. App. 4th 677; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 323; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 714; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7300; 97 Daily Journal DAR 11726



September 9, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 9, 1997. Review Denied December 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 8531.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court San Francisco County. San Francisco County Super. Ct. No. 970772. Honorable William Cahill.



DISPOSITION: The order of dismissal is affirmed with costs to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff consumer representative sought review of an order of the Superior Court of San Francisco County (California), which dismissed its complaint against defendant insurance commissioner and insurer, the real party in interest. Plaintiff sought an award, payable by insurer, of fees and expenses plaintiff incurred in proceedings before the Department of Insurance on insurer's applications for certain insurance rate increases.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff consumer representative sought review of an order dismissing its complaint against defendant insurance commission and real party in interest insurer. Plaintiff sought an award of fees and expenses it incurred in proceedings before the Department of Insurance (department) regarding insurer's applications for insurance rate increases. Pursuant to the court's interpretation of Cal. Ins. Code § 1861.10, defendant had exclusive original jurisdiction over fees in proceedings which were commenced in the department for a determination by defendant on the merits. Because plaintiff's sole remedy under the statute was to seek an award from defendant, the issue became whether defendant's alleged bias excused plaintiff's admitted failure to pursue that administrative remedy. The court found that the futility exception did not apply because defendant had established procedures for the allowance of fees, plaintiff had not requested such an award, and defendant had taken no position on the merits of such a request. Accordingly, because plaintiff failed to exhaust its administrative remedies and the futility exception did not apply, the dismissal was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff consumer representative's complaint because plaintiff's claim for fees was not originally cognizable in court under the relevant provision of the insurance code, and the futility exception did not apply to plaintiff's claim. Thus, plaintiff was required to exhaust its administrative remedy before pursuing a court action on that claim.

People v. Putney


A075990


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


57 Cal. App. 4th 739; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 283; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 705; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7179; 97 Daily Journal DAR 11549



September 4, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing of October 2, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 799. Review Granted December 23, 1997 (S065144), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 8637.
Reprinted without change in the January 2000 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Review Dismissed February 16, 2000 and cause remanded to the Ct. App., 1st Dist., Div. 5 (rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 2000 Cal. LEXIS 996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sonoma County. Super. Ct. No. SCR7906. R. Bryan Jamar, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court of Sonoma County (California), which committed him to the custody of the California State Department of Mental Health for two years under California's Sexually Violent Predator Act, Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had several convictions for rape and sexual assault. Prior to his release from prison, the district attorney filed a petition for defendant's commitment under the California Sexually Violent Predator Act (Act), Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq. The trial court granted the petition and committed appellant to the custody of the State Department of Mental Health for two years. Upon review, the court affirmed, finding that the 1996 amendments to the Act were not given retroactive application and the application of the amendments did not deprive defendant of any vested right in the commitment scheme, and thus, the trial court's decision was supported by substantial evidence. The court found that the Act did not violate state and federal constitutional ex post facto prohibitions because it had no punitive intent, limited confinement to a small segment of dangerous individuals, segregated confined persons from the prison population, afforded them the same status as other civilly committed persons, recommended treatment if possible, and permitted release upon a showing that the individual was no longer dangerous or mentally impaired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's commitment, finding that the amendments to the California Sexually Violent Predator Act were not given retroactive application and that the act did not violate constitutional ex post facto principles because it provided for a civil commitment and defendant could be released upon a showing that he was no longer dangerous or mentally ill.

Barer v. County of Riverside


No. E018126.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


57 Cal. App. 4th 558; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 241; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 700; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7115; 97 Daily Journal DAR 11441



September 2, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 29, 1997. Review Denied November 25, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 8292.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County. Super.Ct.No. I-81844. Arthur S. Block, Judge. * 


* Judge of the Municipal Court for the Desert Judicial District, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to art. VI, § 6 of the California Constitution.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, trustee for plaintiff property owner, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which entered summary judgment in favor of respondent county and respondent county tax collector in an action for declaratory relief to quiet title on land that was the subject of recorded tax liens.


OVERVIEW: Respondent county and respondent county tax assessor recorded a certificate of lien for unpaid taxes against the disputed property, which was placed on the secured roll and became a lien on the possessory interest pursuant to Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 2190.2. A senior lienholder conducted a nonjudicial foreclosure sale of the property but did not pay the delinquent taxes. The possessory interest of the property was subsequently sold to plaintiff property owner. Appellant, trustee for plaintiff, brought an action for declaratory relief to quiet title, contending that the tax liens were eliminated because he was a bona fide purchaser without knowledge of the liens. The court affirmed the summary judgment entered in favor of respondents because ad valorem tax liens on a possessory interest were not eliminated by a nonjudicial foreclosure sale by a senior lienholder. The taxes had priority over all other liens on the property regardless of the time of their creation under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 2192.1. Additionally, the court held that plaintiff was a bona fide purchaser and charged with constructive notice because the taxes were locatable by a search of the proper indexes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment entered in favor of respondent county and respondent county tax collector in an action brought by appellant trustee for plaintiff property owner because recorded tax liens had priority over all other liens in a nonjudicial foreclosure pursuant to the California Revenue and Tax Code. The court also held that appellant had constructive notice of the recorded tax liens.

 

555 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Am. River Fire Prot. Dist. v. Brennan


No. C025051.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


58 Cal. App. 4th 20; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 660; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 792; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7789; 97 Daily Journal DAR 12505



August 29, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published September 29, 1997 on Denial of Rehearing, Reported at: 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 793.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. CV530471. John R. Lewis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. Defendants shall recover their costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant retired firefighters sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which granted plaintiff fire protection district summary judgment and recovery of payments of accrued but unused sick leave made to defendants at their retirement pursuant to negotiated agreements.


OVERVIEW: The collective bargaining agreement between plaintiff fire protection district and the union representing defendant firefighters provided that, upon retirement, accrued but unused sick leave would be converted to additional service credit or employees could be paid for up to one-half of accumulated sick leave and all remaining leave would be applied for retirement credit. In accordance with these agreements, defendants retired and were paid for a portion of their unused sick leave. Plaintiff sought to recover these payments on the ground that the buy-out program violated Cal. Const. art. XI, § 10(a). The trial court granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court reversed because the buyout program provided an alternative that would result in increased benefits upon retirement for some firefighters payable because of their status at retirement, not as extra compensation for work already performed. The court held that the right to pension benefits vested upon the acceptance of employment and an increase after retirement was not prohibited extra compensation within Cal. Const. art. XI, §10(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment because the buy-out provision of the collective bargaining agreement between plaintiff fire protection district and the union representing defendant firefighters did not result in extra compensation for work already performed in violation of the California Constitution but substituted a cash benefit at retirement for an increased pension.

Kraus v. Trinity Management Services, Inc.


A070864/A071375


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


57 Cal. App. 4th 709; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 210; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 685; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7034; 97 Daily Journal DAR 11293



August 28, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted October 29, 1997 (S064870), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 7343.
Reprinted without change in the January 2000 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Court.
Supreme Court of California Opinion of June 5, 2000, Reported at: 23 Cal. 4th 116.
Review Denied November 14, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Cal. LEXIS 7855.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Super. Ct. No. 959982. Roy L. Norman, Judge. *


* Retired judge of the Los Angeles Superior Court, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, section 6 of the California Constitution.



DISPOSITION: With the exception of that portion of the judgment awarding prejudgment interest, which is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion, both the Judgment and the Order Granting Plaintiffs' Motion for Award of Attorney's Fees and Costs are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, landlord and management company, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) in favor of plaintiffs, former tenants, which ordered defendants to disgorge monies collected as a result of illegal rental practices that violated Cal. Civ. Code §§ 1960.5, 1671 because they were found to constitute unfair business practices under Cal Bus. & Prof. Code § 17200.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, former tenants, claimed that defendants, landlord and management company, violated Cal. Civ. Code §§ 1950.5, 1671 by collecting a $ 100.00 nonrefundable lease initiation fee from each new tenant and for including a liquidated damages provision for early termination that was paid from a tenant's security deposit. Defendants claimed that collateral estoppel barred plaintiffs' claims against the fee because an earlier lawsuit held that the fee was legal. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for plaintiffs, which ordered defendants to disgorge the lease initiation and liquidated damages fees. The court held that collateral estoppel was not applicable because § 1950.5(e), which defined security payments, was amended to include the fee as a security. The court held that the fee violated § 1950.5 because it was nonrefundable and used for a prohibited purpose. The court held that the liquidated damages provision violated § 1671 because actual damages for early termination were neither impracticable or extremely difficult to fix, and defendants failed to make a reasonable endeavor to estimate their fair average of compensation for their loss.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of plaintiffs, former tenants. The court held that defendants, landlord and management company, violated the law by charging a lease initiation fee and by including a liquidated damages clause for early termination. The court held that the fee was improper because it was nonrefundable and used for a prohibited purpose, and the liquidated damages clause was void because damages were readily ascertainable.

 

557 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Doe v. Wilson


No. A076721.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


57 Cal. App. 4th 296; 67 Cal. Rptr. 2d 187; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 673; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6791; 97 Daily Journal DAR 11036



August 25, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied November 12, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 7717.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco County, Nos. 982521/982522. William J. Cahill, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order granting the preliminary injunction is vacated. The matter is remanded to the trial court with instructions to enter a new order, denying the request for a preliminary injunction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state officials sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco County (California) that ordered a preliminary injunction that barred appellants enforcement of an interim emergency regulations enacted to comply with the Personal Responsibility and Work Opportunity Reconciliation Act of 1996, 8 U.S.C.S. § 1601 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Respondents sought a preliminary injunction to bar appellant state officials from enforcing an interim emergency regulations enacted to comply with the Personal Responsibility and Work Opportunity Reconciliation Act of 1996 (PRA), 8 U.S.C.S. § 1601 et seq. The injunction was granted, and appellants sought review. In reversing the decision, the court held that appellants acted properly and within their discretion in promulgating emergency administrative regulations to conform state regulations to governing federal law, and to end the state's violation of federal law. When Congress, with plenary immigration powers, decided California could not provide public funding for routine prenatal medical services for illegal aliens, the congressional mandate could not be undermined. Because the state program was rendered immediately illegal, the state judiciary could not frustrate prompt compliance with that federal law by forbidding the state from issuing the necessary emergency regulations that would achieve timely state compliance with its provisions. Appellants properly exercised its discretion when they determined the PRA was an unforeseen situation that called for immediate action.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order that granted respondents preliminary injunction, holding the injunction barred timely implementation of a new and valid federal law, which effectively required appellant state officials to continue a program made illegal by plenary federal law. The court ruled that prompt compliance with federal law could not be frustrated by forbidding appellants from issuing emergency regulations that would achieve compliance.

 

558 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Booth v. Superior Court


No. B108794.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


57 Cal. App. 4th 91; 66 Cal. Rptr. 2d 758; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 656; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6601; 97 Daily Journal DAR 10721



August 18, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 11, 1997. Review Denied December 10, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 8434.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Super. Ct. No. SA017197, Candance D. Cooper, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The petition for a writ of prohibition is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Based on defendant's alleged lack of competence at his preliminary hearing, defendant petitioned for a writ of prohibition against the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) to set aside the information charging him with forcible rape and related crimes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with forcible rape and related charges. After an appearance for arraignment, he was twice found to be not competent, hospitalized for treatment, and declared competent again. Criminal proceedings resumed. The preliminary hearing was held, and defendant answered to the charges. He later appeared in court, was arraigned, pleaded not guilty, and denied special allegations. At a later date, the trial court found defendant not competent and committed him for treatment. When defendant was again found competent and criminal proceedings resumed, defendant moved to set aside the information on the ground that he had not been competent at his preliminary hearing. The trial court denied the motion, and the court affirmed, because there was no evidence defendant was not competent at his preliminary examination. The judge did not state a doubt as to defendant's competence in the record; thus, defendant was presumed competent. He was held to answer and was legally committed to trial by a magistrate. At that point, if defendant were later found to be incompetent, criminal proceedings would be suspended and would resume (not begin anew) when competence was restored.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of prohibition because defendant was presumed competent at his preliminary hearing. The judge voiced no doubts for the record as to defendant's competence, defendant was held to answer for the charges, and he was thus legally committed to stand trial by a magistrate.

 

559 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Trippet


No. A073484.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


56 Cal. App. 4th 1532; 66 Cal. Rptr. 2d 559; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 649; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6513; 97 Daily Journal DAR 10639



August 15, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified September 5, 1997. Review Denied November 25, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 8225.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Contra Costa County, Super. Ct. No. 950331-9. Richard Patsey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appellant's convictions vacated and the cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction in the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California) for possession and transportation of marijuana in violation of Cal. Health and Safety Code §§ 11360(a) and 11357(c).


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of possession and transportation of marijuana. The court on appeal rejected defendant's claim of medical necessity, finding that she could not claim to have no reasonable alternative to smoking marijuana when a legal migraine medication was available. Because a doctor's testimony was relevant only to whether defendant could establish a medical necessity defense, and that defense could not be raised, it was properly excluded. Defendant's religious freedom defense was rejected because application of religion-neutral, general criminal drug laws did not run afoul of U.S. Const. amend. I and defendant provided no evidence of her religious beliefs. The court vacated the convictions and remanded for a limited retrial to retroactively apply Proposition 215, codified as the Compassionate Use Law, Cal. Health and Safety Code § 11362.5, to determine whether a doctor recommended defendant's use of marijuana, what quantity was related to her medical needs, and whether the quantity transported and the method, timing and distance of the transportation were reasonably related to defendant's medical needs.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's convictions for possession and transportation of marijuana and remanded for a limited retrial to determine whether the marijuana was medically necessary, and if so, what quantity was related to her medical needs..

 

560 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Breda Costruzioni Ferroviarie v. L.A. County Metro. Transp. Auth.


No. B098355.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


56 Cal. App. 4th 1433; 66 Cal. Rptr. 2d 416; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 639; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6413; 97 Daily Journal DAR 10447



August 11, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC081022. Abby Soven, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment requiring MTA to pay Breda $ 615,743 is affirmed. Breda shall recover its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant transportation authority sought review of the judgment entered by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), in favor of respondent contractor, requiring appellant to pay respondent interest earned by funds withheld pursuant to a subcontractor's stop notice.


OVERVIEW: Respondent contractor had a prime contract to provide rail cars to appellant transportation authority. A subcontractor supplying respondent filed a stop notice with appellant, requiring appellant to withhold payments owed to respondent. Respondent filed a stop notice release bond, and appellant paid respondent the full principal, but refused to pay the accrued interest. The trial court entered judgment in favor of respondent for the amount of the accrued interest. On appeal, the court held that, under the taking clause in U.S. Const. amend. V and under California common law, appellant's appropriation of the interest was barred. Moreover, there was no provision of the stop notice law which authorized withholding interest to defray expenses of administering the stop notice procedure, nor was there any evidence that such expense was incurred. The court also considered respondent's claim that a 10 percent statutory interest rate should have been applied under Cal. Pub. Cont. § 20204.50, but held that that section applied only to undisputed pay requests, whereas the stop notice in this case disputed respondent's entitlement to the money.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of respondent contractor for the amount of accrued interest withheld by appellant transportation authority because appropriation of the interest was barred by the taking clause and common law.
