Citizens for Responsible Gov't v. City of Albany


No. A073708.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


56 Cal. App. 4th 1199; 66 Cal. Rptr. 2d 102; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 623; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6128; 97 Daily Journal DAR 10014



August 1, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 2, 1997. Review Denied November 12, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 7700.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, Super. Ct. No. 746987-9. Sandra Margulies, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment on the first and sixth causes of action is reversed. In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed. The matter is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. Costs to appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen's group filed an appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which dismissed appellant's complaint for a writ of mandate and declaratory relief against respondent city and respondent real parties in interest, a horse racing track management company and a casino management company, concerning card-room gaming at a waterfront horse racing track.


OVERVIEW: Respondent city placed a measure on the ballot to permit card-room gaming at a waterfront horse racing track managed by respondent real party in interest. Appellant citizen's group sought a writ of mandate and declaratory relief against respondent city, challenging the initiative and development agreement. The trial court denied relief. On appeal, the court reversed in part and remanded. The court found that respondent city's action in submitting the development agreement to the voters constituted conditional approval of the project subject to environmental review under the California Environmental Quality Act. In the absence of an exemption, respondent city was required to prepare an initial study to assess the necessity of an environmental impact report or negative declaration. By failing to conduct any environmental review, respondent city did not proceed in a manner required by law in adopting the ballot measure. The court found that the measure violated Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 19819 concerning a prescribed ballot form. Otherwise, the court found that the development agreement and ballot measure were constitutional, and met city procedural requirements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part and remanded the judgment of the trial court that dismissed appellant's complaint for a writ of mandate and declaratory relief, because the court found that respondent city failed to comply with the California Environmental Quality Act prior to submitting the ballot measure to the voters, and that the measure violated ballot requirements. Otherwise, the court affirmed.

In re Meranda P.


No. F026419, No. F027095.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


56 Cal. App. 4th 1143; 65 Cal. Rptr. 2d 913; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 615; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6024; 97 Daily Journal DAR 9853



July 29, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied November 12, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 7558.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Stanislaus County. Super. Ct. No. A-29767. Timothy J. Helfer, Temporary Judge. *


* Pursuant to Cal. Const., art. VI, § 21

.



DISPOSITION: The order terminating the mother's parental rights to Meranda is affirmed. The request to treat the appeal as a petition for extraordinary relief is denied. The petition for writ of habeas corpus is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mother challenged an order of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County (California), terminating defendant's parental rights as recommended by plaintiff department after finding that returning the child to defendant's care would create a substantial risk of detriment to child's physical and emotional well being. Defendant sought a writ of habeas corpus and requested that her appeal be treated as a petition for extraordinary relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant mother challenged the juvenile court's order terminating her parental rights to her daughter. She was unrepresented by counsel at the detention hearing and throughout the reunification period, having informed the trial court that she did not want counsel. Defendant was a teenager with a history of substance abuse, and both defendant and her daughter tested positive for methamphetamine. Plaintiff department recommended the termination of defendant's parental rights as to the child. The juvenile court found that defendant had made only minimal progress towards reunification, and that the child's return to defendant would create a substantial risk of detriment to the child's physical and emotional well being. Defendant appealed and filed a petition for habeas corpus relief, asserting error in that she was either denied counsel or incompetently represented. The court affirmed and denied defendant's petition, because defendant was barred from raising the propriety of the orders antedating the termination order and from collaterally attacking the termination order or the orders antecedent to it.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed. Defendant mother's parental rights were properly terminated, as were her petition for habeas corpus relief and her appeal, because neither the absence nor blunder of appointed counsel alone entitled defendant to obtain the relief she sought absent proof that the proceeding was rendered fundamentally unfair.

People v. Hedge


D026713


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


56 Cal. App. 4th 773; 65 Cal. Rptr. 2d 693; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 590; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5888; 97 Daily Journal DAR 9317



July 22, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted October 29, 1997 (S063954), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 7341.
Reprinted without change in the January 2000 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Review Dismissed February 16, 2000 and cause remanded to Ct. App., 4th Dist., Div. 1 (rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 2000 Cal. LEXIS 995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from judgments of the Superior Court of San Diego County, Super. Ct. Nos. CR108176, CR129737, CF68607, CR124544, CR77163, CRN7211, CR126057. David J. Danielson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of seven judgments from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which ruled on demurrers to appellant's petitions for commitment, holding that the Sexually Violent Predators Act, Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq., was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to each of the seven respondents. The petitions were dismissed.


OVERVIEW: Petitions for commitment were brought by appellant state against seven respondents under the Sexually Violent Predators Act (act), Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq. The act was directed at a small but extremely dangerous group of sexually violent predators who had diagnosable mental disorders and could be identified while they were incarcerated. The legislature determined that the predators were not safe to be at large and that, if released without treatment, they represented a danger to the health and safety of others in that they were likely to engage in acts of sexual violence. Dismissing the petitions, the trial court ruled on respondent's demurrers that the act was both unconstitutional on its face and as applied to each of the seven respondents. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that the act satisfied federal substantive due process and did not violate the constitutional guarantees of equal protection or against ex post facto laws and double jeopardy. The court rejected the trial court's ruling that the act was essentially a punitive consequence of each defendant's prior convictions and not a "civil" commitment procedure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the seven judgments of the superior court that dismissed appellant state's petitions for commitment. The court found that the Sexually Violent Predators Act satisfied federal substantive due process and did not violate the constitutional guarantees of equal protection or against ex post facto laws and double jeopardy.

 

564 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



152 Valparaiso Assocs. v. City of Cotati


No. A075553.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


56 Cal. App. 4th 378; 65 Cal. Rptr. 2d 551; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 616; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5813; 97 Daily Journal DAR 9336



July 22, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 18, 1997. Review Denied October 29, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 7533.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sonoma County. Court No. 209950. Hon. Laurence K. Sawyer, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of dismissal vacated. Matter remanded to trial court with instructions to overrule demurrer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Sonoma County (California), which sustained a demurrer and dismissed its claim alleging that the rent control laws of respondents, city and rent appeals board, failed to advance the stated objectives and resulted in a taking of appellants' property without just compensation, in violation of U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV, and Cal. Const. art. I, § 19.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owners sought review of a decision which sustained a demurrer and dismissed their claim that respondents, city and rent appeals board, violated U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV, and Cal. Const. art. I, § 19, when respondents failed to allow a rent increase sufficient to give appellants a fair return on their investment in capital improvements to their property because it resulted in an unconstitutional taking of their investment property and because respondents failed to advance their stated public goals. The court held that a property owner could challenge a regulatory taking if it did not advance a legitimate state interest, and that rent control laws were unconstitutional if they deprived a property owner of a fair return on his investment. Whether regulations were fair or unconstitutionally confiscatory was to be determined by the result they produced. The court vacated the judgment of dissmissal and remanded with instructions to overrule the demurrer and to litigate whether appellants' allegations that evidence supported their claim that census data showed no legitimate state interest was advanced, and resulting in a taking of appellants' property.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment dismissing appellant property owners' action was vacated and the case remanded to the lower court with instructions to overrule the demurrer of respondents, city and rent appeals board, in a claim by appellant property owners, because rent control laws were unconstitutional if they deprived a property owner of a fair return on his investment and failed to advance their stated public goals.

De Guere v. Universal City Studios


Nos. B091294, B092813.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


56 Cal. App. 4th 482; 65 Cal. Rptr. 2d 438; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 560; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5640; 97 Daily Journal DAR 9105



July 15, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Los Angeles Superior Court. Super. Ct. No. BC61389. Frances Rothschild, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed as to dismissal of the cause of action for usury. The judgment is reversed and the case is remanded for the trial court to resolve the issues of contract interpretation and enforceability, in a manner consistent with the views expressed in this opinion. Mr. De Guere is to have his costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff television producer sought review of an order and judgment by the Los Angeles Superior Court (California), which adopted the findings of a referee and entered judgment for defendant television studio in plaintiff's action for breach of contract and an accounting. Plaintiff contended that the referee's findings were void, that he was deprived of a jury trial and due process, and that the usury action was incorrectly dismissed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff television producer filed an action against defendant television studio for breach of contract and an accounting concerning entitlement to profits from a television series. Plaintiff appealed from an order adopting the findings of a referee and the judgment entered for defendant. The court found that because the referee's findings concerning contract interpretation and enforceability issues were beyond the scope of the reference under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 639(a), the findings were void and could not have been validly adopted by the trial court. The court found that plaintiff was not deprived of his right to a jury trial because the gist of his action was for an accounting, for which no such right attached, and that his right to due process was not violated. The trial court correctly sustained defendant's demurrer to the usury cause of action because the agreement between plaintiff and defendant was not a loan or forbearance. Accordingly, the court reversed and remanded as to the contract interpretation and enforceability issue, and the court affirmed the dismissal of the usury action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment as to the issues of contract interpretation and enforceability in plaintiff television producer's action against defendant television studio for breach of contract and an accounting because the referee's findings exceeded the scope of the reference. The court affirmed the dismissal of the usury action because the contract at issue was not a loan or forbearance.

 

566 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Bradley v. Medical Bd.


No. D025434.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


56 Cal. App. 4th 445; 65 Cal. Rptr. 2d 483; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 561; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5663; 97 Daily Journal DAR 9089



July 15, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. N65347. Lisa Guy- Schall, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Dr. Bradley to pay defendants' costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff physician appealed from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which granted summary judgment for defendants, Medical Board of California and individuals, in plaintiff's action alleging violations of his federal and state constitutional due process rights, including claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Defendant Medical Board of California (Board) authorized an undercover investigation of plaintiff physician after receiving complaints that plaintiff was prescribing drugs without a good faith examination. Plaintiff was eventually charged in connection with the investigation. The court affirmed the summary judgment for defendants, Board and individuals, in plaintiff's due process action. Defendant attorney general was absolutely immune from plaintiff's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims because defendant attorney general's acts were undertaken as a prosecutor in preparing for the initiation of judicial proceedings. Defendant Board employee who initiated the undercover investigation was entitled to qualified immunity for his actions. Defendant Board had every right to conduct an investigation once it suspected plaintiff of unprofessional conduct. Defendant employee's reliance on another physician's opinion in obtaining a search warrant was reasonable. Defendant private citizens that assisted defendant Board's investigation were entitled to qualified immunity because they performed a governmental function pursuant to a request and their actions were reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment for defendants, Medical Board of California and individuals, in plaintiff physician's action alleging violation of state and federal due process rights. Defendant attorney general was entitled to absolute immunity because he acted as a prosecutor in preparing for trial initiation. Other defendant individuals who initiated and assisted in the investigation were entitled to qualified immunity.

People v. Johns


No. E018206.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


56 Cal. App. 4th 550; 65 Cal. Rptr. 2d 434; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 564; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5676; 97 Daily Journal DAR 9151



July 15, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts 2. 3. 4. and 5.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied October 22, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 6658.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. Super.Ct.No. FWV-8362. Jacob H. Jager, Judge of the Municipal Court, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to art. VI, § 6 of the Cal. Const.)



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California) entering his convictions for oral copulation of a person under the age of 16, committing lewd and lascivious acts on a minor, contributing to the delinquency of a minor, and possession of child pornography, in violation of Cal. Penal Code §§ 288a(b)(2), 288(a), 272, 311.11(a). Defendant contended his right to confrontation was violated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with oral copulation of a person under the age of 16, committing lewd and lascivious acts on a minor, contributing to the delinquency of a minor, and possession of child pornography, in violation of Cal. Penal Code §§ 288a(b)(2), 288(a), 272, 311.11(a). Over a defense objection, the victim's mother sat next to him as he testified. Defendant was convicted. Defendant appealed, contending his right to confrontation was violated by the presence of the mother. The appellate court affirmed. The child testified that he wanted his mother because he liked her. Thus, there was no subconscious message to the jury that the victim was traumatized and it was more likely the sexual assault occurred. Further, her presence did not add credibility to or affect the child's testimony. Thus, defendant's confrontational rights were not violated. Further, the court found that the absence of a requirement of a case-specific showing of necessity did not, as defendant argued, make the statute allowing support persons, Cal. Penal Code § 868.5, unconstitutional per se.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's entry of defendant's convictions for oral copulation of a person under the age of 16, committing lewd and lascivious acts on a minor, contributing to the delinquency of a minor, and possession of child pornography. Although a mother sat next to her son, the victim, as he testified, defendant's confrontational rights were not implicated because her presence did not affect the testimony.

Branson v. Martin


No. B105906.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


56 Cal. App. 4th 300; 65 Cal. Rptr. 2d 401; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 549; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5471; 97 Daily Journal DAR 8828



July 9, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts 1 and 4.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 29, 1997. Review Denied September 24, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 6071.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC151053. George P. Schiavelli, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of dismissal is affirmed. Respondents are awarded costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual appealed an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), entering judgment for defendants, county and county commissioner, in a suit for damages. Plaintiff claimed that defendant county commissioner lacked jurisdiction over him at a traffic violation hearing and that defendants were liable for jailing him when he failed to sign a promise to appear.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff individual received a traffic ticket. At the arraignment, defendant county commissioner asked plaintiff how he wished to plead, and plaintiff stated he wanted to appear before a magistrate. Defendant county commissioner took that as a nonresponse and entered a plea of not guilty pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1042. Plaintiff refused to sign a promise to appear and was jailed. Plaintiff then brought a claim for damages against defendants, county and county commissioner. The claim was denied, and plaintiff sued on various novel grounds. Defendants claimed that judicial immunity barred suit. The trial court granted judgment for defendants. The court affirmed. Because defendant county commissioner had the general power to conduct traffic infraction arraignments and to issue bench warrants, defendant county commissioner qualified as a magistrate under Cal. Penal Code § 807. Because plaintiff failed to overcome the presumption that defendant commissioner validly performed his official duties and because the trial court acted within its jurisdiction, plaintiff's claims were properly dismissed. Claims against defendant county were dismissed where premised upon vicarious liability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff's suit for damages against defendants, county and county commissioner. Because defendant county commissioner qualified as a magistrate, he properly presided over plaintiff's arraignment for a traffic violation. Because plaintiff failed to rebut the presumption that defendant commissioner validly performed his official duties and that jurisdiction was proper, his claims were dismissed.

 

569 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



E.W.A.P., Inc. v. City of L.A.


No. B102861.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


56 Cal. App. 4th 310; 65 Cal. Rptr. 2d 325; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 548; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5473; 97 Daily Journal DAR 8821



July 9, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 7, 1997. Review Denied October 1, 1997 (S063674), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 6248.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC123230. Robert H. O'Brien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bookstore sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied its petition for writ of mandate against respondent city in an action that arose from respondent's ordinance to abate nuisances.


OVERVIEW: Appellant bookstore filed a claim for injunctive relief against respondent city regarding the enforcement of a nuisance ordinance. The trial court denied appellant's claim. Appellant alleged several points of error. The court affirmed and held that Los Angeles, Cal., Municipal Code ch. I, art. 2 § 12.21A-15 was constitutional because it primarily targeted nuisance activities. The court held that § 12.21A-15 was not vague and that appellant did not have standing to argue against the ordinance in the abstract. The court determined that the lack of sworn testimony and cross-examination at an administrative proceeding on nuisance abatement did not violate appellant's right to due process because of fiscal burdens. The court held that substantial evidence review was properly applied because an administrative decision that resulted in profit reduction was an impact on economic interests not fundamental rights. The court determined that the underlying decision of the zoning board was supported by substantial evidence because of statements from witnesses. The court held that that the zoning board relied on cumulative evidence in reviewing the decision of the zoning administrator.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which denied appellant bookstore's writ of mandate. The court held that respondent city's nuisance ordinance was constitutional because its primary target was nuisance activities and that appellant's due process rights were not violated in zoning board proceedings because sworn testimony and cross-examination of witnesses were not required.

 

570 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Marroquin


A065808


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


56 Cal. App. 4th 1; 65 Cal. Rptr. 2d 62; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 522; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5120; 97 Daily Journal DAR 8298



June 26, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied October 15, 1997 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 6361.


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of San Francisco. Superior Court Ct. No. 150568-1. Honorable Alex Saldamando.

Original Opinion of March 28, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 242.



DISPOSITION: We reverse the judgment as to count IX, a conviction of participation in a criminal street gang under Penal Code section 186.22, subdivision (a). The remainder of the judgment is affirmed. We remand the matter for retrial on count IX and/or resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions from the City and County of San Francisco Superior Court (California) for assault, firearm related crimes, and participation in a criminal street gang, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 186.22. Defendant claimed, among other things, that his conviction for participation in a criminal street gang was barred by the double jeopardy clause. U.S. Const. amend. V.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions for assault-and firearms-related crimes as well as his conviction for participating in a criminal street gang, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 186.2. The court affirmed defendant's assault-and firearms-related convictions and reversed defendant's conviction for participating in a criminal street gang. The court did not certify for publication its rulings regarding defendant's assault-and firearms-related convictions. Regarding the gang-related conviction, the court ruled that reversal was required because the conviction violated the double jeopardy clause. U.S. Const. amend. V. The court observed that defendant stipulated that he was a member of a gang and that he participated in two of the underlying crimes, for which he had been previously convicted and punished. However, the court reasoned, the jury found did not find the gang enhancements true, and therefore the conviction must have been based upon his earlier criminal conduct and not upon any active participation. Thus, because the trial court did not instruct the jury that the conviction had to be based upon current, active participation, reversal was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed all of defendant's conviction assault-and firearm-related convictions and reversed his conviction for participation in a criminal street gang. The evidence did not support a finding that defendant was, at the time of the charged offenses, currently and actively participating in a criminal street gang, but rather that the jury's verdict was based impermissibly on defendant's prior conviction.

 

571 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Agnew v. State Bd. of Equalization


B101992


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


55 Cal. App. 4th 1479; 64 Cal. Rptr. 2d 771; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 513; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5076; 97 Daily Journal DAR 8101



June 25, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted October 1, 1997 (S063339), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 6164.
Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Supreme Court of California Disposition Reported at: 21 Cal. 4th 310.
Review granted, Depublished by Agnew v. California State Bd. of Equalization, 68 Cal. Rptr. 2d 290, 945 P.2d 281, 1997 Cal. LEXIS 6164 (Cal., 1997)
Superseded by, Affirmed by Agnew v. State Bd. of Equalization, 21 Cal. 4th 310, 87 Cal. Rptr. 2d 423, 981 P.2d 52, 1999 Cal. LEXIS 5305 (1999)
Costs and fees proceeding at, Remanded by Agnew v. State Bd. of Equalization, 2005 Cal. App. LEXIS 1877 (Cal. App. 2d Dist., Dec. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC137289. Frances Rothschild, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that sustained the demurrer of appellee California State Board of Equalization. Appellant argued that he should not have been required to pay the accrued interest on a tax deficiency, as well as the tax claimed due and owing, as a necessary precondition for review by appellee of a claim for refund of an alleged overpayment of sales or use tax.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer received "notices of determination" from appellee California Board of Equalization that he owed sales and use taxes. Appellant filed claims for refund of overpayment with appellee. In one case he paid the tax deficiency and the accrued interest thereon, as required by appellee as a pre-condition for a refund review. In another, he paid the tax deficiency, but not the accrued interest. Appellant sought declaratory relief that appellee was not entitled to require payment of the accrued interest. Appellee demurred on the basis that appellant did not exhaust his administrative remedies and that California law precluded any action to prevent the collection of sales and use tax. The trial court sustained the demurrer. On appeal, the court reversed. The court noted that appellant's action did not seek to avoid payment of any tax or to compel a refund of paid taxes. The court held that there was no statutory basis for appellee's policy on accrued interest. The court ruled that as appellant had met the requirements for filing a valid claim for refund prior to filing his action he had in fact exhausted his administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that sustained appellee California State Board of Equalization's demurrer. The court ruled that appellant taxpayer was not required to pay accrued interest in addition to the underlying tax as a necessary precondition to filing a valid claim for refund or to filing its action for declaratory relief. The court remanded with directions to overrule the demurrer and afford appellee time to answer the complaint.

 

572 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. McCleod


No. D025447.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


55 Cal. App. 4th 1205; 64 Cal. Rptr. 2d 545; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 489; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4691; 97 Daily Journal DAR 7718; 97 Daily Journal DAR 8355



June 18, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. 1 


1 Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part IV.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified on Denial of Rehearing of July 16, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 571. Review Denied October 1, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 6287.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, Super. Ct. No. SCD116317. Melissa J. Lasater, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sex offender registrant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), convicting him of failing to register a change of address as required by Cal. Penal Code § 290 (f) and sentencing him to a five-year enhanced prison term.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sex offender registrant was evicted from his apartment and was transient for a period of time. He was later arrested at his new residence, charged, and convicted of violating Cal. Penal Code § 290 (f) for failing to inform police in writing of his new address. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the trial court properly instructed the jury on the elements required for conviction and was not required to define the commonly understood term "residence" in response to a jury question. Appellant waived any possible violation of Cal. Penal Code § 1138 by not objecting to a continuation of deliberations while the parties worked on a definition. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. The jury could have reasonably inferred that after the eviction appellant was residing with either his mother or his girlfriend until he moved and that he willfully failed to notify police of either address within 10 days of the eviction. It was sufficient for a showing of willfulness under § 290(f) that his actions were done with a purpose or willingness. The jury did not need to find he specifically intended to evade police.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. The trial court properly instructed the jury on the elements required for conviction under the sex offender registration statute and was not required to further define the term "residence" in response to a jury question. The conviction was supported by sufficient evidence of all required elements of the offense; evidence of intent to evade police was not necessary for a finding of willfulness as defined by statute.

People v. Roberts


B099308


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


55 Cal. App. 4th 1073; 65 Cal. Rptr. 2d 17; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 483; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4591; 97 Daily Journal DAR 7576



June 17, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified June 19, 1997. Review Denied October 1, 1997 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 6232.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BA096654. Arthur M. Lew, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of three counts of second degree robbery in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 211, which found that he had used a firearm in each robbery in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12022.5(a), and which sentenced him to prison for 93 years to life because of his prior convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second degree robbery in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 211(a), and he was found to have personally used a firearm in each robbery in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12022.5(a). The trial court found true that defendant had seven serious felonies pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 667(a), and the trial court found that each was a "strike" pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 667(b)-(i) and that three were state prison priors pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 667.5(b). Defendant was sentenced to state prison for 93 years to life. Defendant appealed, contending that testimony that gang members would testify falsely for a non-gang member from the same neighborhood was not relevant and that consecutive sentences violated Cal. Penal Code § 667. The court affirmed, holding that the testimony was relevant and the prejudicial effect was minimal. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the testimony pursuant to Cal. Evid. Code § 352. Moreover, the court held that defendant could be separately and consecutively punished for each robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of three counts of second degree robbery and which sentenced him to prison for 93 years to life. The court held that the trial court did not err in admitting testimony about gang behavior and that defendant could be consecutively punished for each robbery conviction.

People v. White


No. D025862.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


55 Cal. App. 4th 914; 64 Cal. Rptr. 2d 245; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 463; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4439; 97 Daily Journal DAR 7357



June 10, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, Super. Ct. No. CR125511. David J. Danielsen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a portion of his sentence from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) following his conviction for continuous sexual abuse of a child in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 288.5(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to continuous sexual abuse of a child in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 288.5(a). Defendant's 16-year prison sentence was stayed pending a 5-year grant of probation. Probation was subsequently revoked and defendant was resentenced by stipulation. Part of defendant's revised sentence included a restitution fine and direct restitution to be paid from prison wages pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 2085.5. Defendant appealed his sentence and contended that the payment of direct restitution from his prison wages was in violation of the prohibition against ex post facto legislation. However, defendant failed to object to the manner of payment of restitution and, therefore, did not preserve the issue for appeal. Therefore, the issue was waived on appeal and judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment ordering defendant to pay direct restitution from his prison wages was affirmed. Because defendant failed to raise an objection to the issue of the manner of payment, he waived the issue on appeal.

People v. Crooks


No. C023565.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


55 Cal. App. 4th 797; 64 Cal. Rptr. 2d 236; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 456; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4375; 97 Daily Journal DAR 7328



June 10, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts I, II, V and VI of the Discussion.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied September 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 5802.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, Super. Ct. No. 95F09547. Kenneth L. Hake, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The sentence is modified to increase the enhancement on count 5 to two years. As modified, the judgment is affirmed. The trial court shall prepare an amended abstract of judgment reflecting this modification and shall furnish a copy to the Department of Corrections.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which convicted him of burglary and rape, and which imposed an enhanced sentence under the provisions of California's "first strike" sentencing law, Cal. Penal Code § 667.61. Defendant claimed the sentence violated the U.S. Const. amend. VIII and was excessively disproportionate. The prosecution claimed the sentence was too light.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary and rape of a victim in her own bedroom, for which he was sentenced to 25 years to life under Cal. Penal Code § 667.61, the "one strike" provision mandating life sentences for certain forcible rapes. Defendant appealed, claiming that the statute was unconstitutional and the sentence was disproportionate. The prosecution not only disagreed with defendant's claims of error but contended that defendant's sentence was too light because the trial court's imposition of a reduced enhancement on one of the counts was unauthorized by law. The court held that defendant's sentence was impermissibly disproportionate and not cruel and unusual under U.S. Const. amend. VIII or the equivalent provision of the California constitution, nor did it violate defendant's rights to equal protection of the law under U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Cal. Const., art. I, § 7(a). However, the court agreed with the prosecution that the reduced enhancement was not authorized, so it modified the sentence to impose the full enhancement, and affirmed the conviction and sentence as modified.


OUTCOME: The court held that the sentence did not constitute cruel or unusual punishment, nor did it violate defendant's right to equal protection of the laws. However, the court found that the trial court's reduction of one of the enhancements was unauthorized by law. Therefore, the court modified the sentence to increase the enhancement and affirmed the judgment as modified.

 

576 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Lucas


No. A068400.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


55 Cal. App. 4th 721; 64 Cal. Rptr. 2d 282; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 450; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4332; 97 Daily Journal DAR 7189



June 6, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 7, 1997. Review Denied September 24, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 6014.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo County, Super. Ct. No. SC33381. Clarence B. Knight, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed as to both defendants. For clarity, the superior court shall in Donaghe's case direct the preparation, and forwarding to the proper authority, of an amended abstracted of judgment reflecting that Donaghe's one-year enhancement on the count 2 conspiracy to commit robbery is pursuant to section 12022, subdivision (a)(1).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed an order from the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), entering their convictions for second-degree murder, robbery, conspiracy to rob, personal gun use, discharge at an occupied vehicle causing death, and simple arming, in violation of Cal. Penal Code §§ 187- 189, 212.5, 182, 12022.5(a) and 12022.5(d), and 12022(a)(1). Defendants claimed reversal was necessary due to improper jury charges and insufficient evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendants robbed a drug dealer. Later, believing that the occupants of another car were threatening them, one defendant asked for his co-defendant's gun and discharged the gun at the car. The driver died. Defendants were convicted of second-degree murder, robbery, conspiracy to rob, personal gun use, discharge at an occupied vehicle causing death, and simple arming, in violation of Cal. Penal Code §§ 187- 189, 212.5, 182, 12022.5(a) and 12022.5(d), and 12022(a)(1). Defendants appealed. The aiding and abetting defendant claimed that the trial court gave an improper jury charge regarding the target crimes. Further, defendant claimed the state gave improper notice of the target crimes. Defendants also claimed that there was insufficient evidence to convict. The appellate court affirmed. Although the trial court failed to identify and describe potential target crimes, there was no reasonable likelihood that the jury found defendant aided and abetted any noncriminal behavior which led, as a natural and probable consequence, to the murder. Because the alleged instructional error was the sole error and was considered harmless error, the convictions were upheld.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's entry of defendants' conviction for, inter alia, second-degree murder, robbery, and aiding and abetting. Although the trial court failed to identify and describe potential target crimes in its jury charge, the jury did not improperly rely on any noncriminal behavior to convict defendant of aiding and abetting. Because this sole error was harmless, defendants' convictions were upheld.

 

577 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Cmty. Redevelopment Agency v. Force Electronics


No. B095278.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


55 Cal. App. 4th 622; 64 Cal. Rptr. 2d 209; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 441; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4258; 97 Daily Journal DAR 7089



June 4, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Super. Ct. No. BC003752. Ernest M. Hiroshige, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the holdings herein. Appellant to recover costs of this appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an eminent domain action, defendant sought review from a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted plaintiff's poverty motion and allowed the remaining balance owed defendant paid over 10 years with interest.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff agency condemned, took possession of, and demolished the improvements on the real property of defendant. After final judgment, plaintiff was unable to fully pay the amount of just compensation awarded to defendant. Defendant acted to repossess the property. Plaintiff pled poverty to the trial court, asking it to order the remaining balance owing paid over 10 years with interest. The trial court granted plaintiff's motion. On appeal, the court stated that under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1268.010(a), not later than 30 days after final judgment, the condemner had to pay the full amount required by the judgment. If an award remained unpaid after 30 days, the condemnee had the option to obtain a dismissal of the proceedings and repossess the property. If the condemner did not pay the full amount, the condemnee was allowed to choose whether to proceed under the California Government Code or get the property back. Defendant had no part in creating plaintiff's financial condition and simply sought the return of its property. The court held that defendant was entitled to this remedy. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which granted plaintiff's poverty motion and allowed the remaining balance owed defendant paid over 10 years with interest, and remanded for further proceedings. Because plaintiff did not pay the full amount of just compensation to defendant, defendant was entitled to the return of its property under statute.

International Assn. of Plumbing etc. Officials v. California Building Stds. Com


No. C022340.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


55 Cal. App. 4th 245; 64 Cal. Rptr. 2d 129; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 416; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4051; 97 Daily Journal DAR 6841



May 23, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 17, 1997. Review Denied August 13, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 5089.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, Super. Ct. No. 95CS00953. Ronald W. Tochterman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff private organizations appealed from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) which held defendant California Building Standards Commission was not precluded by the State Buildings Standards Law, Cal. Health & Safety Code § 18901 et seq., from adopting the Uniform Mechanical Code published exclusively by real party in interest private organization as the basis of the California Mechanical Code, Cal. Code Regs. tit. 24, § 4.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff private organizations challenged a trial court decision that denied plaintiffs' petition for a writ of mandate and held that the State Building Standards Law (Law), Cal. Health & Safety Code § 18901 et seq., did not preclude defendant California Buildings Standards Commission from adopting the version of the Uniform Mechanical Code exclusively published by real party in interest private organization as the California Mechanical Code, Cal. Code Regs. tit. 24, § 4. The court affirmed the trial court decision. Plaintiff, by withdrawing from the Uniform Mechanical Code that it previously published jointly with real party in interest, could not force defendant to adopt an older, outdated model code as the basis for state regulation with the force of law simply because that model code was specially listed in Cal. Health & Safety Code § 18938(b). The interpretation of the Law urged by plaintiff would amount to unlawful delegation of the lawmaking power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a trial court decision that that held the State Buildings Standards Law did not preclude defendant California Buildings Standards Commission from adopting the most recent version of the Uniform Mechanical Code, exclusively published by real party in interest, as the California Mechanical Code. Plaintiff was unable to force adoption of an older uniform code that it jointly published with real party in interest.

 

579 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Fitch


No. C023811.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


55 Cal. App. 4th 172; 63 Cal. Rptr. 2d 753; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 402; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3882; 97 Daily Journal DAR 6546



May 22, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts IV, V and VI.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 20, 1997. Review Denied September 3, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 5613.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, Super. Ct. No. 95F07496. Richard Kent Park, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which convicted him of rape. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in admitting evidence of appellant's commission of another sex offense and that Cal. Evid. Code § 1108, which permitted the admission of such evidence, was a violation of his due process rights and the ex post facto clauses of the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a judgment that convicted him of rape, contending that the trial court erred in allowing the admission of evidence of his commission of another sex offense. Appellant also contended that Cal. Evid. Code § 1108, which permitted the admission of character evidence to prove disposition to commit sexual crimes, violated his due process rights because the statute treated those accused of sex offenses differently from those accused of other crimes and was applied ex post facto. Appellant argued that the statute was subject to a strict scrutiny analysis because it infringed upon his constitutionally protected rights. Finding no prejudicial error, the appellate court affirmed the judgment of conviction, holding that Cal. Evid. Code § 1108 on its face did not violate the due process clause because it did not implicate any constitutional guarantees, nor did it offend any fundamental principle of justice. The appellate court also held that a new rule of evidence that admits evidence not previously admissible or which extends competency to a witness may validly operate in the trial of a prior offense.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment convicting appellant of rape was affirmed. The court held that the legislature was free to determine that the nature of sex offenses, both their seriousness and their secretive commission which resulted in trials that were primarily credibility contests, justified the admission of relevant evidence of the commission of other sex offenses.

People v. Mines


B102838


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


55 Cal. App. 4th 698; 63 Cal. Rptr. 2d 706; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 393; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3831; 97 Daily Journal DAR 6453



May 20, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified May 29, 1997. Review Denied July 30, 1997 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 4871.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Albert D. Matthews, Judge. Super. Ct. No. BA114964.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review after the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) sentenced him under the three strikes law following his conviction for the sale or transportation of cocaine base, in violation of Cal. Health & Safety code § 111352(a), and added consecutive sentence enhancements for two prior convictions pursuant to Cal. Health and Safety Code § 11370.2(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of the sale or transportation of cocaine base in violation of Cal. Health & Safety code § 11352(a). In addition to imposing a sentence of 25 years to life under the three strikes law, the trial court added consecutive enhancements for two prior convictions pursuant to Cal. Health and Safety Code § 11370.2(a). The appellate court affirmed, holding that a vacation and remand for resentencing was unnecessary, although the trial court misunderstood the scope of its discretion to strike a three strikes prior conviction, because the record clearly indicated that the trial court would not have exercised its discretion to strike the three strikes prior conviction allegations in any event. Also, the trial court properly denied appellant's pretrial motion to strike the alleged prior convictions as unconstitutional because the alleged constitutional errors raised by appellant could not be used to collaterally attack those convictions. Finally, the trial court did not err in imposing the two prior conviction enhancements pursuant to § 11370.2(a) consecutive to the term of 25 years to life.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the 25 year sentence imposed on defendant under the three strikes law, following his conviction for the sale or transportation of a cocaine base. Defendant was not allowed to collaterally attack the prior three strikes convictions and the trial court did not err in adding consecutive sentence enhancements for two other prior convictions.

People v. Ramirez


No. A073316.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


55 Cal. App. 4th 47; 64 Cal. Rptr. 2d 9; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 398; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3821; 97 Daily Journal DAR 6433



May 20, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part II.B.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied August 27, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 5433.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo County, Super. Ct. No. SC36793. Mark R. Forcum, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the constitutionality of Cal. Penal Code § 293.5 (1992) and the verdict from the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), that convicted appellant of assault with intent to commit rape, attempted rape, and sexual battery, and permitted the victim to be identified as "Jane Doe" pursuant to § 293.5.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was convicted of assault with intent to commit rape, attempted rape, and sexual battery, he sought review and argued that Cal. Penal Code § 293.5 (1992) violated U.S. Const. amend. VI because it allowed under certain circumstances the alleged victim of a sex offense to be identified as "Jane Doe" rather than by her true name. The appellate court found that there was no absolute right for appellant to have a jury hear the victim's true name. The appellate court affirmed appellant's conviction and upheld the constitutionality of § 293.5 because the statute provided for a balancing test that weighed the privacy interest of the victim of a sex offense and the resulting state interest in facilitating the reporting of sex offenses against the minimal intrusion on an accused's nonabsolute right of confrontation and as applied, the statute did not violate appellant's confrontation and cross-examination rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and upheld the constitutionality of the statute that permitted the victim of a sex offense to be identified as "Jane Doe" because the statute provided for a balancing test that weighed the privacy interest of the victim of a sex offense against the minimal intrusion on an accused's nonabsolute right of confrontation and as applied, appellant's confrontation and cross-examination rights were not violated.

Gilbert v. Nat'l Enquirer


No. B106923.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


55 Cal. App. 4th 1273; 64 Cal. Rptr. 2d 659; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 492; 97 Daily Journal DAR 7753; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4738; 25 Media L. Rep. 2147



May 20, 1997, Decided  
May 20, 1997


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976(b)(1) and (3), this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II and III.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court to Partial Published June 19, 1997. Review Denied August 20, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 5235.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Super. Ct. No. BC 131079. Aviva K. Bobb, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the order denying the Enquirer's motion for fees and costs under section 3344 and award Gilbert costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a tabloid publisher and ex-husband of respondent celebrity, challenged the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied appellant tabloid publisher's request for attorney fees and costs as the prevailing party under Cal. Civ. Code § 3344(a) following respondent's voluntary dismissal without prejudice of her commercial appropriation claims brought pursuant to that statute.


OVERVIEW: Respondent celebrity, plaintiff below, commenced an action claiming libel, invasion of privacy, and commercial appropriation under Cal. Civ. Code § 3344(a), against appellants, a tabloid publisher and her ex-husband, for appellants' publication of fabricated interviews. Respondent's libel and invasion of privacy claims were dismissed on appellants' demurrer, but her § 3344(a) claims survived. To expedite her appeal of the order dismissing her libel and invasion of privacy claims, respondent voluntarily withdrew her surviving claims without prejudice. The trial court at that point entered a judgment of dismissal for appellant tabloid publisher with respect to all of respondent's claims. Appellant tabloid publisher then moved for attorney fees and costs as the prevailing party under § 3344(a). The trial court denied the motion, and the court affirmed. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion because such a determination was to be made on a practical level, and, on a practical level, it was impossible to determine at that early stage of the litigation who would ultimately prevail on the surviving commercial appropriation claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying appellant tabloid publisher's motion for attorney fees and costs as the prevailing party on claims which respondent celebrity voluntarily dismissed without prejudice because, on a practical level, it was too early to determine which party would ultimately prevail on the voluntarily withdrawn claims.

In re Josh W.


No. A074495.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


55 Cal. App. 4th 1; 63 Cal. Rptr. 2d 701; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 388; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3784; 97 Daily Journal DAR 6391



May 19, 1997, Decided  
May 19, 1997


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part I.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied August 27, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 5435.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Solano County, Super. Ct. No. J27213. Barbara James, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: For all the foregoing reasons, the dispositional order of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Solano County (California), which in a juvenile proceeding under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 602, placed appellant on probation for one year on the condition that he was to be committed to juvenile hall for 15 weekends unless and until he revealed the identity of the other participants in the incident which gave rise to the petition.


OVERVIEW: Appellant minor challenged a decision that, pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 602, which placed him on probation for one year on the condition that he was to be committed to juvenile hall for 15 weekends unless and until he revealed who the other participants in the incident that gave rise to the delinquency petition against him. The court affirmed the dispositional order because the condition for the probation was reasonably related to a proper rehabilitative objective. The court stated that there was no reason to believe the two juveniles who eluded the police were any more or less responsible than appellant was for the offenses with which he was charged or the offense he confessed to. The court also stated that a disclosure requirement related to the offense for which appellant was held responsible in that it was to lead to enhanced restitution to the victim of that offense. Furthermore, if appellant's confederates were apprehended and afforded rehabilitation in the juvenile justice system, it would reduce the probability that appellant and they would have resumed their individual or collective criminal activities upon release.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dispositional order because the condition for the probation was reasonably related to a proper rehabilitative objective, and the disclosure requirement related to the offense for which appellant minor was held responsible was to lead to enhanced restitution to the victim of that offense.

 

584 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


International Brotherhood of Electrical Workers v. Superior Court


A077424


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


54 Cal. App. 4th 1291; 63 Cal. Rptr. 2d 555; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 365; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3549; 97 Daily Journal DAR 5985



May 9, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted July 9, 1997 (S061492), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 4197.
Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Court.
Review Dismissed April 21, 1999, pursuant to Real Parties motion to dismiss review and supported by statement, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 2418.


PRIOR HISTORY: San Francisco County Super. Ct. No. 982894. Honorable William Cahill.



DISPOSITION: Writ issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, unions and taxpayer, sought a writ of mandate regarding the order of respondent San Francisco County Superior Court (California), challenging the right of department director, real party in interest, to proceed with four wage surveys arguably designed to implement a new weighted-average methodology in determining a prevailing wage rate and seeking to enjoin real party in interest from spending appropriated funds on surveys.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, unions and taxpayer, sought writ relief from a writ of mandate challenging the right of department director, real party in interest, to proceed with four wage surveys arguably designed to implement a new weighted-average methodology (methodology) in determining a prevailing wage rate and seeking to enjoin respondent from spending more appropriated funds on the surveys in violation of Cal. Gov't Code § 13332.15. Respondent superior court denied injunctive relief and discovery. The court of appeal issued a peremptory writ directing respondent to order real party in interest from spending appropriated funds to implement the prevailing wage rate methodology, and permitting wage survey discovery. After discovery, respondent was to consider on the merits petitioners' claim that the surveys were being conducted in order to implement the methodology. The Budget Act deletion, by the legislature of a proposed line item appropriation, constituted a "formal action" to deny funding for the purpose of implementing the methodology, within the meaning of § 13332.15, which prohibited a use of an appropriation to achieve any purpose that was denied by legislative formal action.


OUTCOME: The court of appeal issued a peremptory writ, favoring petitioners, unions and taxpayer, directing respondent superior court to order department director, real party in interest, from spending appropriated funds to implement the prevailing wage rate weighted-average methodology and permitting wage survey discovery.

 

585 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Kilroy v. Superior Court


No. B107509.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


54 Cal. App. 4th 793; 63 Cal. Rptr. 2d 390; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 327; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3113; 97 Daily Journal DAR 5421



April 28, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BD244176, James D. Endman, Temporary Judge. *


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, § 21.



DISPOSITION: Writ Granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father requested a writ of prohibition to quash an order by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), requiring petitioner to show cause for a modification of a Georgia child support decree. Petitioner contended that pursuant to The Full Faith and Credit for Child Support Orders Act, 28 U.S.C.S. § 1738B, California did not have jurisdiction to modify the Georgia decree.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner father requested a writ of prohibition to require respondent trial court to quash and dismiss a show cause order for modification of a Georgia child support decree. Petitioner was a resident of California but plaintiff mother and child were residents of Georgia. Petitioner and plaintiff had entered a consent child support order in Georgia for support of petitioner's minor child. Plaintiff had filed for a modification of support in California after the child developed medical problems that required substantial additional support. The court granted the writ of prohibition requiring the trial court to dismiss the action because California courts did not have jurisdiction. The court held that pursuant to the Full Faith and Credit for Child Support Orders Act, 28 U.S.C.S. § 1738B(a), Georgia had continuing exclusive jurisdiction over support of the child because plaintiff and the child still resided in Georgia, and petitioner had not consented to transferring the action to California. The court concluded that the supremacy clause, U.S. Const. art. VI, required that deference be given to Georgia, and that there was no violation of the U.S. Const. amend X.


OUTCOME: The court issued the writ of prohibition requested by petitioner father and ordered respondent trial court to quash and dismiss the show cause order for a modification of petitioner's child support obligation. California courts did not have jurisdiction to modify the Georgia child support decree because plaintiff mother and child were still residents of Georgia and the action should properly be taken in Georgia.

 

586 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Pala Band of Mission Indians v. Bd. of Supervisors


No. D024621.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


54 Cal. App. 4th 565; 63 Cal. Rptr. 2d 148; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 314; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2970; 97 Daily Journal DAR 5199



April 23, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. 1 


1 Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of Discussion parts III., IV., V., VI., VII., VIII. and X.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied July 9, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 4357.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County, No. N66667. Lisa Guy-Schall, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the judgment, except that we conclude Section 8A is void and must be stricken from the initiative. Each party to bear its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of an order of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) denying its petition for a writ of mandate against respondent County of San Diego and real party in interest corporation. Appellant asked the trial court to declare a voter initiative invalid because it violated the California Constitution and state law. The initiative designated land adjacent to appellant's as a solid waste facility.


OVERVIEW: San Diego County voters approved an initiative amending the county general plan to designate an area for use as a privately owned solid waste facility. Appellant owned land adjacent to the designated area and brought suit against respondent San Diego County alleging that the initiative violated the state constitution. In affirming the trial judge, the court ruled that the initiative was constitutional because it proposed a direct amendment to the general plan, was consistent with other portions of the plan, did not eliminate essential county functions, and adequately informed voters of the initiative provisions. The court found, however, that the portion of the initiative that defined respondent corporation as the "applicant" and provided it with powers, duties, and functions relating to the application process and to the operation of the facility violated Cal. Const. art. II., § 12 which prohibited an initiative from naming a private corporation to perform any function or have any powers or duties. The court ruled that because the unconstitutional section was volitionally, functionally, and grammatically severable, the remainder of the initiative was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in refusing to invalidate the voter initiative that designated land adjacent appellant property owner's for a solid waste facility. The court also concluded that the section of the initiative that granted powers, duties, and functions to respondent corporation was void. Because that section was severable, however, the rest of the initiative remained valid.

 

587 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Hewlett v. Squaw Valley Ski Corp.


No. C020539.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


54 Cal. App. 4th 499; 63 Cal. Rptr. 2d 118; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 310; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2939; 97 Daily Journal DAR 5145



April 22, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Placer County, No. 86683, James D. Garbolino, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Plaintiffs' cross-appeal is dismissed as moot. Plaintiffs shall recover their costs on appeal. Plaintiffs Hewitt and Sierra Club are awarded their reasonable attorney fees on appeal in an amount to be determined by the trial court. (See Serrano v. Unruh (1981) 32 Cal. 3d 621, 637-638 [186 Cal. Rptr. 754, 652 P.2d 985].)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant ski resort appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Placer County (California) that imposed fines, ordered an injunction, and awarded attorney fees pursuant to defendant's removal of trees in violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17200, Cal. Pub. Res. Code § 4511 et seq., a conditional use permit, and a temporary restraining order.


OVERVIEW: Defendant ski resort cut down numerous trees. Plaintiffs, the district attorney and two interested parties, filed suit alleging unfair business practices under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17200. The trial court held that defendant violated Cal. Pub. Res. Code § 4511 et seq., a conditional use permit, and a temporary restraining order. The trial court imposed fines, ordered injunctive relief, and awarded attorney fees. Defendant appealed, contending there were no ongoing unlawful business practices and no violations of § 4511 or the restraining order. Defendant asserted that unlawful business practices could not be based upon violations of a conditional use permit or restraining order and challenged the remedies and fees. The court affirmed because the multiple violations constituted ongoing unlawful business practices and the trees were cut for commercial purposes. In addition, violations of a conditional use permit or restraining order could be the basis for a claim of unlawful business practices and the fines imposed were not excessive. The injunctive relief and award of attorney fees were appropriate; therefore, their imposition did not constitute an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court because the violations constituted ongoing unlawful business practices and the trees were cut for commercial purposes. Additionally, the fines were not excessive and the injunctive relief and award of attorney fees did not constitute an abuse of discretion. Lastly, claims of unlawful business practices could be based upon violations of a conditional use permit or temporary restraining order.

Sue E. v. Superior Court


No. B108455.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


54 Cal. App. 4th 399; 62 Cal. Rptr. 2d 726; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 308; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2913; 97 Daily Journal DAR 5091



April 21, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. CK13286. John Paventi, Temporary Judge. *


* Pursuant to California Constitution, art. VI, § 21.



DISPOSITION: Because substantial evidence supports the juvenile court's determination to hold the hearing described in section 366.26, the petitions are denied on the merits.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner parents challenged an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which ordered a hearing under Cal. Welf. Inst. Code § 366.26 that had the potential to terminate petitioners' parental relationship with their child.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner parents filed separate writs of mandate that challenged a juvenile court's order setting a hearing under Cal. Welf. Inst. Code § 366.26 regarding a permanent plan for their child that might have terminated the parental relationship. The court denied those petitions, finding that substantial evidence supported the juvenile court's determination to hold the contested hearing. The court also concluded that petitioners failed to take advantage of the sufficient reunification efforts they were offered. The court additionally cited petitioners' past neglect of the child's siblings, their current inadequate living environment, and their lack of motivation to correct the behavior that led to the child's dependency as further evidence of their inability to care for her. The court further determined that failing to file a petition for extraordinary writ review pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26(1) would only have precluded subsequent appellate review of matters in the juvenile court's order to set a hearing under § 366.26 and would not have affected appellate rights as to matters that may have arisen after the hearing was set.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner parents' writs of mandate as to a juvenile court's order that set a hearing that might have ended their parental relationship with their child. The court cited petitioners' not taking advantage of reunification efforts and other evidence in support of a hearing, and held that extraordinary writs were unnecessary to preserve appellate rights as to matters that may have arisen after the hearing was set.
